PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 25 of 200
Question ID: 613068
Working as a project manager for a drug manufacturing project, you are performing a schedule
network analysis to generate the project schedule model. You have already determined the
critical path and float, optimized resources, and calculated a 90% probability of completing the
project by May 28.
What else is left to do?
- **A Using a Monte Carlo simulation to calculate possible outcomes of the project schedule**
- **B Adjusting the start and finish dates to balance the demand for resources with their**
availability
- **C Assessing the need to aggregate schedule reserves to reduce the possibility of schedule**
slippage
- **D Applying precedence diagramming to arrange the activities according to their logical**
order
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You can eliminate any techniques that would be used to produce what the scenario describes as
having been done.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Schedule network analysis is an umbrella term for several tools and techniques used to develop a
project schedule. It includes the critical path method, resource optimization (including resource
leveling and resource smoothing), schedule modeling (including what-if scenario analysis and
simulation such as the Monte Carlo simulation). In the scenario described, all three of these

---

techniques have been completed. Additional analysis includes assessing the need to aggregate
schedule reserves to reduce the possibility for schedule slip, making this the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Using a Monte Carlo simulation to calculate possible outcomes of the project schedule**
Incorrect. In the scenario described, you have already calculated a 90% probability of
completing the project by a specific date. Since such a calculation is an output of the Monte
Carlo simulation, it can be implied that this data analysis technique has already been
completed.
- **B Adjusting the start and finish dates to balance the demand for resources with their**
availability
Incorrect. Balancing the demand for resources with their availability by adjusting activity
start and finish dates is resource leveling, which is a technique for resource optimization.
The scenario indicates that resources have already been optimized.
- **C Assessing the need to aggregate schedule reserves to reduce the possibility of schedule**
slippage
Correct. Aggregating schedule reserves to reduce the risk of schedule delays is an
analytical task in schedule network analysis. One form of this analysis is the critical chain
method, which can only be done on a resource-optimized schedule. Using the critical path
diagram as a basis, you must identify divergences and convergences at risk of delaying
multiple activities. You can collect or aggregate the available float for multiple tasks on a
path, accelerating their start and finish dates to create a buffer before at-risk path
convergences. You only use the schedule reserves if necessary.
- **D Applying precedence diagramming to arrange the activities according to their logical**
order
Incorrect. The precedence diagramming method is a tool used in the Sequence Activities
process. By this point in the project described, the critical path and float have already been
calculated. Both the critical path and the float are determined using the critical path
method, which uses the precedence diagram as a basis. Therefore, the precedence diagram
has already been completed.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 194, 209-214; see also The Practice Standard
for Scheduling – Second Edition, Project Management Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 12
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 26 of 200
Question ID: 612548
- **A project team has just completed estimates for both the activity durations and the activity**
resources for the project you are managing. Tomorrow morning, you need to present a
preliminary schedule to the key stakeholders.
What is your best course of action?
- **A Pre-assign the resources required for the project**
- **B Apply resource optimization techniques**
- **C Present the project schedule network diagram**
- **D Develop the schedule management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Think about what processes have been completed at this point in the project, and what needs to
be developed next, with which inputs and outputs.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Having completed duration and resource estimates in the scenario presented, you have completed
the Estimate Activity Durations process. The next logical step is to begin the Develop Schedule
process. However, performing this process may be time-consuming, while according to the
scenario, you have to present the preliminary project schedule tomorrow. The precedence
diagramming method (PDM) is a technique used during the Sequence Activities process to
construct a schedule model in which activities are represented by nodes and are graphically
linked by one or more logical relationships to show the sequence in which the activities are to be
performed. A project schedule network diagram is an output of the Sequence Activities process,

---

which is typically carried out before the Estimate Activity Durations process, and therefore,
should have been completed prior to the activities described in the scenario. While not ideal, the
project schedule network diagram produced earlier during the Sequence Activities process along
with the activity estimates produced during the time described in the scenario can be used as a
preliminary schedule.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Pre-assign the resources required for the project**
Incorrect. Pre-assignment is a tool used in the Acquire Resources process. While some
resources may be pre-assigned as part of the Develop Project Charter process,
pre-assignment would not help you complete a preliminary schedule. Furthermore, you may
not be even able to acquire the resources until after you have baselined your project
schedule and budget.
- **B Apply resource optimization techniques**
Incorrect. Resource optimization is a tool of the Develop Schedule process, but it needs a
preliminary schedule to be developed first based on the estimates that have been completed
in this scenario.
- **C Present the project schedule network diagram**
Correct. A project schedule network diagram is a graphical representation of the logical
relationships among the project schedule activities. A project schedule network diagram is
an output of the Sequence Activities process, which is, as implied by the question, has
already been completed. Under the constraints of the situation provided, presenting the
project schedule network diagram along with the activity estimates produced during the
time described in the scenario is likely to be your best course of action.
- **D Develop the schedule management plan**
Incorrect. The schedule management plan is the main output of the Plan Schedule
Management process. According to the scenario, the team has already completed estimates
for both the activity durations and the activity resources. These tasks are typically
accomplished after the development of the schedule management plan is completed,
implying the plan has already been developed.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 194
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 27 of 200
Question ID: 651425
Decisions were made to move a major portion of the work and to add some additional work to an
outsourcing firm in another country where labor costs are cheaper.
Which components of the project management plan are likely to be updated as a result of the
approved change?
- **A Benefits management plan and project charter**
- **B Requirements documentation and requirements traceability matrix**
- **C Scope baseline, cost baseline, and schedule baseline**
- **D Risk register, stakeholder register, and lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which ones are project plans and which are project documents?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the Control Scope process is underway. There are a variety of project
management plan updates that are an output of this process. In this scenario, the scope was
changed to include more work as well as to specify who was to perform that work. As such,
various components of the project management plans may be updated. These components
include but are not limited to the scope management plan (to specify the work added), the
resources management plan (to describe who is doing the work and other resources needed), the
schedule management plan (to indicate when work is being done), the communications
management plan (to mention the flow of information is going to change), the procurement
management plan (to guide how the work will be sourced and managed), the quality

---

management plan (to define how the standards are to be assured and controlled), the risk
management plan (to outline the new risks involved), and the stakeholder engagement plan (to
indicate there are more stakeholders in the project). All of those plans could be the answer. In
this case, the options presented did not include a collection of those plans, but the other essential
components of the project management plan: the baselines of scope, cost, and schedule. The
other answer choices include project documents, which could be updated as a result of the
approved change but are not components of the project management plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Benefits management plan and project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is a high-level document explaining the objectives of the
project, not the plans for sourcing the work. Benefits management plan is a documented
explanation defining the processes for creating, maximizing, and sustaining the benefits
provided by a project. None of those artifacts is a component of the project management
plan, nor either one of them is updated as a result of the Control Scope process suggested
by the question.
- **B Requirements documentation and requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. While the requirements documentation and requirements traceability matrix may
be updated as a result of the Control Scope process described in the scenario, these are
project documents, not components of the project management plan.
- **C Scope baseline, cost baseline, and schedule baseline**
Correct. The scope baseline, cost baseline, schedule baseline, and performance
measurement baseline could be updated based on the approved change. These baselines are
among the components of the project management plan.
- **D Risk register, stakeholder register, and lessons learned register**
Incorrect. Although updates to the lessons learned register is an output of the Control
Scope process implied by the scenario, the risk register, stakeholder register, and lessons
learned register are all project documents, not components of the project management plan.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 171

Question 28 of 200
Question ID: 613758
As part of project planning, you and your project team are developing a comprehensive list of
individual project risks and sources of overall project risk. You want to analyze the validity of
assumptions and constraints to determine which pose a risk to the project.
Which technique will be the most helpful for you?
- **A Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis**
- **B Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis**
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
- **D Data analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique explores the validity of assumptions and constraints as part of the Identify Risks
process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project team is performing the Identify Risks process. Assumption
and constraint analysis is one of the data analysis techniques used during the Identify Risks
process. Assumption and constraint analysis explores the validity of assumptions and constraints
to determine which pose a risk to the project. This is the data analysis technique being used by
the project team.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis**
Incorrect. Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing individual project
risks for further analysis or action by assessing their probability of occurrence and impact
as well as other characteristics. The question implies the project team is performing the
Identify Risks process. Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is a process and not a data
analysis technique associated with the Identify Risks process.
- **B Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis**
Incorrect. Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis is the process of numerically analyzing the
combined effect of identified individual project risks and other sources of uncertainty on
overall project objectives. The question implies you are carrying out the Identify Risks
process. Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis is a process and not a data analysis technique
associated with the Identify Risks process.
- **C Cost-benefit analysis**
Incorrect. A cost-benefit analysis is a financial analysis tool used to determine the benefits
provided by a project against its costs. This is a data analysis technique associated with
many of the project management processes. However, it is not a technique used for the
Identify Risks process.
- **D Data analysis**
Correct. The question implies the Identify Risks process is underway. While data analysis is
not a specific technique used in this process, data analysis represents a set of different tools
and techniques used to identify risks on a project. Assumption and constraint analysis is
one of those techniques. This technique explores the validity of assumptions and constraints
to determine which pose a risk to the project, making this choice the best answer to the
question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 415

Question 29 of 200
Question ID: 651421
Near the end of an iteration, the project team is ready to lead a product review with the product
manager.
What is the objective of the review?
- **A Validate the product scope**
- **B Manage product quality**
- **C Control the product scope**
- **D Close the project or phase**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is being reviewed?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Validate Scope is the process of formalizing acceptance of the completed project deliverables.
This process can be carried out at the end of an iteration (sprint), phase, project, or any other
point where the product work can be reviewed and inspected. Inspections are among the tools
and techniques of the Validate Scope process. In the Validate Scope process, stakeholders are
determining whether or not the scope completed is acceptable. In a project utilizing agile
practices, there is a product review at some point or points in the iteration. Since most of the
iteration is to get to a workable version for review, that often is at or near the end of the iteration.
Whenever such a review happens, it is a tool and technique to examine and validate the project
work and product deliverables.

---

Inspections are sometimes called reviews, product reviews, and walkthroughs.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Validate the product scope**
Correct. The purpose of the product reviews is to examine the product to see if meets
requirements and can be accepted. This is the Validate Scope process.
- **B Manage product quality**
Incorrect. Managing product quality is part of the Manage Quality process. This process is
concerned with translating the quality management plan into executable quality activities.
According to the scenario, the team is going to lead a product review with the product
manager rather than translate the quality management plan into executable quality
activities.
- **C Control the product scope**
Incorrect. Control Scope is the process of monitoring the status of the project and product
scope and managing changes to the scope baseline. There is nothing in the scenario to
suggest the team is involved in the Control Scope process. The product review described in
the scenario may lead to changes. However, the main purpose of the product review is to
validate, rather than control, the product scope.
- **D Close the project or phase**
Incorrect. Close project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities for the project,
phase, or contract. The question suggests the team is going to review the product with the
product manager rather than finalize all activities for the project, phase, or contract.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166

Question 30 of 200
Question ID: 612515
All work planned to produce the deliverables of your project is now complete, and you begin to
finalize activities for the project.
What should you do next?
- **A Release the project team**
- **B Close contracts with vendors**
- **C Hand over the final product**
- **D Update the project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In the closing process of the project, what is it called when the final product is exchanged from
the seller to the buyer?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Finalizing activities for the project in which all work required to produce deliverables has been
complete implies the project enters its final stage, closure. As part of the Close Project or Phase
process, the final product, service, or result is handed over to a different group or organization
that will operate, maintain, and support it. The final product, service, or result transition is an
output of the Close Project or Phase process. This output refers to the transition from one
team/group/department/organization to another. Transferring the ownership of deliverables to the
assigned stakeholders in accordance with the project plan is performed to facilitate project
closure.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Release the project team**
Incorrect. The question implies the project has entered its last stage - closure. Work
completed does not necessarily mean all activities are completed. There are many activities
associated with project closure that may require the project team. Releasing the team is a
premature action.
- **B Close contracts with vendors**
Incorrect. Contracts are closed as part of the Control Procurements process. During
project closure implied by the scenario, the project manager and team confirm the formal
acceptance of the vendor's work. Regardless, there is not enough information in the
question to determine if there are any contracts on the project.
- **C Hand over the final product**
Correct. As part of the Close Project or Phase process implied by the scenario, the final
product, service, or result is handed over to a different group or organization that will
operate, maintain, and support it.
- **D Update the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is a document that formally authorizes the project and the
project manager. It is rare when a project charter is updated, especially at the end of the
project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123, 127

Question 31 of 200
Question ID: 651374
The project has to produce 10,000 new parts. The inspection points and their frequency along
production must be determined. The part specifications and inspection modes to be used also
need to be decided.
In which process are these project plans defined?
- **A Plan Resource Management**
- **B Create WBS**
- **C Manage Stakeholder Engagement**
- **D Plan Quality Management**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which process plans the standards and how they are assured?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Every project must determine the quality standards for that project and how to assure those
standards. The Plan Quality Management process identifies quality requirements and standards
for the project and its deliverables. The plan also documents how the project will demonstrate
compliance with these quality requirements and standards. In the scenario described, the
implementation of these activities is accomplished by identifying the specifications of the parts
and the inspection methodology to be used to check the specifications. As those are being
determined, the resources, stakeholders, costs, schedule activities, and many other project areas
are being updated and referenced.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Plan Resource Management**
Incorrect. Resources are going to be needed to conduct the inspections planned, but the
Plan Resource Management process does not directly determine what inspections are
needed and which specifications are being inspected. Rather, the Plan Resource
Management process defines how to estimate, acquire, manage, and utilize physical and
team resources.
- **B Create WBS**
Incorrect. The Create WBS process breaks down the project scope into more manageable
segments. The process does not establish the quality specifications being measured and the
inspection methodology to be used to assure the quality standards.
- **C Manage Stakeholder Engagement**
Incorrect. The Manage Stakeholder Engagement process is influenced by the work of the
quality plans, but the process does not directly determine the specifications and the
inspection methodology. Rather, the process is concerned with communicating and working
with stakeholders to meet their needs and expectations.
- **D Plan Quality Management**
Correct. The Plan Quality Management process defines the quality standards the project is
to meet and how to go about ensuring those established quality standards are met.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 277-278

Question 32 of 200
Question ID: 651381
Your company was awarded a software development project. You have just drafted the scope
management plan and submitted it to the sponsor for her initial review. The sponsor reviews the
plan and states that the client specified the use of Scrum, while according to the plan, the scope
will be delivered using waterfall project management practices.
Which component of the project management plan should you correct?
- **A Project life cycle description**
- **B Development approach**
- **C Requirements management plan**
- **D The contract with the client**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which input for the Plan Scope Management process specifies the development framework for
the project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scope management plan is created as an output of the Plan Scope Management process. The
question indicates that the project requirements specified by the client included the use of Scrum
as a development methodology, while the scope management plan reflects a waterfall
framework. The components of the project management plan that may serve as inputs into the
Plan Scope Management process typically include the quality management plan, project life
cycle description, and development approach. The development approach defines whether
waterfall, iterative, adaptive, agile, or a hybrid development approach will be used on the project.

---

Scrum is an example of an agile methodology. Therefore, according to the scenario, it is
reasonable to assume that the development approach indicated in the project management plan
mistakenly called for waterfall instead of Scrum. Hence, the development approach is the
component of the project management plan that should be corrected.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project life cycle description**
Incorrect. The project life cycle determines the series of phases that a project passes
through from its inception to the end of the project. Whereas, the question is asking about
the development approach (Scrum versus waterfall) rather than the use of phases.
- **B Development approach**
Correct. The development approach is considered an element of the project management
plan. The development approach defines whether waterfall, iterative, adaptive, agile, or a
hybrid development approach will be used on the project. Scrum is an example of an agile
methodology.
- **C Requirements management plan**
Incorrect. The question suggests that you are carrying out the Plan Scope Management
process. The two outputs of this process include the scope management plan and the
requirements management plan. Thus, the requirements management plan cannot serve as
an input into the process in which it is created.
- **D The contract with the client**
Incorrect. The contract with the client should contain any requirements for a particular
development approach for the project. However, the question is asking about a component
of the project management plan. The contract with the client is not a component of that
plan.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 135,137

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 33 of 200
Question ID: 613767
During project risk planning, the project manager and the team are trying to decide whether to
invest $10 million to develop new software or to instead invest $5 million to upgrade the existing
software. The team is uncertain how strong will demand be for their product and, therefore, must
account for this uncertainty in their analysis.
What would be the best tool for the project manager to use in this case?
- **A Tornado diagram**
- **B Monte Carlo analysis**
- **C Influence diagram**
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which technique is designed to present different project decisions under consideration and the
implications that may arise from choosing one path or another?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the project manager is carrying out the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis
process. Decision tree analysis is an example of a data analysis technique that can be used as part
of that process. The project manager is trying to decide between two different courses of action,
which a decision tree analysis is most suited for. A decision tree can be used to quantify the
different options in monetary terms and support decision-making in the face of uncertainty,
which, in this case, is market demand.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Tornado diagram**
Incorrect. A tornado diagram is used to analyze the influence of a whole range of potential
risks, whereas a decision tree is used to support the selection of the best of several courses
of action.
- **B Monte Carlo analysis**
Incorrect. A Monte Carlo analysis is not used to decide between the best of several courses
of action. Instead, it is a computational method used to analyze the combined effects of
individual project risks.
- **C Influence diagram**
Incorrect. An influence diagram is a graphical aid to establish relationships between
project entities, outcomes, and influences. A computational simulation technique, such as
Monte-Carlo analysis, is then performed to indicate the risk elements with the greatest
influence. However, in this scenario, the project manager is more concerned with
quantifying two possible courses of action in monetary terms - a need that is best met using
a decision tree analysis.
- **D Decision tree analysis**
Correct. A decision tree is used to support the selection of the best of an established set of
possible courses of action. It quantifies the different options in monetary terms and
supports decision-making in the face of uncertainty (the uncertainty, in this case, being
market demand).

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 433-436
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 34 of 200
Question ID: 612846
- **A project is underway to construct a 50 story office building. With construction nearly complete,**
a government inspector has issued a stop order because one of the cranes failed inspection. The
schedule reserves are inadequate to cover the resulting delay from the unavailability of the key
resource.
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Update the resource management plan**
- **B Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline**
- **C Submit a change request to update the cost baseline**
- **D Terminate the project since the project objectives cannot be met**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project will not be completed when originally planned.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to
the project are available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of
resources and performing corrective action as necessary. In this case, a key resource will not be
available as originally planned, and the schedule reserves are inadequate to cover the resulting
delay. As a result of the Control Resources process, the schedule baseline may be updated to
reflect the actual versus planned availability of assigned resources. With inadequate schedule
reserves, the schedule baseline must be revised in order for the project to continue. Therefore, of

---

the available options, submitting a change request to update the schedule baseline is the best
response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Update the resource management plan**
Incorrect. The resource management plan should be updated in this scenario. However, the
resource management plan, as a component of the project management plan, requires an
approved change request to modify. If other answer choices did not have a change request
as part of their wording, this answer choice could have been a plausible option.
- **B Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline**
Correct. In this case, a key resource will not be available as originally planned, and the
schedule reserves are inadequate to cover the resulting delay. Therefore, the schedule
baseline must be updated in order for the project to continue, and an approved change
request is required to modify any of the project's baselines.
- **C Submit a change request to update the cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline may or may not need to be updated in this situation. However,
the question does not provide any information on the project's cost performance or the
impact of the work stoppage on the project budget. While the cost baseline 'might' need to
be updated in this scenario, the schedule baseline 'should' be updated if the project is to
continue.
- **D Terminate the project since the project objectives cannot be met**
Incorrect. The work stoppage may cause the project to be terminated. However, with
construction nearly complete, termination of the project seems unlikely. Regardless,
terminating the project at this point is a premature action. The project manager should seek
approval to revise the schedule baseline (along with any other required changes to
configuration elements) before terminating the project. Additionally, a project manager
lacks the authority to terminate the project and would first need to seek approval from the
appropriate authority.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 358

Question 35 of 200
Question ID: 613679
- **A project manager is preparing for a status meeting by examining the project's cost performance**
to date. She produces a chart which depicts the performance of EV, PV, and AC over the past
year. The chart reveals that even though costs are over budget, cost performance has been
improving over the past four consecutive months.
What tool or technique has the project manager used?
- **A Trend analysis**
- **B Reserve analysis**
- **C Variance analysis**
- **D Root cause analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique is used to determine if performance is improving or deteriorating over
time?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Trend analysis is one of the tools and techniques that may be used during the Control Costs
process, which is the process described by the question. Trend analysis examines project
performance over time to determine if performance is improving or deteriorating. Charts can be
particularly helpful in visualizing trends derived from earned value analysis. Therefore, of the
choices provided, it is reasonable to assume that in the scenario described, the project manager
has performed a trend analysis.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Trend analysis**
Correct. Trend analysis examines project performance over time to determine if
performance is improving or deteriorating. Charts can be particularly helpful in visualizing
trends derived from earned value analysis.
- **B Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is an analytical technique used to establish a reserve for the
schedule duration, budget, estimated cost, or funds for a project. Based on the description
provided by the question, the project manager is not determining a reserve.
- **C Variance analysis**
Incorrect. Variance analysis is a technique for determining the cause and degree of
difference between the baseline and actual performance. Variance analysis by itself does
not provide information on performance over time. Thus, of the available options, variance
analysis is not the best choice.
- **D Root cause analysis**
Incorrect. Root cause analysis is an analytical technique used to determine the basic
underlying reason that causes a variance or a defect or a risk. The project manager is
depicting cost performance over time rather than the causes of the variance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 36 of 200
Question ID: 613766
- **A project manager has just completed a Monte Carlo analysis simulation when he learns from a**
team member that some of the cost estimates used in the simulation were incorrect. The project
manager is highly risk-averse and concerned about this issue, so he meets with his team to
discuss options on how to move forward.
What would the team likely do with the results from this Monte Carlo analysis?
- **A Use the results; the simulation data can still be of value because incorrect estimates are**
accounted for in the algorithm
- **B Reject the results and use the triangular distribution technique instead**
- **C Use the results but set aside additional contingency reserves to address the project risks**
- **D Reject the results; the Monte Carlo results would be inaccurate and should not be used**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

If the project estimates are too broad, or too narrow, a Monte Carlo analysis may misstate the
overall risk.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Accurate cost estimates are the most important part of a Monte Carlo analysis. If the project
estimates are too broad, or too narrow, the analysis may misstate the overall risk. In turn, this
could create serious problems for project planning. Since inaccuracies in the cost estimates can
significantly change the results, it is best for the project team to reject the Monte Carlo analysis
results and re-run the simulation once they have better estimates.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use the results; the simulation data can still be of value because incorrect estimates are**
accounted for in the algorithm
Incorrect. Accurate cost estimates are the most important part of a Monte Carlo analysis.
The validity and the usefulness of the analysis are only as good as the project team's ability
to estimate their costs.
- **B Reject the results and use the triangular distribution technique instead**
Incorrect. Although it is best for the project team to reject the results of the Monte Carlo
analysis, there is not enough information given to know whether applying a triangular
distribution technique makes sense for this particular project instead of a Monte Carlo
analysis. Moreover, since we know from the question that it is a large construction project,
led by a highly risk-averse project manager, the relatively simplistic triangular distribution
technique may not be appropriate for this particular project.
- **C Use the results but set aside additional contingency reserves to address the project risks**
Incorrect. This approach could introduce additional risk to the project. The results of a
Monte Carlo analysis can help determine the amount needed for a contingency reserve, but
if the recommended contingency reserve is based on inaccurate data, then the amount of
reserve will likely be inaccurate as well. Simply setting aside additional contingency
reserves to cover any potential shortfall is risky and not the best approach here.
- **D Reject the results; the Monte Carlo results would be inaccurate and should not be used**
Correct. Since inaccuracies in the cost estimates can significantly change the results, it is
best for the project team to reject the Monte Carlo analysis results and re-run the
simulation once they have better estimates.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 433-434

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 37 of 200
Question ID: 651424
Senior management has changed direction on the products and features to roll out this quarter.
Your agile project is impacted.
What is your best next action as the project manager?
- **A Add the new features requested by senior management to the product backlog**
- **B Evaluate the delta between the current product backlog and the new features**
- **C Await directives from senior management as to what features exactly should be added**
- **D Complete the development of the current backlog as fast as possible to avoid changes**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is going to change?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

When senior management, project sponsors, and others directing business strategy alter the
business strategy, the projects within their domain may be affected. The number of projects
affected and the degree of impact is going to vary. Hence, before any changes to the project and
the product backlog are made, the project manager and project team must assess the differences
between the current project plans and completed product increments to the proposed new plans.
Controlling the scope may take on different forms depending on the project management
approach (predictive, agile, hybrid) as well as evaluations and discussions amongst all
stakeholders. It may be determined that the changes are so grand that it is better to cancel the
current project and start a new one. So before any work is added to the current project,

---

assessment of the business strategy and what the current project has done and can do is the first
action to take.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Add the new features requested by senior management to the product backlog**
Incorrect. Adding the new features to the product backlog without first evaluating their
impact on all project constraints is a premature action. On agile projects, specifically, the
product backlog is managed by the product owner. You, as a project manager, are not
supposed to add new items to the product backlog at will without, at least, talking to the
product owner.
- **B Evaluate the delta between the current product backlog and the new features**
Correct. Evaluation of the requested changes compared to the work already planned and
completed provides a project manager an opportunity to assess the degree to which the
current product backlog will have to be changed. Technically, this evaluation will have to
be done by the product owner and the project team. You, as a project manager, will have to
facilitate this activity.
- **C Await directives from senior management as to what features exactly should be added**
Incorrect. The project manager does not need to sit on their hands awaiting direction and
instructions from senior management. Proactively engaging in conversation with senior
management can serve better the project manager and team for changes and future plans.
- **D Complete the development of the current backlog as fast as possible to avoid changes**
Incorrect. Purposefully completing the development of the current backlog as fast as
possible just to avoid changes is an unethical course of action and will waste project
resources.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 167-168

Question 38 of 200
Question ID: 613060
Your project team members are writing software code together as a pair and reviewing each
other's work to determine if the code conforms to the requirements documentation.
Which of the following will be a result of these reviews?
- **A Accepted deliverable**
- **B Acceptance criteria**
- **C Work performance data**
- **D Verified deliverable**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Peer reviews are considered part of the inspection tool and technique.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Writing software code together as a pair and reviewing each other's work is known as pair
programming. This practice is often used on agile projects. As far as traditional project
management is concerned, the scenario suggests the team is in the Control Quality process and is
using the tool of inspection, such as peer reviews, to determine if the software conforms to
documented standards. The goal of the Control Quality process and the inspection is to verify the
correctness of deliverables thereby producing the output of verified deliverables. The verified
deliverables then become an input to the Validate Scope process to determine if the deliverables
meet the acceptance criteria for formal acceptance by the customer or sponsor. Formal
acceptance of the verified deliverables produces an output from the Validate Scope process

---

called accepted deliverables. Since the team is conducting a code review to determine the
correctness of the software, the result of their efforts will be a verified deliverable.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Accepted deliverable**
Incorrect. Accepted deliverables are products produced by a project and validated by the
project customer or sponsors as meeting their specified acceptance criteria. Accepted
deliverables are an output of the Validate Scope process. In this scenario, the team is
checking the deliverables for correctness which is done during the Control Quality process
and results in a verified, not accepted, deliverable.
- **B Acceptance criteria**
Incorrect. Acceptance criteria is a set of conditions that are required to be met before
deliverables are accepted by the customer or sponsor. The acceptance criteria are
determined during the Define Scope process and are part of the project scope statement.
The Control Quality process described in the scenario does not produce acceptance
criteria.
- **C Work performance data**
Incorrect. Work performance data is the raw observations and measurements identified as
part of the activities performed during project execution. In the scenario described, the
team is carrying out code review sessions suggesting the processes of the Monitoring and
Controlling Process Group are being performed rather than the processes of the Executing
Process Group.
- **D Verified deliverable**
Correct. Verified deliverables are completed project deliverables that have been checked
and confirmed for correctness through the Control Quality process. In the scenario, the
team is using the tool of inspection to determine if the software conforms to the
requirements documentation which will ultimately result in a verified deliverable.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 305

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 39 of 200
Question ID: 651378
Managing the project team for an agile based project, the project manager takes a servant role
and allows the team to be self-organizing.
Why is this possible?
- **A The team relies on the project manager's leadership and assignments.**
- **B The team is comprised of subject matter experts that have specific roles and skills.**
- **C The team is comprised of generalists and able to support each other fluidly.**
- **D The team is larger than one project manager can put in one meeting room.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Agile project teams are made up of cross-functional members who have both a focused specialty
plus a breadth of experience across multiple skills.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Directing and managing a project team in an agile environment often enables the project
manager to take a servant role and the project team to take more ownership and decision making
roles. Ideally, agile teams are comprised of generalized specialists, meaning the team members
are cross-functional who have both a focused specialty plus a breadth of experience across
multiple skills, instead of subject matter experts as often acceptable in traditionally managed
projects. As such, the project team can move as necessary between the tasks and form
self-organizing units freely and fluidly as the project demands. The project manager takes a more
supportive role and works to remove roadblocks and empower the team.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The team relies on the project manager's leadership and assignments.**
Incorrect. In agile projects where the team members are highly capable and
knowledgeable, the role of the project manager does not require them to direct and instruct
the team members. The team members are empowered to make their own choices and
direction without a need to rely on the project manager's leadership and assignments.
- **B The team is comprised of subject matter experts that have specific roles and skills.**
Incorrect. Teams comprised of specialists can primarily only perform the tasks they are
trained for. As such, this does not enable them to freely move between tasks and be
self-organizing.
- **C The team is comprised of generalists and able to support each other fluidly.**
Correct. Self-organizing teams are successful when the team members have broad skills
and understanding of the project activities enabling them to effectively move between tasks
and project needs.
- **D The team is larger than one project manager can put in one meeting room.**
Incorrect. The size of agile teams is typically small - around 6 to 10 members in most
circumstances. Nevertheless, the size of the room does not dictate or mandate the teams to
be self-organizing or not. The team's ability to be self-organizing is not based on physical
limitations.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 310-311

Question 40 of 200
Question ID: 651377
Services are still being billed to the project even though the project manager believes no
additional services are required or requested.
What is the best course of action for the project manager to take?
- **A Confirm that no more services are needed and the procurement agreements are closed**
- **B Close all agreements with all service providers engaged with the project**
- **C Forward the service bills to the project management office for further review and approval**
- **D Continue paying the bills until the project is formally closed to avoid claims**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How certain can the project manager be?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Disputes and miscommunications between buyers and sellers can happen. Some unintentional or
by mistake. The additional bills from the service provider to the project may be planned or in
error. Until the project manager confirms the situation and that no further billing to the project
should occur, the appropriate actions are still not fully known. In this scenario, it could be part of
the procurement agreement that the bills are spread out over the course of the project and not
only at the point of delivery. Or it could be that the automatic billing activity was to stop once the
final services were delivered. Gathering information and understanding the root of the problem is
the best option for the project manager to take in this situation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Confirm that no more services are needed and the procurement agreements are closed**
Correct. Before taking action on questionable procurement documents, the project manager
ensures that no services are required or being requested by the project. Confirming the
state of the procurement agreements enables the project manager to make the appropriate
response.
- **B Close all agreements with all service providers engaged with the project**
Incorrect. There may be multiple open agreements with several service providers. Closing
all the agreements may close procurement arrangements that are still active and required
by the project to meet its objectives.
- **C Forward the service bills to the project management office for further review and approval**
Incorrect. The purpose of the project management office (PMO) is not to handle payments
and contract disputes with suppliers. The PMO can provide direction and resources, but
handing off the responsibility to the PMO is not the best option in most organizations.
- **D Continue paying the bills until the project is formally closed to avoid claims**
Incorrect. Until the project manager confirms that the payments are to continue, the
payments should not be paid blindly until the project is closed. Procurements can be closed
while the project still goes on. If agreements between the parties specify so, then the
payment should continue after confirmation of those terms. Otherwise, the payments should
stop provided the project manager confirmed that no more services are needed, and the
procurement agreements are closed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 492-494, 496, 499

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 41 of 200
Question ID: 613217
On your construction project, you are eight weeks away from achieving a milestone for which
your client will award you a $10,000 bonus. However, the workers union of your supplier has
announced a strike. If your supplier cannot settle the dispute within three weeks, the supply
interruption could delay your project. There is a 20% chance the strike exceeds three weeks, and
you predict the delay will cost $50,000.
What is the expected monetary value (EMV) of this risk?
Top of Form
- **A -$2,000**
- **B $18,000**
- **C $50,000**
- **D $250,000**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Take the opportunity value as a positive impact and the threat value as a negative impact for the
EMV calculation. Don't forget to account for the probability of both.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The expected monetary value (EMV) is often used in decision tree analysis as part of the
Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process. EMV is calculated by multiplying the impact of

---

each possible outcome by its probability of occurrence and adding the products together.
Opportunities or potential gains are taken as positive values, while threats or potential losses are
taken as negative values. In this scenario, you need to find both the threat and the opportunity for
the risk described:
● There is a 20% chance that you will lose $50,000.
● There is an 80% chance that you will achieve the milestone that allows you to claim a $10,000
bonus.
Using the EMV formula:
EMV = (-$50,000 x 20%) + ($10,000 x 80%) = -$10,000 + $8,000 = -$2,000.
Some users wonder as to where did the number 80% come from. Here is why: the scenario indicates that
there is a 20% chance the strike exceeds three weeks. This implies that there is an 80% chance (100% -
20% = 80%) that the strike does not exceed three weeks. Therefore, there is a 20% chance of a $50,000
loss and an 80% chance of getting the $10,000 bonus.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A -$2,000**
Correct. Using the EMV formula: EMV = (-$50,000 x 20%) + ($10,000 x 80%) = -$10,000
+ $8,000 = -$2,000
- **B $18,000**
Incorrect. You might have gotten this value if you neglected to account for $50,000 being a
threat of loss, which means it is a negative number.
- **C $50,000**
Incorrect. The potential impact of the negative risk is $50,000. However, to calculate EMV
properly, you must account for the 20% probability of the strike lasting more than three
weeks. You must also account for the impact and probability of the opportunity to gain a
bonus for achieving your milestone.
- **D $250,000**
Incorrect. You might have gotten this answer by multiplying the 5 affected weeks by the
potential impact of $50,000. However, the scenario did not actually indicate that the impact
was weekly.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 435
Bottom of Form

Question 42 of 200
Question ID: 612446
- **A project manager is about to start planning a software development project. The project sponsor**
would like to review any project risks that have been identified at this point.
Which document should the project manager recommend the sponsor to review?
Top of Form
- **A Project charter**
- **B Issue log**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Risk report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which document is available at this point in the project and might contain high-level project
risks?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Ideally, to learn about all identified risks on the project, the project sponsor would have to review
the risk register. However, the question states that the project manager is about to start project
planning, implying that the risk register, which is created during the Identify Risks process, is not
yet available. At this point in the project, only the project charter can serve the needs of the

---

project sponsor as it contains a list of high-level risks that were identified at the time the project
charter was drafted and approved.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project charter**
Correct. The project charter contains any high-level risks that have been identified at the
time the charter was drafted and approved.
- **B Issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document that is created during the Direct and Manage
Project Work process. Not only does the issue log not yet exist at this point in the project,
but also, the issue log contains issues that have occurred rather than risks.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a project document that is created as an output of the Identify
Risks process and captures the details of identified individual project risks. However, the
question states that the project manager is about to start project planning, implying that the
risk register is not yet available.
- **D Risk report**
Incorrect. The risk report presents information on sources of overall project risk, together
with summary information on identified individual project risks. The risk report is created
during project planning as an output of the Identify Risks process which, according to the
scenario described, has not yet started.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81, 417

Question 43 of 200
Question ID: 612698
You have completed a nine-month project, and you are in the closing stage. The project
completed on time and under budget and everyone in your department has congratulated you on
your achievement. The vice president of your company heard about the success of your project
and wants a summary overview of project performance so that he can talk about your success at
the next board meeting.
What should you provide to him?
Top of Form
- **A Lessons learned repository**
- **B Project closure documents**
- **C Final lessons learned register**
- **D Final report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You are looking for a summary overview of project results.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests the project has been closed. In other words, the Close Project or Phase
process is now complete. The final report is one of the outputs of this process. The final report
includes information such as a summary level description of the project, a summary of any risks

---

and issues encountered and how they were addressed, a summary of how the final product,
service or result was achieved, and more. Since the vice president wants a summary overview of
project results, providing the vice president with the final report will likely meet their needs and
is, therefore, of the choices provided, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. The lessons learned repository is a store of historical information about lessons
learned from projects. Even though the lessons learned repository includes the final lessons
learned and knowledge gained throughout the project, the vice president wants a summary
of project performance, not lessons learned. The summary of project performance is
typically found in the final report and not the lessons learned repository. Therefore, this
choice is not the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Project closure documents**
Incorrect. The project closure documents consist of formal documentation on completion of
the project and the information on project deliverables transferred to the ongoing
organization. The project closure documents do not contain a summary of project
performance, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **C Final lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The final lessons learned register is finalized during project closure, before being
entered in the lesson learned repository. Even though the final lessons learned register
includes the final lessons learned and knowledge gained throughout the project, the vice
president wants a summary of project performance which is found in the final report and
not the final lessons learned register.
- **D Final report**
Correct. The final report provides a summary of the project performance. The report
includes information such as a summary level description of the project, a summary of any
risks and issues encountered and how they were addressed, a summary of how the final
product, service or result was achieved, etc. Therefore, providing the final report to the vice
president would address her needs, making this choice the best answer to the question
asked.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 44 of 200
Question ID: 651405
Two project team members are having a disagreement over how to approach a minor technical
detail. The project manager has little experience working with them, and her technical
knowledge is limited.
What is the best action for the project manager to take?
Top of Form
- **A Abide by the decision of the most senior team member**
- **B Avoid being involved in the discussion and decision making**
- **C Stop the discussion and direct the team members to get back to work**
- **D Request the human resource department's representative to step in**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How much help is the project manager in this debate?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

As the project team is working on the project, there are going to be situations where an answer
must be worked out. Sometimes these situations are complex, requiring a lot of debate and
discussion; other times these are very simple decisions. These minor conflicts are commonplace
in almost every project. A project environment that supports the decision making and trust
among team members, so they can resolve issues and find beneficial solutions are hallmarks of

---

high-performing teams. A project manager must assist in creating and developing such an
environment and the team. That sometimes means backing away from situations where the
project manager is not a value-add and allowing the project team to problem solve and decide.
While this option sounds counter-intuitive, under the circumstances described in the scenario,
withdrawing from the conflict and not making the decision is the best course of action for the
project manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Abide by the decision of the most senior team member**
Incorrect. Although experience or tenure at a company may provide one with more
knowledge and leverage a certain advantage, require the team members to go with the
decision of the most senior person is most likely not the best way to resolve a technical
issue. Sometimes, junior team members have innovative ideas that are better than the old
tested approaches.
- **B Avoid being involved in the discussion and decision making**
Correct. The project manager does not have the information and insight to help the team
members come to a resolution. The inclusion of the project manager is not of benefit.
- **C Stop the discussion and direct the team members to get back to work**
Incorrect. The scenario suggests the team members are arguing over technical detail.
Stopping the discussion would not resolve the issue.
- **D Request the human resource department's representative to step in**
Incorrect. There is nothing in the scenario to suggest the issue is personal warranting the
representative of the human resource department to step in.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 341, 349
Bottom of Form

Question 45 of 200
Question ID: 613464
You are managing a project to design equipment to load shredded recycled tires into railroad cars
for transport. While testing the equipment, you notice a lot of shredded tires are on the ground
around where the railroad car was loaded. You are not sure if any spillage is allowable.
Where would you find this information?
Top of Form
- **A Quality control plan**
- **B Project management plan**
- **C Quality report**
- **D Quality policy**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The necessary document is a component of a larger document.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario, you want to carry out the Control Quality process. The project
management plan is an input to this process. The quality management plan is a component of the
project management plan that describes how quality policies, procedures, and guidelines will be
implemented to achieve quality objectives. The plan outlines the quality objectives, activities,
and resources necessary to meet the objectives as well as the quality standards that will be used

---

in the project. Information such as whether or not spillage is allowed by the equipment when
transferring the shredded tire to the railroad car would be included in the quality management
plan. Ideally, the quality management plan would be a better answer than the project
management plan, however, this option is not provided. Since the quality management plan is a
component of the project management plan, of the choices available, the latter is the best answer
to the question asked.
Note, specific levels of spillage would likely be described in the quality metrics document, not
the quality management plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality control plan**
Incorrect. The 'quality control plan' is a made-up term.
- **B Project management plan**
Correct. The quality management plan, a component of the project management plan,
defines how quality control will be performed within a project as well as acceptable
thresholds of deviation. The plan may include general guidance on whether spillage is
allowed.
- **C Quality report**
Incorrect. The quality report is an output of the Manage Quality process. The quality report
contains information detailing how well the quality for the project is being managed and
recommendations for changes to processes to obtain better quality. In the scenario, you are
looking for a quality standard for the acceptable spillage. This information is not part of
the quality report.
- **D Quality policy**
Incorrect. The quality policy expresses the fundamental principles that will govern an
organization's actions as they implement quality management. The quality policy typically
includes systems that will be followed corporately to guarantee quality rather than
addressing specific projects.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 300, 286

Question 46 of 200
Question ID: 613680
You are a project manager assigned to a bridge construction project. Senior management has
expressed their concerns regarding cost overruns in labor and materials which may jeopardize
the successful completion of the project. You are asked to research the cause and impact of the
cost overruns and determine if corrective actions are needed.
What tool or technique is most helpful in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Earned value analysis**
- **B Trend analysis**
- **C Reserve analysis**
- **D Variance analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What analysis technique is useful in providing insight into the cause of a gap in cost
performance?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

It can be inferred from the question that the Control Costs process is being performed, and one of
the techniques that may be useful during this process is variance analysis. When variance
analysis is used during the Control Costs process, it can be helpful in determining the cause and

---

degree of variance relative to the cost baseline and deciding whether a corrective or preventive
action is required. Of the available answer choices, only variance analysis provides insight into
the cause(s) of a cost variance and whether corrective action is needed.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Earned value analysis**
Incorrect. Earned value analysis can be used to compare the performance measurement
baseline to actual schedule and cost performance. However, earned value analysis is not
helpful in determining the cause of a variance.
- **B Trend analysis**
Incorrect. Trend analysis is an analytical technique that uses mathematical models to
forecast future outcomes based on historical results. Trend analysis may be helpful in the
situation described by the question, but it will not provide information related to the cause
of a cost variance or decisions on corrective action.
- **C Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. During cost control, reserve analysis is used to monitor the status of contingency
and management reserves for the project. Reserve analysis may be necessary for the
scenario described by the question, but it does not provide insights into causes or
corrective actions.
- **D Variance analysis**
Correct. Variance analysis is used during the Control Costs process to determine the cause
and degree of variance relative to the cost baseline and deciding whether a corrective or
preventive action is required.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 262

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 47 of 200
Question ID: 613134
While looking at the project cost baseline graph shown below, a project manager sees that the
last point of the stair-step line is higher than the estimate at completion (EAC).
What does this relationship mean for the project?
Top of Form
- **A The project is running over budget**
- **B The management reserve is too large**

---

- **C Total funding for the project exceeds the project's anticipated needs**
- **D The project is behind schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the difference between budget, funding, and the cost baseline?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project cost baseline graph displays a time-phased view of the cost baseline along with
funding requirements and expenditures. The stair-stepped line on the graph represents the
funding requirements, which includes the cost baseline and the management reserve. The project
budget is represented by the last point of the stair-step line. The question states that EAC
(estimate at completion) is less than the project budget (the top stair step). Therefore, in this
scenario, total funding for the project exceeds the project's anticipated needs.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project is running over budget**
Incorrect. The stair-step line is the funding limit reconciliation line, and the highest point is
the last amount of money released to the project. This amount includes management reserve
and represents the entire project budget. Since the project budget is higher on the chart
than the EAC, the project is running under, not over budget.
- **B The management reserve is too large**
Incorrect. The management reserve is established to address unknown project risks. The
management reserve is only one component of the overall project budget. In this scenario,
all that can be surmised is that the project budget, represented by the last point of the
stair-step line, exceeds the EAC. There is no information presented by the question to
suggest that the management reserve is excessive.
- **C Total funding for the project exceeds the project's anticipated needs**
Correct. The stair-stepped line on the graph represents the project's funding requirements.
The project budget is represented by the last point of the stair-step line. Therefore, the
estimate at completion is less than the project budget, meaning total funding for the project
exceeds the project's anticipated needs.

---

- **D The project is behind schedule**
Incorrect. The project cost baseline graph displays a time-phased view of the cost baseline
along with funding requirements and expenditures. Thus, the graph provides cost and not
schedule information. Therefore, it is not possible to determine whether or not the project is
behind schedule from the information provided by the question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 254-256

Question 48 of 200
Question ID: 613250
- **A project has just been canceled due to the customer going bankrupt and unable to finance the**
remainder of the project. About half of the deliverables are complete, and the other half are in
various stages of development.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Recall all of the deliverables in the customer's possession**
- **B Hold all deliverables that are about to be shipped to the customer**
- **C Review the contract and prepare the project closure documents**
- **D Turn over all deliverables to the customer whether or not they are complete**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What determines the ownership of deliverables when a project is terminated?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario infers the project should enter the Close Project or Phase process since it has been
terminated by the customer. Contracts (agreements) are an input to this process. The contract
terms and conditions outline the rights and obligations of each party. The procurement contract
should contain a termination clause that determines ownership of deliverables which are
completed or in progress. Before taking any action, the project manager should first understand

---

the legal obligations in the event the project is terminated. This action will likely involve others
including the legal department to ensure any action taken is in alignment with the contractual
agreement. Once the relevant terms and conditions are clearly understood, the project closure
documents are then prepared with the reasons why the project was terminated and the formalized
procedures for the transfer of the finished and unfinished deliverables of the canceled project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Recall all of the deliverables in the customer's possession**
Incorrect. It is unlikely that deliverables already in the customer’s possession would be
recalled, especially if the customer has already paid for them. However, even if this is the
case, the contract should first be reviewed to determine the course of action in this
situation.
- **B Hold all deliverables that are about to be shipped to the customer**
Incorrect. Holding the deliverables may or may not be the appropriate action. The actual
ownership of the deliverables, complete or in progress, should be outlined in the
termination clause of the contract.
- **C Review the contract and prepare the project closure documents**
Correct. The termination clause of the contract should outline ownership of deliverables
(complete and in progress) when a project is terminated prematurely. The project closure
documents are then created with the reasons why the project was terminated and the
procedures for the transfer of the finished and unfinished deliverables of the canceled
project.
- **D Turn over all deliverables to the customer whether or not they are complete**
Incorrect. The need to turn over all deliverables to the customer under these circumstances
is determined by the terms and conditions of the contract. Turning over all deliverables to
the customer whether or not they are complete without checking the contract may violate
the contract and result in damage to the customer and/or performing organization.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 125, 128, 489

Question 49 of 200
Question ID: 651363
- **A project team notices that over the last four work performance reports, the overall costs**
allocated to a work package are rising steadily, exceeding the funds allocated for this work
package.
What should the project team do next?
Top of Form
- **A Calculate the TCPI to determine if the work package is still expected to be completed within**
budget
- **B Submit a change request to adjust the necessary components of the project management plan**
- **C Run additional reports from the ensuing time period to determine if the trend continues**
- **D Conduct a trend analysis and root cause analysis to determine the reason(s)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the reason for the pattern? Is it known?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Trend analysis and root cause analysis are among the data analysis techniques that can be used as
part of the Monitor and Control Project Work process described in the scenario. Trend analysis is
used to forecast future performance based on past results. Root cause analysis seeks to determine
the underlying reason or reasons. In this scenario, it appears that there is a trend based on the

---

project team's review of the performance reports. How much of a trend and to what extent those
past results reflect the potential future of the project's costs is what needs to be explored via the
trend analyses. If any pattern or patterns are identified, then getting to the potential root cause
assists the project team in resolving the issue before it comes worse or unmanageable.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Calculate the TCPI to determine if the work package is still expected to be completed**
within budget
Incorrect. The to-complete performance index (TCPI) does not provide information the
project team is seeking in the scenario. The TCPI would inform the team the rate at which
they must perform to meet certain targets not whether the work package can be completed
within budget.
- **B Submit a change request to adjust the necessary components of the project management**
plan
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine whether or not a
change request is required at this point. First, an analysis should be conducted to identify
the reason(s) behind the questionable performance. Then, based on the results of the
analysis, actions can be taken which may or may not include submitting a change request.
- **C Run additional reports from the ensuing time period to determine if the trend continues**
Incorrect. Four weeks of reports are hinting that there may be a trend. If no trend or root
cause is uncovered or suspected after an initial trend analysis, then conducting another one
in the future is a worthwhile action. In the meantime, conducting a trend analysis now is a
better option, even if only to collect data.
- **D Conduct a trend analysis and root cause analysis to determine the reason(s)**
Correct. According to the work performance reports, there may be a trend. How much of a
trend or simply a coincidence needs to be examined via a deeper analysis of the trends.
Additionally, if any trends are uncovered, an analysis as to the root cause(s) would allow
the team to react to the information.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 111
Bottom of Form
