PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 74 of 200
Question ID: 612808
Your boss is giving you a rough outline of the scope, constraints, and risks involved in a
prospective client's project. The project is highly similar to the project you are currently closing.
The sponsor wants to know how long this project would take your team to complete.
You think your team may need two months, but what should your answer be?
Top of Form
- **A "Let me run some numbers in a simulation, and get back to you tomorrow."**
- **B "Give us two months. We will knock it out just like the project that we are closing now."**
- **C "If it truly resembles this project we are closing, it could be six to ten weeks."**
- **D "Considering the uncertainty in scope, I estimate three months."**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember, you are aspiring to be a Project Management Professional, with the experience to
make realistic estimates, and the confidence to stand by them.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Considering your immediate experience of a similar project, you should give an estimate in the
form of a range. As a component of a schedule management plan, the level of accuracy specifies
the acceptable range used in determining realistic duration estimates. The range accounts for risk
contingencies. These contingencies may be some threats of delay or opportunities to gain

---

efficiencies and accelerate the schedule. A project in the initiation phase (which is the case in this
scenario) might have a rough order of magnitude estimate in the +/-50% range. If you would
estimate 8 weeks is most likely, a rough range of 4 to 12 weeks is reasonable. But that range is
not among your answer choices. Later, as more information becomes available, estimates could
narrow to a range of +/-10%. In the scenario provided, you have a team that is experienced in
this kind of project, making the narrower range of six to ten weeks the best of the available
choices.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A "Let me run some numbers in a simulation, and get back to you tomorrow."**
Incorrect. The prospective client's project has a rough outline of scope, constraints, and
risks. However, you have no numbers to run through a simulation (e.g., Monte Carlo),
making this choice a weak response.
- **B "Give us two months. We will knock it out just like the project that we are closing now."**
Incorrect. You want to avoid the tendency to fixate on a single number. If you say 2 months,
your boss will remember exactly 2 months and hold you accountable for it.
- **C "If it truly resembles this project we are closing, it could be six to ten weeks."**
Correct. When we try to forecast the future, there is always a degree of uncertainty. You
want to give yourself room for schedule flexibility. The inner and outer limits veer away
from fixating on a single number from your initial two-month estimate.
- **D "Considering the uncertainty in scope, I estimate three months."**
Incorrect. Without a real basis to add more than 50% to the length of the project, this
response smacks of padding your estimate. The best way to account for uncertainty in a
forecast is to use a range, plus or minus a reasonable variance from your most likely
estimate, depending on your degree of confidence.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 182, 203-204; see also the PMI Practice
Standard for Project Estimating.

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 75 of 200
Question ID: 651325
During the evaluation of the project's financial statements at the end of a project phase, concerns
about some of the charges were raised. The project manager explains that the costs were justified
both early in the project and as the project progressed.
Which of the following is the best input for the project manager to provide for reconciliation?
Top of Form
- **A Quality reports**
- **B Assumption log**
- **C Project charter**
- **D Basis of estimates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Note that the costs have justification.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the project is in the Close Project or Phase process. As an input to this
process, the basis of estimates is used to compare the actual results with the planned results and
other cost assumptions. The cost estimates along with their rationale provide justification for the
expected costs. Monitoring and controlling those estimates as the project progresses adds more
justification and credibility, most notably during closure.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality reports**
Incorrect. Quality reports list the quality management issues detected by the team during
the course of the project and areas for improvement. The quality report does not provide
cost justifications.
- **B Assumption log**
Incorrect. The project's assumption log documents the assumptions and constraints that
guided the project team throughout the project. Assumptions on their own do not equate to
cost justifications.
- **C Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter may provide a ballpark figure on the estimated costs, but is
not going to provide explanations for the costs and their validation as the project
progresses.
- **D Basis of estimates**
Correct. The basis of estimates, as it pertains to the Close Project or Phase process
described in the scenario, is used to evaluate how the estimates of duration, cost, resources,
and cost control compared to actual results.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 124
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 76 of 200
Question ID: 651366
The project team is in need of additional resources to complete project work. They want to
procure the items while keeping costs under control.
Which of the following should they reference to make their decisions?
Top of Form
- **A Cause-and-effect diagrams**
- **B Basis of estimates**
- **C Project funding requirements**
- **D Actual cost**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Does the project have the budget to purchase more items at the time the team need them?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario refers to the Control Costs process. Project funding requirements is an input to this
process. There are a lot of costs to control in a project, especially when acquiring more resources
from outside the project organization. When controlling the costs and the procurements of a
project, the project team must reference the budget and the project funding requirements. The
project funds are typically allocated or released at the start of the project. Although, the project
funding may be allocated per a schedule over the project lifecycle. Knowledge of how the project

---

funding is distributing and other constraints on those funds allows the project team to acquire the
resources through procurement as needed while at the same time controlling the costs. In this
scenario, the funding to procure additional resources may or may not be available at the current
time. Requesting funds at the incorrect times may risk the resources being denied. Proper
planning with the needed information increases the team's possibility for success.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cause-and-effect diagrams**
Incorrect. Cause-and-effect diagrams are typically used in the processes of the Project
Quality Management Knowledge Area to determine the root cause of a problem. The
scenario refers to the Control Costs process, where the application of cause-and-effect
diagrams is very unlikely.
- **B Basis of estimates**
Incorrect. The basis of estimates is the supporting documentation outlining the details used
in establishing project estimates such assumptions, constraints, level of detail, ranges, and
confidence levels. The basis of estimates does not include information that would help the
team to determine how to procure more resource for the project while keeping the costs
under control.
- **C Project funding requirements**
Correct. The project funding requirements provide the project team with the details on
projected expenditures and other funding information. That information will assist the
project team in controlling the costs while procuring the resources.
- **D Actual cost**
Incorrect. Actual cost (AC) is the realized cost incurred for the work performed on an
activity during a specific time period. AC alone would not help the team understand how
much of the budget they may consume to procure the additional resources without
exceeding the funds allocated for the project for the period of time they plan to procure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 260

Question 77 of 200
Question ID: 613681
- **A project manager determines that actual costs to date are $5M and then estimates that**
approximately $4M will still need to be spent to complete the project for a total anticipated
expenditure of $9M. However, the budget for the project is only $8.5M, which is a projected
variance of -$0.5M. The anticipated expenditure of $9 MM is documented and reported to
stakeholders according to the communications management plan.
What has been reported to the stakeholders?
Top of Form
- **A Estimate to complete**
- **B Cost baseline**
- **C Activity duration estimates**
- **D Cost forecasts**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

An estimate at completion (EAC) is an example of what?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

It can be inferred from the question that the Control Costs process is being performed. Cost
forecasts are an output of the Control Costs process. The scenario implies an estimate at
completion (EAC) of $9M, which is the actual costs to date plus the estimated costs to complete.

---

The EAC is an example of a cost forecast, which is what has been documented and
communicated to stakeholders.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Estimate to complete**
Incorrect. The estimate to complete (ETC) is the expected cost to finish all the remaining
project work, which is represented by the $4M rather than the $9M being asked about in
the question.
- **B Cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline is the approved version of the time-phased project budget,
excluding any management reserves. The project budget is stated by the question at $8.5M,
and the question is asking about the $9M estimate at completion.
- **C Activity duration estimates**
Incorrect. Activity duration estimates are the quantitative assessments of the likely number
of time periods that are required to complete an activity. The question is asking about a cost
estimate, which is unrelated to activity duration.
- **D Cost forecasts**
Correct. The question indicates an estimate at completion (EAC) of $9M, which is the
actual costs to date plus the estimated costs to complete. The EAC is an example of a cost
forecast, which is documented and communicated to stakeholders.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 269

Question 78 of 200
Question ID: 613140
During the construction of a hotel, the project has experienced an unforeseen difficulty with the
generators being used to supply the required electricity for the project. The output of the
generators is inadequate, and the project manager will need to either rearrange the scheduled
activities to reduce peak demand or acquire more generators to keep the project on track.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Implement a corrective action**
- **B Revise the issue log**
- **C Rearrange the scheduled activities**
- **D Acquire more generators**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document is used to record information about problems encountered during the
project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to
the project are available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of
resources and performing any corrective action as necessary. The issue log represents one of the

---

project documents that may be updated as part of this process. The issue log is a project
document where information about issues is recorded and monitored. The problem with the
generators not being able to supply the necessary electricity should be recorded in the issue log
where it can be tracked to resolution. Therefore, of the available options, revising the issue log is
what the project manager should do first.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Implement a corrective action**
Incorrect. A corrective action is an intentional activity that realigns the performance of the
project work with the project management plan. A corrective action will likely need to be
taken to keep the project on track in this case. However, the project manager must first
decide 'what' action of the alternatives available is the best for the project.
- **B Revise the issue log**
Correct. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. The problem with the generators not being able to supply the necessary
electricity should be captured in the issue log where it can be tracked to resolution.
- **C Rearrange the scheduled activities**
Incorrect. Rearranging the scheduled activities is one of the alternatives provided in the
scenario. However, before taking any specific action, the problem should be documented in
the issue log, an owner assigned, alternatives discussed, and the best alternative selected.
- **D Acquire more generators**
Incorrect. Acquiring more generators is one of the alternatives provided in the scenario.
However, before taking any specific action, the problem should be documented in the issue
log, an owner assigned, alternatives discussed, and the best alternative selected. If the
option of acquiring more generators is selected, a change request should be submitted and
analyzed against all project constraints.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 358

Question 79 of 200
Question ID: 651417
- **A project manager has been called into an urgent meeting with senior management that starts in**
an hour, which is the same time that the project manager is supposed to attend a brainstorming
session being held by the project team to determine the best technical approach for the
development of the features for the next iteration.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Reschedule the brainstorming meeting so the project manager can facilitate the session**
- **B Attend the first half of the management meeting and then ask to leave to join the team**
- **C Attend the senior management meeting, then get an update from the team later**
- **D Postpone the senior management meeting until after the brainstorming meeting**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Can any meeting be held without the project manager present?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Meetings make up a large part of how projects manage communications. Meetings happen in
many ways and formats. Not all project meetings require the project manager to lead, facilitate,
or control. More so, some project meetings may not even require the presence of the project
manager, such as the meeting described in the scenario where a technical approach will be

---

discussed. A project manager must do what they can to ensure the proper flow and exchange of
communications occurs. They are not required to personally deliver all communications or
micromanage the techniques used for project communications. In this scenario, the project team
is likely capable of handling the brainstorming session they have planned to hold. A project
manager's best action is to communicate with the project team before and after the concurrent
meetings.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reschedule the brainstorming meeting so the project manager can facilitate the session**
Incorrect. A project manager does not need to control and facilitate every meeting.
Meetings for iterations are repeated more than once over the project life cycle granting
enough experience to the project team to handle the discussions.
- **B Attend the first half of the management meeting and then ask to leave to join the team**
Incorrect. It is unlikely that the project manager will be able to leave in the middle of the
meeting with senior management easily. Even if she does, the benefit of attending half of
each one of the meetings is unclear. Leaving meetings in the middle is not a good practice
and may harm the reputation of the project manager. This course of action does not look
like the best approach.
- **C Attend the senior management meeting, then get an update from the team later**
Correct. The project team is capable of conducting their own brainstorming session. A
project manager's time is better spent on the senior management meeting. Communication
between the project manager and team can happen before and after the meetings.
- **D Postpone the senior management meeting until after the brainstorming meeting**
Incorrect. The project manager most likely does not have the authority to postpone or
reschedule senior-level meetings.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 386

Question 80 of 200
Question ID: 613089
As part of project initiation, a project manager is identifying stakeholders for her project and
records this information in the stakeholder register.
Which of the following activities is the project manager least likely to perform as part of this
activity?
Top of Form
- **A Assess any available project documentation and lessons learned from past projects**
- **B Perform stakeholder analysis to develop a list of stakeholders with relevant information**
- **C Submit a change request to update the stakeholder engagement plan**
- **D Categorize the stakeholders' stakes including interest, rights, ownership, and contribution**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project is still in the initiation stage, and project planning has yet to begin.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question describes a project in the initiation, which implies that the first iteration of the
Identify Stakeholders process is being performed. The stakeholder register may be 'updated'
during subsequent iterations but is 'created' during the first iteration. During the first iteration of
stakeholders' identification, there will not be any change requests. As stakeholder identification
continues throughout the project, new stakeholders, or new information about stakeholders, may

---

result in a change request to the product, project management plan, or project documents.
However, change requests are not necessary until the project has been baselined after project
planning is complete. Note, the question is asking for the activity that the project manager is
'least' likely to perform in this scenario. The incorrect answer choices all represent data analysis
techniques that may be used during the first iteration of the Identify Stakeholders process.
Therefore, of the available choices, submitting a change request to update the stakeholder
engagement plan is the best response to the question.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Assess any available project documentation and lessons learned from past projects**
Incorrect. This answer choice describes document analysis, which is one of the data
analysis techniques associated with the Identify Stakeholders process. Document analysis
can be used during the creation of the stakeholder register and involves assessing the
available project documentation and lessons learned from previous projects to identify
stakeholders and other supporting information.
- **B Perform stakeholder analysis to develop a list of stakeholders with relevant information**
Incorrect. Stakeholder analysis is a data analysis technique which is useful for the creation
of the stakeholder register. Stakeholder analysis results in a list of stakeholders and
relevant information such as their positions in the organization, roles on the project,
"stakes," expectations, attitudes, and their interest in information about the project.
- **C Submit a change request to update the stakeholder engagement plan**
Correct. The question states that the stakeholder register is being created, which implies
that the first iteration of the Identify Stakeholders process is being performed. During the
first iteration of identifying stakeholders, there will not be any change requests.
Additionally, the stakeholder engagement plan does not exist until later in the project as an
output of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process.
- **D Categorize the stakeholders' stakes including interest, rights, ownership, and contribution**
Incorrect. Categorizing the stakeholders' stakes is part of the stakeholder analysis which is
a data analysis technique used in the Identify Stakeholder process. Stakeholders' stakes can
include interest, rights, ownership, knowledge, and contribution. This information can be
used during the creation of the stakeholder register.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 512, 514

Question 81 of 200
Question ID: 651408
The project manager is in discussions with vendors about their bids that came in higher than
expected. Additionally, according to the vendors' responses, none of them will be able to deliver
by the deadline requested. The project manager talks to the sponsor and other key project
stakeholders to see if additional funds are needed to cover the extra costs and deliver on
schedule.
Which process is the project manager performing?
Top of Form
- **A Control Costs**
- **B Control Schedule**
- **C Acquire Resources**
- **D Conduct Procurements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents getting work done from outside the project organization?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Conduct Procurements process is the process of obtaining seller responses, responding to
those proposals and questions that may come from the vendors, selecting a vendor, and hopefully
finalizing an agreement between all involved parties. To reach such agreements, plans are

---

executed and adjusted as needed. The planned procurement documentation, such as requests for
proposals, is used to solicit responses from potential sellers. In this scenario, as those responses
came in and were analyzed, external negotiations with the vendors as well as internal
negotiations with the sponsor and other key project stakeholders were necessary to determine the
best course of action. Negotiation is an example of the interpersonal and team skills that can be
used as part of the Conduct Procurements process. Of the choices available, Conduct
Procurements was likely the process being performed by the project manager in the scenario
described.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control Costs**
Incorrect. Control Costs is the process of monitoring the status of the project to update the
project costs and manage changes to the cost baseline. While the question suggests that the
project manager monitors costs as she is anticipating cost increase, the focus of the
question is on reviewing vendors responses and negotiating externally and internally. These
actions fall under the Conduct Procurements process. The contracts have not yet been
awarded. Therefore, it is unclear if any changes to the cost baseline will be even required.
Maybe a contingency reserve would be sufficient.
- **B Control Schedule**
Incorrect. Control Schedule is the process of monitoring the status of the project to update
the project schedule and manage changes to the schedule baseline. The question suggests
the project manager is concerned with the fact the vendors will be unable to deliver on
schedule implying the Control Schedule process is relevant to the scenario. However, the
focus of the question is on reviewing vendors responses and negotiating externally and
internally, which belongs to the Conduct Procurements process. The contracts have not yet
been awarded. Therefore, it is unclear if any changes to the schedule baseline will be
eventually required.
- **C Acquire Resources**
Incorrect. Acquire Resources is the process of obtaining team members, facilities,
equipment, materials, supplies, and other resources necessary to complete project work.
Resources are not being acquired in this scenario. What is being sought is work from
outside the project organization, which is part of procurement management.
- **D Conduct Procurements**

---

Correct. The activities of obtaining seller proposals, negotiating internally and externally
to reach agreements, and analyzing potential agreements are all examples of activities
performed as part of the Conduct Procurements process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 488

Question 82 of 200
Question ID: 651407
Midway into project execution, a competitor is about to release a product similar to the one
planned to be delivered by your project. If the competitor launches their product to the market
before you, your project will be deemed as failed.
With a response prepared to run some of the development activities in parallel, what should you
do next?
Top of Form
- **A Compress the schedule**
- **B Meet with the team to assess the risk**
- **C Terminate the project**
- **D Request management reserves**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is there a risk response plan?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When identified project risks are realized, project managers and their team implement the
planned risk responses. The question reads, 'with a response prepared', implying the risk of the
competitor releasing a similar product has been identified, and the response has been planned.
The risk response was to run some of the development activities in parallel which is the essence

---

of fast tracking. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique in which activities or phases
that are normally done in sequence are performed in parallel for at least a portion of their
duration. By compressing the schedule, the project will likely be completed earlier than planned
and hopefully ahead of their competitor. Therefore, of the available choices, implementing the
planned risk response, i.e. compressing the schedule, is what you should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Compress the schedule**
Correct. The risk response plan was to speed up the schedule. Now that the risk has been
realized, the response should be implemented. Fast tracking is a method to speed up the
schedule.
- **B Meet with the team to assess the risk**
Incorrect. The scenario implies the risk has already been identified and assessed, and the
response has been planned. The team now needs to implement the plan.
- **C Terminate the project**
Incorrect. Terminating the project is a premature action. According to the scenario, the
competitor has not yet released the product. The competitor is 'about to release' it. First, a
response planned to address the risk should be implemented. If the response does not result
in the desired effect, other actions, including project termination may be considered.
- **D Request management reserves**
Incorrect. Management reserves are allocated for unknown risks. According to the
scenario, the risk of the competitor releasing a similar product has been identified, and the
response has been planned.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 449-451, 215

PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 83 of 200
Question ID: 612705
As your project progresses and creates product increments with each consecutive iteration, the
project team carries out the Collect Requirements process and Identify Risks process to collect
new requirements and identify new risks. You want to ensure that work planned for the
upcoming iterations is completed with the consideration of the new risks and requirements.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Reprioritize work in a risk-adjusted backlog**
- **B Hold an iteration retrospective meeting**
- **C Update the requirements-risk repository**
- **D Distribute a risk report after each iteration**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Wouldn't it be nice if there were one place to keep all the features, requirements, and risk
responses for a project, and sort it so that each upcoming iteration provides the most value to the
customer?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a hybrid project where the product is developed incrementally using an
agile framework over the course of several iterations, while the requirements and risks are

---

collected and identified using the Collect Requirements process and Identify Risks process which
are associated with the predictive project management approach. Products developed
incrementally in an adaptive approach by cross-functional project teams are frequently reviewed
to accelerate knowledge sharing and ensure that risks are understood and managed. Risks are
identified, analyzed, managed, and considered when selecting the content of each iteration.
Additionally, the requirements are kept as a living document that is regularly updated. Work may
be reprioritized as the project progresses, based on an improved understanding of current risk
exposure. Agile teams strive to balance delivering the highest-value features and mitigating the
biggest risks. They achieve this by moving the items with the greatest value and risk to the top of
the backlog so that the backlog becomes risk-adjusted. Therefore, to ensure that upcoming
iterations reflect the new risks and requirements, the team should reprioritize work in a
risk-adjusted backlog.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reprioritize work in a risk-adjusted backlog**
Correct. One of the key agile considerations for project risk management is to keep the
requirements as a living document that is regularly updated. In agile terms, this list of
requirements is called the project or product backlog. Based on an improved understanding
of current risk exposure, work may be reprioritized as the project progresses. After such
sorting takes place, the document becomes a risk-adjusted backlog.
- **B Hold an iteration retrospective meeting**
Incorrect. A regular retrospective meeting is an agile practice for inspecting the team's
performance and collaborating on ways to minimize risk. However, a retrospective is held
at the end of an iteration to reflect on team performance and adapt the process used by the
team to develop the product, not to plan the next iterations.
- **C Update the requirements-risk repository**
Incorrect. The 'requirements-risk repository' is a made-up term.
- **D Distribute a risk report after each iteration**
Incorrect. A risk report is a project document that provides information on sources of
overall project risk, together with summary information on identified individual project
risks. Distributing the risk report after each iteration is unlikely to ensure that work
planned for the upcoming iterations is completed with the consideration of the new risks
and requirements as requested in the scenario.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 400, 131, 177, 671
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 84 of 200
Question ID: 625062
You are managing a project to produce 50,000 concrete blocks for a construction site. The
quality management plan allows for examination of 10% of the blocks and requires them to be
free from any defects. You select 100 of the first 1,000 blocks produced, and you find that some
of them have minor cracks. The customer inspection is in two days.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Inspect another 100 of the next 1,000 blocks produced**
- **B Repair the blocks that have been found defective**
- **C Proceed with the production but create a mind map**
- **D Stop the production and conduct a root cause analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The question clearly tells us that the production process is faulty.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests you are in the Control Quality process performing an inspection of the
concrete blocks produced. The quality management plan allows for inspecting a 10% sample of
the concrete blocks produced rather than inspecting the entire lot. This technique is known as
statistical sampling and is used when it is believed there won't be many defects in project

---

deliverables or when inspecting the entire population will take too long, cost too much, or be too
destructive. According to the scenario, the quality management plan requires that all the blocks
are free of defect. However, during the inspection, you found some of the blocks were defective.
The use of statistical sampling for the inspection does not influence what the next step should be.
The production process is faulty as some defective blocks were produced. Customer inspection is
of secondary concern. You must stop the production and carry out a root-cause analysis of the
problem so that you will produce blocks free of defects as specified in the quality management
plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Inspect another 100 of the next 1,000 blocks produced**
Incorrect. Statistical sampling involves choosing a part of a population for inspection, for
example, 10% of the 1,000 concrete blocks, instead of inspecting all the blocks. You have
already determined that some of the blocks have defects, therefore, inspecting another 10%
will not change that fact.
- **B Repair the blocks that have been found defective**
Incorrect. While repairing the defective blocks may be possible, the repair will not prevent
cracks from occurring in a future set of blocks produced. It appears that there is a problem
somewhere in the production process since some of the blocks have cracks. Instead of
applying patches, the root cause of the problem should be found and fixed.
- **C Proceed with the production but create a mind map**
Incorrect. Mind mapping is an example of a data representation technique that can be used
in the Plan Quality Management process. This technique is a diagramming method that
helps visually organize information. Mind mapping is not used as part of the Control
Quality process described by the scenario. Proceeding with the production that results in
defective deliverable would ignore the specifications outlined in the quality management
plan.
- **D Stop the production and conduct a root cause analysis**
Correct. The quality management plan requires all blocks be free from defects. You have
found that some have minor cracks and therefore are defective. You need to perform a root
cause analysis to identify the source of the defects.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 303
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 85 of 200
Question ID: 651391
The agile project team members are all working in an open office space arrangement. There are
many conversations happening concurrently throughout the day.
Which of the following is the best option for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule frequent team checkpoints and post project artifacts in a transparent fashion**
- **B Request team members to hold off their conversations until formal meeting times**
- **C Record the conversations and post them in a shared repository**
- **D Designate afternoons as quiet work times**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Agile projects thrive on regular, informal communications.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Open, frequent, and informal communication is the cornerstone of agile managed projects. The
best form of communication is face to face conversations. Agile teams working in a collocated
space that supports communication is ideal. Planning communications management that hinders
or places boundaries on those conversations is counterproductive. A project manager needs to
encourage more communication, not less. A project manager also needs to support the capturing
and flow of communication between stakeholders. Scheduling more communication checkpoints,

---

such as daily standup meetings, increases the communication exchanges. And, when possible,
posting and distributing information to the team aids communication flow - whether in physical
locations, digitized, or both. Withholding conversations or enforcing extended quiet times is the
antithesis of good communication flow.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule frequent team checkpoints and post project artifacts in a transparent fashion**
Correct. Frequent and flexible information exchanges are good for agile management
projects. An open work arrangement supports that. Offering checkpoint times, posting
information, and other ways to support the sharing and access to information extends the
free flow of project knowledge and communications.
- **B Request team members to hold off their conversations until formal meeting times**
Incorrect. Agile managed projects thrive on open, constant face to face conversations
amongst stakeholders. Holding conversations to designated meeting times hinders the free
flow of information and the informal exchanges that occur regularly in agile projects.
- **C Record the conversations and post them in a shared repository**
Incorrect. With so many conversations occurring daily, capturing them all, storing them,
and distributing them in a manner that would be relevant, useful, and not out of date would
be highly unlikely and counterproductive.
- **D Designate afternoons as quiet work times**
Incorrect. Team members in an agile managed project collocated in an open arrangement
thrive on constant communication and ease of face-to-face conversation. Enforcing long
quiet periods is counterproductive.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 365
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 86 of 200
Question ID: 651359
An alert on the project's dashboard indicates that the project's CPI has gone above the upper
control limit on the control chart.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Communicate the results as a positive outcome**
- **B Find an assignable cause**
- **C Communicate the results as a negative outcome**
- **D Wait for the CPI to fall back within the control limits**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What does it mean to be out of the control limits?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes the Control Costs process. Earned value analysis (EVA) is an example of
the data analysis tools and techniques that can be used as part of this process. When monitoring
and controlling the costs of the project, the cost performance index (CPI) can be used to measure
the project's cost performance in a ratio using the earned value (EV) against actual costs (AC).
The CPI is not a steady, constant value. What is an acceptable fluctuation over time is
determined by the project. The ebbs and flows of the project's CPI can be tracked, measured, and

---

charted over time in a control chart. Any measurement that falls within the established upper and
lower control limits are within controls. Any value outside those limits indicates that something
is out of control. The reason why it is out of control must be found and assigned to a probable
cause.
Note, a CPI value greater than 1 means the project is below budget. Typically, this situation is
perceived as good for the project. However, this could also mean that costs estimates were
padded intentionally during planning to make project performance look better during execution.
Any variance is not a good thing and should be investigated. Additionally, the scenario does not
say the CPI is greater than 1. Rather, it says the CPI has gone above the upper control limit.
While it is reasonable to assume the upper control limit has been set above the value of 1, it
could be that the control limits have been set between 0.7 and 0.9. So if the CPI has been
measured at 0.95 (which is above the upper control limit), the project is still over budget.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communicate the results as a positive outcome**
Incorrect. The value that falls above the control limit is not a positive outcome in most
situations. Any value being measured and charted on a control chart is expected to remain
within the upper and lower limits. Any value outside those limits is considered out of
control.
- **B Find an assignable cause**
Correct. Values that are measured and charted over time in a control chart are expected to
fall within the established upper and lower control limits. Any value outside those limits
indicates that something is out of control. The reason for this incident is called an
assignable or special cause and should be investigated.
- **C Communicate the results as a negative outcome**
Incorrect. Any value that falls outside a control limit typically is not welcomed news since it
indicates that the value being measured is out of control. Nevertheless, this result may not
be a negative outcome until the reason is known.
- **D Wait for the CPI to fall back within the control limits**
Incorrect. While the CPI may eventually fall back into the control limits area, hoping for
this knowing the current CPI is out of control is withholding information from the project
stakeholders. Project managers are expected to provide accurate and timely
communications.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 262-263, 304, 702; see
also https://www.projectmanagement.com/discussion-topic/28349/Common-cause-VS-special-ca
use
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 87 of 200
Question ID: 613519
An infrastructure upgrade project is in the initial planning stage, and the project manager is
facilitating a risk workshop focused on prioritizing individual risks for further analysis or action.
Which of the following might lead to the development of more effective risk responses for this
project?
Top of Form
- **A Performing risk audits**
- **B Reviewing requirements documentation**
- **C Monitoring risks closely**
- **D Categorizing risks using RBS**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best way to focus attention and effort on the areas of highest risk exposure?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing individual project risks for
further analysis or action by assessing their probability of occurrence and impact as well as other
characteristics. This description reflects the scenario provided in the question. Risk
categorization is one of the tools and techniques which may be beneficial for this process. Risks
to the project can be categorized by sources of risk using a risk breakdown structure (RBS).

---

Grouping risks into categories can lead to the development of more effective risk responses by
focusing attention and effort on the areas of highest risk exposure, or by developing generic risk
responses to address groups of related risks. Therefore, of the available choices, categorizing
risks using RBS is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Performing risk audits**
Incorrect. Risk audits are among the tools and techniques of the Monitor Risks process and
are used to consider the effectiveness of the risk management process. The question states
the project is in the initial planning stage where risk audits are typically not applicable.
- **B Reviewing requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation is an input to the Identify Risks process and can
help the project team identify those requirements that could be at risk. However, for the
Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process described in the scenario, requirements
documentation is of little value.
- **C Monitoring risks closely**
Incorrect. Risks are monitored as part of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group,
whereas the scenario describes a project in early planning.
- **D Categorizing risks using RBS**
Correct. Risks to the project can be categorized by sources of risk using a risk breakdown
structure (RBS). Grouping risks into categories can lead to the development of more
effective risk responses by focusing attention and effort on the areas of highest risk
exposure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 425

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 88 of 200
Question ID: 651344
- **A software development project is being chartered. The sponsor informs the to-be-assigned**
project manager that while the project will be performed using the traditional predictive project
management approach, the deliverables will be developed incrementally, over the course of
several iterations, by a team of agile practitioners.
How does that directive alter the expectations of the project manager's role?
Top of Form
- **A More reliance on the project manager to plan out the work**
- **B Nothing changes for the project manager.**
- **C The role of the project manager is replaced by the product owner.**
- **D More servant leadership and team delegation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In agile project management, the cooperative team is of high importance.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a hybrid project, which will be managed using the traditional project
management approach; however, the deliverables will be developed in an agile manner. Initiating
a project where the project team will be comprised of agile practitioners compared to a project
lead in a more traditional approach does alter the role and expectations of a project manager. On

---

projects where deliverables are developed using agile practices, the project teams are smaller and
more heavily involved in the planning and decision making. The teams are typically more
independent, self-organizing, and self-managing. Therefore, project managers must transition
from a top-down command-and-control management style to servant leadership which fosters
involvement and focuses on building a collaborative decision-making environment.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A More reliance on the project manager to plan out the work**
Incorrect. The project work in an agile approach is planned by the entire project team, not
just the project manager. Hence, the expectation is 'less' reliance on the project manager to
plan the project work, not more.
- **B Nothing changes for the project manager.**
Incorrect. The role of a project manager does alter somewhat when a project (or parts of it)
is managed in an agile manner compared to managing the project in a more traditional
way.
- **C The role of the project manager is replaced by the product owner.**
Incorrect. It's true that on projects where deliverables are developed using agile practices,
there are additional roles, such as the product owner. However, this individual does not
'replace' the project manager. Instead, the project manager role 'complements' that of the
product owner. For example, the product owner is mainly responsible for the scope of the
project, while the project manager leads all other aspects of the project and facilitates
collaboration. A project manager on an agile project is sometimes called the scrum master
or an agile coach.
- **D More servant leadership and team delegation**
Correct. In an agile approach to project management, the project manager's role focuses
more on building and supporting collaboration and the delegation of planning and decision
making to the team.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 74, 65
Agile Practice Guide - First Edition, 2017 Project Management Institute, page 39

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 89 of 200
Question ID: 612999
During a recession, a project manager posts a positive risk that in the current economic
environment, cheaper resources may become available. On the way into work, the project
manager hears about a competitor going out of business and contacts the competitor to acquire
some equipment, materials, and supplies at a fraction of their normal value.
What is the project manager doing?
Top of Form
- **A Executing a mitigation plan**
- **B Reacting to a contingency plan trigger**
- **C Transferring an identified risk**
- **D Sharing a realized positive risk**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

An event has occurred to make the opportunity arise.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Some risk responses are designed for use only if certain events occur. For some risks, it is
appropriate for the project team to make a response plan that will only be executed under certain
predefined conditions. Risk responses identified using this technique are often called

---

contingency plans or fallback plans and include identified triggering events that set the plans in
effect.
The question describes a positive risk (opportunity) that was identified and captured in the risk
register along with the risk trigger and responses. Part of the responsibility of the project
manager and the risk owner is to understand what events may cause (or trigger) a risk to occur.
In this case, the project manager heard of a competitor going out of business which triggered the
action of contacting the competitor to acquire resources much cheaper than they otherwise could
have been purchased. Note that the project manager also exploited an opportunity in this
situation. However, exploiting the realized risk was not offered as an answer choice. Therefore,
of the available options, reacting to a contingency plan trigger is the best response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Executing a mitigation plan**
Incorrect. A positive risk is also known as an opportunity. Mitigation represents a strategy
to respond to a threat rather than an opportunity. The project manager should exploit, not
mitigate, the opportunity described by the question.
- **B Reacting to a contingency plan trigger**
Correct. The question suggests that a positive risk (opportunity) was captured in the risk
register. The news of the competitor going out of business was a trigger that action must be
taken to realize the benefits of the previously identified opportunity.
- **C Transferring an identified risk**
Incorrect. Transference involves shifting ownership of a threat to a third party who will
manage the risk and bear its impact if the threat occurs. The most common example of
transference is the purchase of insurance. It does not make sense for the project manager to
transfer a positive risk (opportunity).
- **D Sharing a realized positive risk**
Incorrect. Sharing involves transferring ownership of an opportunity to a third party so
that it shares some of the benefits if the opportunity occurs. In this scenario, the project
manager is exploiting an opportunity, and there is no indication that the benefits are being
shared. If the project manager partnered with another company to acquire the resources,
then the project manager would be sharing the positive risk (opportunity).

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 445
Bottom of Form

Bottom of Form Prev Next

Question 90 of 200
Question ID: 651422
The project team has worked for months on an open-ended concept product for their
organization. Some team members are ready to push it out to users to get feedback. Others are
not sure.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Release the product then ask the team to validate scope**
- **B Consider the options then go with what feels right**
- **C Hear the competing arguments then ask all to vote**
- **D Refer to the stakeholder register then decide**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Have all viewpoints been considered?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Performing the Validate Scope process requires some decisions as to whether the scope is, in
fact, complete and acceptable. There are many tools and techniques a project manager can use
with stakeholders to make decisions. In this scenario, the stakeholders involved in validating the
scope are members of the project team. As such, there is some interpretation as to whether the
project that delivers on an open-ended concept product may or may not have clear directives and

---

well-documented scope and requirements. The decision making requires more input and
consultation with those involved. Before any decision is made, it is advisable to concern all
inputs, perspectives, and arguments. After an appropriate time to discuss those inputs relative to
the project and its timeline, a more informed decision can be made.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Release the product then ask the team to validate scope**
Incorrect. Although the scope can be validated further with the feedback and information
gained from the release, main validation of the scope to formally accept the deliverables
occurs before releasing the deliverable.
- **B Consider the options then go with what feels right**
Incorrect. Gut feelings and other impressions done without any data to back decisions can
work from time to time but is not a recommended practice. Evaluating data will make for
better and informed decisions.
- **C Hear the competing arguments then ask all to vote**
Correct. Decision making regarding validation of the scope is best done by incorporating
or including the input from various stakeholders to add confidence to the decision because
multiple perspectives and evaluations were considered.
- **D Refer to the stakeholder register then decide**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register documents the identification, assessment, and
classification of project stakeholders. This information is not sufficient for the project team
to decide on whether to release the product or not.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166

PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 91 of 200
Question ID: 613294
One of the risks that has been identified during project planning is that the company will be
unable to retain the planned number of qualified developers for the software development project
you are leading. You need to determine the likelihood of this risk as well as its impact on the
project schedule.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Meet with the developers and get their input**
- **B Create a probability and impact matrix**
- **C Perform a risk data quality assessment**
- **D Conduct a risk probability and impact assessment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What data analysis technique associated with the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process
evaluates the likelihood that a specific risk will occur and the potential effect on one or more
project objectives?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you are conducting the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process.
Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis is the process of prioritizing individual project risks for

---

further analysis or action by assessing their probability of occurrence and impact as well as other
characteristics. A data analysis technique associated with this process is the risk probability and
impact assessment. Risk probability assessment considers the likelihood that a specific risk will
occur, such as the risk that the company would be unable to retain some of its developers
planned for the project. Therefore, to determine the likelihood of this risk as well as its impact on
the project schedule, conducting a risk probability and impact assessment is what you should do
first.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Meet with the developers and get their input**
Incorrect. It is unlikely that the developers will share their plans to leave the company with
you. Additionally, it is unclear from the scenario what is the reason the company is unable
to retain their employees. If it's the matter of budget, then even if the developers do not
have plans to leave, the company may be the one who lets them go. There are too many
assumptions in this choice making it not the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Create a probability and impact matrix**
Incorrect. A probability and impact matrix is a grid for mapping the probability of
occurrence of each risk and its impact on project objectives if that risk occurs. A
probability and impact matrix may be used to graphically represent the probability and
impact of the risk described by the question. However, an assessment must first be made to
determine the values which will be entered into the probability and impact matrix.
- **C Perform a risk data quality assessment**
Incorrect. Risk data quality assessment evaluates the degree to which the data about
individual project risks is accurate and reliable as a basis for qualitative risk analysis. A
risk data quality assessment would not provide an assessment of the probability and impact
of the risk described by the question.
- **D Conduct a risk probability and impact assessment**
Correct. A risk probability assessment considers the likelihood that a specific risk will
occur. A risk impact assessment considers the potential effect on one or more project
objectives, such as the project schedule.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 423

Question 92 of 200
Question ID: 613430
- **A project manager is in the process of obtaining the necessary equipment and team members for**
her construction project. She has just learned that the grader originally planned for use on the
project is not available and has decided to rent two smaller graders instead. The project manager
will also add a new team member to run the second grader.
What is the project manager least likely to do next?
Top of Form
- **A Create the resource management plan**
- **B Modify the resource requirements**
- **C Adjust the resource breakdown structure**
- **D Revise the stakeholder register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is performing the Acquire Resources process rather than the Plan Resource
Management process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is conducting the Acquire Resources process by
obtaining equipment and team members for the project. All of the answer choices represent items
that may be updated in this scenario. While the resource management plan may be 'updated'

---

during the Acquire Resources process to reflect actual experience in acquiring resources for the
project, it is 'created' earlier in the project as part of the Plan Resource Management process.
Thus, the resource management plan would already exist at this point in the project. Note, the
question is asking for the activity that the project manager is 'least' likely to perform in this
scenario. Therefore, of the available options, creating the resource management plan is the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Create the resource management plan**
Correct. The question implies that the Acquire Resources process is underway. The
resource management plan is created earlier in the project as part of project planning.
Thus, the resource management plan would already exist at this point in the project.
Therefore, creating the resource management plan is the least likely next step for the
project manager to take.
- **B Modify the resource requirements**
Incorrect. The resource requirements reflect the types and quantities of resources required
for each activity in a work package. Resource requirements documentation should be
updated in this scenario to reflect the resources acquired for the project.
- **C Adjust the resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The resource breakdown structure is a hierarchical representation of resources
by category and type. Resources acquired during the Acquire Resources process are
recorded in the resource breakdown structure.
- **D Revise the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register should be revised in this scenario to reflect the addition
of the second grader operator. As a project team member, the grader operator is also a
stakeholder in the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 334-335

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 93 of 200
Question ID: 651429
The project is required to notify the public at various stages. A public relations specialist was
involved in planning the communications for the project. Now, when the project is in execution,
the communications with the public up to this point do not appear to be effective. A survey
revealed only 2% of the public was aware of the project.
Whom should the project manager contact first?
Top of Form
- **A The public relations specialist**
- **B The project sponsor**
- **C The project management office**
- **D A quality specialist**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who knows most about the topic?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario surrounds the Monitor Communications process. Expert judgment is among the
tools and techniques that can be used as part of this process. Expertise should be considered from
individuals or groups with specialized knowledge or training in communications with the public,
the community, and the media.

---

When monitoring and controlling the project communications there are often many people
involved in the process. A project manager's role is not always to be the one performing all the
project activities, but assuring that they are being done. For the benefit of the project and all
involved, activities, such as in this scenario where decisions need to be made regarding the
communications with external stakeholders (the public), the project manager is better off
consulting with those who know most and can suggest the most effective solutions. That is the
public relations specialist in the company. S/He is the subject matter expert (SME) in this case.
They are most equipped to recommend what to do next. The project manager and relevant
stakeholder can make an informed decision based on the advice from the SME. The project
manager is the one responsible for turning those decisions into actionable plans and results. The
project sponsor provides the authority and support - typically in the form of resources and
finances - to commission those actions. All the identified roles are involved, but the best advice
can come from the one with the most expert judgment.
While it can be argued for the effectiveness (or the lack thereof) of the public relations specialist,
project communications failure cannot be blamed on only one person. The specialist was
involved in project planning, however, it is unclear if the specialist's inputs have been properly
documented. And even if yes, the failure could have been caused by the improper
implementation of the Manage Communications process. There are too many assumptions to be
made as to why the communications up to this point do not appear to be effective. While the
public relations specialist could be one of the reasons, under the circumstances described in the
scenario and with the given set of the answer choices (none of which is a perfect/ideal answer), it
is still the public relations specialist who is the best to advise on how to proceed with the
communications with the public.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The public relations specialist**
Correct. At this point to best monitor and control the communications the expert judgment
of a public relations subject matter expert is best to determine what is the next best action
for the project.
- **B The project sponsor**
Incorrect. The project sponsor is backing the project, primarily thru finances and
resources. The project sponsor would not typically have the knowledge related to the
communication needs of the public.
- **C The project management office**
Incorrect. The project management office (PMO) is an organizational structure that
standardizes the project-related governance processes and facilitates the sharing of

---

resources, methodologies, tools, and techniques. It is unlikely that contacting the PMO
would help the project manager in advising on the issue described in the scenario.
- **D A quality specialist**
Incorrect. A quality specialist would be most helpful with quality management issues
related to the project rather than topics covering communications with the public.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 391
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 94 of 200
Question ID: 651342
The previous project was a failure, and its objectives have not been achieved. However, since the
organization still needs the deliverables that were to be produced by that project, the organization
initiates a new project.
What should the project manager do to ensure that the new project starts with a higher
probability of success?
Top of Form
- **A Include the assumption in the project charter that this project may also fail to set stakeholder**
expectations accordingly
- **B Make certain that the team members from the failed project are not involved in the new project**
to avoid repeating the failure
- **C Review the lessons learned from the failed project to incorporate this knowledge into the project**
charter of the new project
- **D Gather information from the project manager and the team of the failed project and use this**
information to plan the new project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How do we know what went wrong the previous time?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**


---

Based on the scenario, it can be inferred that the project is in initiating. When initiating new
projects in any organization, examining and assessing the successes and failures of past projects
can serve as excellent information to support the project(s) under consideration. Learning from
failed projects can provide valuable information towards the success of another project.
Repeating the same mistakes should not occur if the organization reviews past projects, assesses
the lessons learned, and applies them to the next project, as in the form of the project chartering
in this scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Include the assumption in the project charter that this project may also fail to set**
stakeholder expectations accordingly
Incorrect. All projects may fail. There is no need to call out that failure as an option and a
possibility. Stakeholder expectations can be managed in other ways.
- **B Make certain that the team members from the failed project are not involved in the new**
project to avoid repeating the failure
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if the team was the
reason for the failure of the previous project and should be excluded from working on the
new one. Furthermore, including team members from previous, failed projects may actually
be a benefit, not a liability, for the next project. They bring experiences and lessons learned
that could be shared and applied.
- **C Review the lessons learned from the failed project to incorporate this knowledge into the**
project charter of the new project
Correct. Positioning a project for success takes in information and assessments from many
angles. This includes the lessons learned from previous projects - successful or failed.
- **D Gather information from the project manager and the team of the failed project and use**
this information to plan the new project
Incorrect. While meeting with the project manager and the team of the previous failed
project may provide insights into the reasons for the failure of that project, the information
they will share may be biased and/or faded. Additionally, it is unclear if those individuals
are still available.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 74

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 95 of 200
Question ID: 651402
After completing eight iterations, the team realizes the mistakes they made in the first iteration.
What is the next best action for the project team to do?
Top of Form
- **A Proceed to the next iteration as planned**
- **B Update the lessons learned repository**
- **C Apply the lesson learned to the next iteration**
- **D Restart the first iteration**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When is this knowledge most useful?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario is designed around the Manage Project Knowledge process which is the process of
using existing knowledge and creating new knowledge to achieve the project's objectives and
contribute to organizational learning. Managing the vast amount of project knowledge and the
lessons that are constantly learned by all project stakeholders throughout the project enables the
project team to leverage that knowledge and apply it. Applying lessons learned and project
knowledge supports the project organization, the project outcomes, and operation of the current
and future projects. Documenting the knowledge into a lesson learned register is one method of

---

capturing that knowledge to ensure it is not lost. Applying that knowledge to the project is even
more beneficial. There is a misconception that projects must wait until the end of a project in
order to document it. Just accepting mistakes happened is not enough. Knowledge is fluid and
best shared and used at the point it is most needed.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Proceed to the next iteration as planned**
Incorrect. Mistakes happen on projects all the time. It is important that the project team
understands their mistakes and how to correct or avoid repeating them in the future.
Proceeding to the next iteration as planned without taking any action to correct the
mistakes is unlikely to be the best choice in this situation.
- **B Update the lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. The lessons learned repository is a store of historical information about the
lessons learned from projects. The lessons learned repository is typically updated at the end
of the project/phase as part of project/phase closure. It is unclear from the scenario
provided if the project has entered the Close Project or Phase process. Therefore, updating
the lessons learned repository may be premature.
- **C Apply the lesson learned to the next iteration**
Correct. The project knowledge and the lessons learned are most useful when applied. This
knowledge may be explicit and immediately applicable or could be tacit and subtly
influence the decisions and actions at any point throughout the project.
- **D Restart the first iteration**
Incorrect. Project iterations are timeboxed sections of a project organized in an agile
fashion. Projects and iterations move forward. Restarting the first iteration is unfeasible. It
would be better to apply the lesson to the next iteration instead of trying to rewrite history.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 100

Question 96 of 200
Question ID: 612643
You are managing the development of a new product. The customer has provided the objectives
and description of the product. The project team is decomposing the customer's high-level
requirements to the level of detail needed to design the product and define its scope.
In which activity is the project team involved?
Top of Form
- **A Technical performance analysis**
- **B Data analysis**
- **C Define Activities**
- **D Product analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The term used to describe various techniques such as system engineering, product breakdown,
and value engineering.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies you are in the Define Scope process. Product analysis is among the tools
and techniques of this process and can be used to define products and services. By asking
questions about a product and forming answers to those questions, a description of the use,
characteristics, and other relevant aspects can be determined about the product that is going to be

---

delivered. In product analysis, requirements are captured at a high level and decomposed to the
level of detail needed to design the final product which is what described by the scenario,
making product analysis the best answer to the question asked. Examples of product analysis
techniques include product breakdown, requirements analysis, systems analysis, systems
engineering, value analysis, and value engineering.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Technical performance analysis**
Incorrect. Technical performance analysis is a technique that compares technical
accomplishments during project execution to the schedule of technical achievement. This
technique is part of the Monitor Risks process while the situation described in the scenario
implies the project is in planning.
- **B Data analysis**
Incorrect. Data analysis is a way of organizing, assessing and evaluating data and
information. The scenario describes a team working to define the scope, specifically to
define the product; they are not analyzing data.
- **C Define Activities**
Incorrect. The Define Activities process decomposes work packages obtained from the WBS
into schedule activities that provide a basis for estimating, scheduling, executing,
monitoring, and controlling the project work. In the scenario described, you are defining
the scope which precedes the processes of Create WBS and Estimate Activities, making this
choice an incorrect answer.
- **D Product analysis**
Correct. For projects that have a product as a deliverable, product analysis can be used as
a tool to define the scope of the product. As described in the scenario, requirements are
captured at a high level and decomposed to the level of detail needed to design the final
product.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 97 of 200
Question ID: 613455
- **A project manager is getting ready to transition the final product to the customer.**
Which of the following should the project manager issue as part of this process?
Top of Form
- **A Risk report**
- **B Final report**
- **C Quality report**
- **D Transition report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the following is an output of the Close Project or Phase process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The final product, service, or result transition is one of the main outputs of the Close Project or
Phase process. The question states that the project manager is getting ready to transition the final
product to the customer implying the project is in the Close Project or Phase process. The final
report provides a summary of the project performance and may include information such as the
summary level description of the project or phase, objectives of scope, quality, cost as well as the
criteria used to determine if the project has met these objectives. Of the choices provided, the

---

final report is the only document 'issued' during the Close Project or Phase process and is the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk report**
Incorrect. The risk report is a project document developed progressively throughout the
project. This report summarizes information on individual project risks and the level of
overall project risk. The risk report will likely be marked as the final version as part of the
Close Project or Phase process described in the scenario, however, is not likely to be
'issued' at this point in the project.
- **B Final report**
Correct. The final report is a project document that provides a summary of the project
performance. The final report is among the outputs of the Close Project or Phase which is
the process suggested by the scenario.
- **C Quality report**
Incorrect. The quality report is a project document that includes quality management
issues, recommendations for corrective actions, and a summary of findings from quality
control activities. The quality report is issued as an output from the Manage Quality
process rather than during project closure inferred by the scenario.
- **D Transition report**
Incorrect. 'Transition report' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127
