Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 124 of 200
Question ID: 651328
- **A project has been closed for a week. The project manager for that project has been notified that**
resources are still charging to the project's account.
Which of the following is the most likely reason for this situation?
Top of Form
- **A While closing the project, the project manager did not release all the resources from the project**
- **B While planning the project, the project manager did not estimate how long the resources were to**
be needed
- **C While closing the project, the project manager did not acquire stakeholder acceptance**
- **D While initiating the project, the project manager did not clarify the expected end to the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Why would resources still be billing a project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When closing a project, the project manager is responsible for ensuring that all personnel,
equipment, materials, and other resources are released and no longer assigned to the project. Not
properly releasing the resources risks resources remaining on the project even after the project is
closed and billing to the project.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A While closing the project, the project manager did not release all the resources from the**
project
Correct. The project manager is responsible for ensuring all resources - human and
physical - are released from the project and no longer billable to the project.
- **B While planning the project, the project manager did not estimate how long the resources**
were to be needed
Incorrect. Once the project ends, resources should not be billing to the project regardless
how long the project manager estimated their need unless it explicitly stated in some
agreement that resources may charge to a project even after closure.
- **C While closing the project, the project manager did not acquire stakeholder acceptance**
Incorrect. The project is closed meaning stakeholder acceptance was obtained. Regardless,
their acceptance does not impact the resource billing.
- **D While initiating the project, the project manager did not clarify the expected end to the**
project
Incorrect. When initiating the project, the project manager and other project stakeholders
are speculating the duration of the project, but these estimates are high level and not for
certain. Also, at that point in a project, a project manager does not fully understand the
resource needs, duration, and other details.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 125 of 200
Question ID: 612085
You are managing an engineering design project. The vendor has created 50 engineering
drawings. Since the project is on a tight schedule and budget, checking every drawing for
accuracy and completeness would be impossible. You direct the team to randomly select 20
drawings for inspection.
This exercise can best be described as an example of:
Top of Form
- **A Inspection**
- **B Statistical sampling**
- **C Attribute sampling**
- **D Control charting**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What data gathering technique involves choosing a portion of a population to inspect for quality
control?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

This scenario is an example of statistical sampling since it involves the team selecting 20 out of
50 engineering drawings at random to measure accuracy and completeness. Statistical sampling
is among the data gathering techniques that can be used as part of the Control Quality process.

---

Statistical sampling is often applied when inspecting the entire population would be too costly or
time-consuming. In this instance, given that the project is on a tight schedule and budget,
statistical sampling makes sense to use to inspect the engineering drawings.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Inspection**
Incorrect. An inspection is the examination of a work product to determine if it conforms to
documented standards. In the scenario described, inspection is what the team is doing on
the individual drawings. Randomly selecting a portion of a population for an inspection is
a different technique which is better described by another answer choice.
- **B Statistical sampling**
Correct. The team is using a data gathering technique known as statistical sampling, which
involves selecting a random portion of a population of work products (in this case,
engineering drawings) for inspection to measure controls and verify quality. Statistical
sampling can be used when inspecting the entire population may take too long or cost too
much.
- **C Attribute sampling**
Incorrect. Attribute sampling involves inspecting a work product to determine whether the
item being sampled possesses certain characteristics, or attributes (e.g., color or size). In
attribute sampling there are two responses to a test: yes or no - the result either conforms
or does not conform to established specifications. In the scenario, there is not enough
information to determine if attribute sampling is the specific technique being used to
inspect the engineering drawings.
- **D Control charting**
Incorrect. A control chart is a type of data representation technique used to determine
whether or not a process is stable or has predictable performance. Control charting
involves specifying upper and lower specification limits based on project requirements, as
well as statistically calculated control limits, to help determine if the processes are in
control. In the scenario, the team is inspecting a random sampling of engineering drawings
to verify their accuracy and completeness. This activity is different from control charting.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 303

PMP Exam 7

Question 126 of 200
Question ID: 612959
- **A domestic vendor that is supplying the most critical component for a project you are leading is**
acquired by a major foreign conglomerate. The conglomerate has a history of replacing the
executive team in the companies they acquire with new people from their corporate office. The
only change that affects your project is that invoices are now payable to the conglomerate's
corporate office.
Which of the following project artifacts will you least likely need to update?
Top of Form
- **A Communications management plan**
- **B Schedule baseline**
- **C Procurement management plan**
- **D Risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The acquiring company inherits all of the assets and liabilities of the company being acquired.
Delivering the project as planned is one of the liabilities of the acquiring company.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where a foreign company has acquired an important vendor
and will likely replace the executive management of the company acquired. These changes may

---

impact the current project, which might require updates to components of the project
management plan. Note, the question is asking to select an item that will 'least' likely need to be
updated. The contract with the vendor is still valid as the acquiring company inherits all of the
assets and liabilities of the company being acquired. Thus, the vendor is still legally obligated to
provide the deliverables according to the existing schedule as contracted. While the change in
executive structure may introduce new risks that might eventually affect the schedule, those risks
should be captured in the risk register rather than directly reflected in the schedule baseline.
Therefore, of the available choices, the schedule baseline is the least likely project artifact to be
updated.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan describes how project communications
will be planned, structured, implemented, and monitored for effectiveness. This plan likely
needs to be updated to reflect a change in communications needs with the vendor’s new
corporate offices.
- **B Schedule baseline**
Correct. At this point, there is no need to update the schedule baseline, although any
schedule concerns need to be documented in the risk register.
- **C Procurement management plan**
Incorrect. The procurement management plan contains the activities to be undertaken
during the procurement process. This plan likely needs to be updated around the change in
payments and any issues with currency exchange, especially if there were no foreign
vendors in the past.
- **D Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository in which the outputs of the risk management
process are recorded. There are many potential risks in an acquisition that may affect the
project ranging from new management, policies, processes, etc. Those new risks should be
documented in the risk register.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 489-491

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 127 of 200
Question ID: 651369
You are leading a project for a client. A vendor you contracted with to supply materials for the
project was late on delivery on two separate instances. This caused you to delay the deliverables
to the client, who inflicted penalty costs on your project as specified in the terms and conditions
of the contract with the client.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Cancel the contract with the client**
- **B Analyze the vendor's financial records**
- **C Cancel the contract with the vendor**
- **D Revise the lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What does the project team know?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Monitoring and controlling the project requires observing and learning from what has happened,
what is happening, and what could be happening in the project. Discussing and capturing the
lessons learned from the interactions with the vendor and the penalties incurred by the client can
guide the project team on how to manage things better and complete the project. Especially in

---

this situation where the issue has occurred more than once. Much can be gleaned from the two
deliveries in this project, whether or not additional deliveries from this vendor are expected or
planned. Learning from what goes well and what goes wrong is useful for the project and future
projects. Revising the lessons learned register is another way of saying capturing the lessons
learned from the experience the project has had with the vendor. Updates to the lessons learned
register are among the outputs of the Control Costs process implied by the scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cancel the contract with the client**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the penalty costs inflicted by the client are in line with
the terms and conditions of the contract with the client. It is your vendor and not the client
who is at fault. Canceling the contract with the client does not seem to be the best course of
action in this situation.
- **B Analyze the vendor's financial records**
Incorrect. The financial solvency of the vendor is not under question or at issue in the
scenario. What is at issue is the vendor's ability to deliver on time.
- **C Cancel the contract with the vendor**
Incorrect. The terms and conditions of the procurement agreements between the project and
the vendor are not identified in the scenario. Canceling without further qualifiers and
additional information is premature and presumptive.
- **D Revise the lessons learned register**
Correct. Many things can be learned, especially where similar situations have occurred
more than once. Discussing and capturing any lessons and observations benefit the project
and the project team.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 270

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 128 of 200
Question ID: 613672
You are planning a project to upgrade the software for your company's retail point-of-sale
system. You need to assign an approximate value to the investment that will be required for the
project. After finishing the necessary analysis using a bottom-up approach, you are forecasting
that a $50,000 investment will be needed for the project plus an additional $5,000 for a
contingency reserve, and $5,000 as a management reserve.
What have you created in this scenario?
Top of Form
- **A Scope baseline**
- **B Cost management plan**
- **C Cost performance index**
- **D Cost estimates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What do the probable costs of a project represent?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Estimate Costs process is being carried out. One output of the
Estimate Costs process is cost estimates. Cost estimates include quantitative assessments of the
probable costs required to complete project work, as well as contingency amounts to account for

---

identified risks, and a management reserve to cover unplanned work. Cost estimates have been
produced based on the description provided by the question.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The question implies that the Estimate Costs process is underway. The scope
baseline is an output of the Create WBS process and not the Estimate Costs process.
- **B Cost management plan**
Incorrect. The cost management plan describes how costs will be planned, structured, and
controlled. The cost management plan does not produce cost estimates as implied in the
question.
- **C Cost performance index**
Incorrect. The cost performance index (CPI) is expressed as the ratio of earned value to
actual cost. The question states that the project is in the planning stage. Therefore, the
project could not have produced any earned value with which to calculate a CPI.
- **D Cost estimates**
Correct. Cost estimates include quantitative assessments of the probable costs required to
complete project work, as well as contingency amounts to account for identified risks, and
a management reserve to cover unplanned work.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 246
Bottom of Form

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 129 of 200
Question ID: 651416
As an employee of a large organization, you have been building a business case for a community
outreach project. The project selection steering committee is meeting in a few weeks.
What is the best action for you to get your project chartered?
Top of Form
- **A Find a potential sponsor who can champion your project at the meeting**
- **B Use pre-assignment to secure the best available team in the organization**
- **C Prepare the list of key project deliverables and milestone schedule**
- **D Offer to act as both the project sponsor and the project manager**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who holds more influence to get a project chartered?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

To develop and greenlight a project to initiate via a project charter, a project sponsor is needed to
authorize and allocate necessary resources to fulfill project objectives. The project sponsor may
be an individual or a group of individuals. Whatever the makeup of the entity, a sponsor must be
willing to back a project and its alignment to business needs and strategy. In this scenario, there
is a project selection steering committee. Having someone on that committee to evangelize the
benefits, merits, and business case of a project proposal increases the chances of the project

---

being selected and chartered. No other work on the project, such as pre-assignment of resources,
should occur until a project is chartered.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Find a potential sponsor who can champion your project at the meeting**
Correct. The steering committee at the enterprise in this scenario selects projects.
Presenting and attempting to influence a potential sponsor who is part of the selection and
can support its selection is the best action for a project manager to get the project
chartered.
- **B Use pre-assignment to secure the best available team in the organization**
Incorrect. No project has yet been chartered. As such, no resources should be acquired,
procured, or pre-assigned. There are no funds granted for these actions. Additionally, it is
unclear from the scenario if you even have the power and authority over resources.
- **C Prepare the list of key project deliverables and milestone schedule**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project has not yet even been selected. Key project
deliverables and milestone schedule are typically prepared later, during project initiation,
as part of the Develop Project Charter process, which has not yet started (and may not
even start if the project is not selected eventually).
- **D Offer to act as both the project sponsor and the project manager**
Incorrect. A project sponsor must be someone or some group with enough authority and
ability to allocate resources. It is unclear from the scenario if you have the necessary power
and authority in the organization to sponsor the project. Typically, employees in large
organizations do not have the power to charter their own projects and subsequently lead
them.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 73, 75-77

Question 130 of 200
Question ID: 625024
It comes to the attention of the project manager that some of the vendors do not receive project
communications, although the project management plan has specific instructions as to how
project information should be shared with vendors.
What might be the most likely reason that has caused this issue?
Top of Form
- **A Neglecting to include vendors in the communications management plan**
- **B There is no issue; vendors are not supposed to receive project communications**
- **C Forgetting to perform the Develop Project Management Plan process**
- **D Failing to review the agreements as part of the Identify Stakeholders process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager must fulfill their contractual obligations.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

If the vendors were not captured in the stakeholder register as part of the Identify Stakeholders
process, the result could be missed communications. The agreements serve as an input to the
Identify Stakeholders process since the parties to an agreement are stakeholders by definition. If
the project team failed to review the agreements when the stakeholder register was created, the
result could be an incomplete stakeholder register. The stakeholder register, in turn, serves as an

---

input to the Plan Communications Management process by providing the list of stakeholders
with whom project information can be shared. Obviously, if some stakeholders are not recorded
in the stakeholder register, they would not receive project communications. Therefore, of the
available choices, the most likely cause of the issue described by the question is the failure to
review the agreements as part of the Identify Stakeholders process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Neglecting to include vendors in the communications management plan**
Incorrect. The scenario indicates that the project management plan specifies the vendors to
be included in project communications, implying the communications management plan,
which is a component of the project management plan, has been properly developed.
- **B There is no issue; vendors are not supposed to receive project communications**
Incorrect. Vendors are project stakeholders. The decision on whether or not to include them
in project communications is made during project planning and is documented in the
communications management plan (a component of the project management plan).
According to the scenario, the project management plan specifies that the vendors should
receive project communications, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **C Forgetting to perform the Develop Project Management Plan process**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, project communications are specified in the project
management plan. This plan is the main output of the Develop Project Management Plan
process, implying this process has been performed.
- **D Failing to review the agreements as part of the Identify Stakeholders process**
Correct. If the project team was unable to review the agreements when the stakeholder
register was created, the result could be an incomplete stakeholder register. Those
stakeholders that were not recorded in the stakeholder register are not likely to receive
project communications.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 510

Question 131 of 200
Question ID: 613156
You are facilitating a sprint planning meeting. The attendees include seven developers, a scrum
master, and a product owner. The team has already decomposed the selected highest-priority user
stories from the product backlog into actionable tasks with estimates in hours. To establish the
sprint backlog, you call for the fist-of-five technique. Five developers hold up three fingers, and
two developers hold up two fingers.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Close the meeting, because the sprint plan is done**
- **B Set the team's capacity for the current sprint to 19 hours**
- **C Ask the two developers to explain their objections**
- **D Ask the five developers to pull three stories to their queue**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The goal of the fist-of-five technique is to achieve consensus: the more fingers, the more support
for the decision.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario, the team is involved in the Estimate Activity Durations process.
Decision Making is among the tools an techniques of this process and is typically used during

---

meetings. The question describes a sprint planning meeting where the team has been estimating
the duration of each activity required to complete the work for the upcoming sprint. The next
step is to validate that the selected amount of work is achievable within the time available during
the sprint, based on the team's capacity, availability, skill, resources, and past performance. In
this scenario, five developers held up three fingers. If this group of five had been the entire
development team, their vote of three fingers would be enough to achieve a consensus. Notice
that none of them fully support the currently selected sprint backlog. If any voters had held up
five fingers, that would indicate complete support. The developers who held up less than three
fingers should voice their objections. The team can then adjust the sprint backlog to resolve those
objections. The team repeats the vote until a consensus is achieved, where all votes are three
fingers or more. With a consensus, the team commits to the product owner that the sprint backlog
will be complete in the upcoming sprint.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Close the meeting, because the sprint plan is done**
Incorrect. In the fist-of-five technique, holding up two fingers is a sign that more discussion
is needed to achieve consensus and commitment before the meeting can be closed.
- **B Set the team's capacity for the current sprint to 19 hours**
Incorrect. The fist-of-five technique is not used to identify the number of hours or other
measures of time the team is available to work.
- **C Ask the two developers to explain their objections**
Correct. In the fist-of-five technique, the developers who held up less than three fingers
should share what prevents them from committing to completing the selected sprint backlog
items within the current iteration.
- **D Ask the five developers to pull three stories to their queue**
Incorrect. The fist-of-five technique is not used to assign tasks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 203

Question 132 of 200
Question ID: 613200
After losing a member of her high performing team, the project manager implements the
response planned for this risk by hiring an independent contractor. However, as a result of adding
the new team member, the team is thrown back to the storming stage of team development, and
the project falls behind schedule.
How might the project manager have avoided this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Developed a response plan for the residual risk**
- **B Established sufficient contingency reserves**
- **C Developed a response plan for the secondary risk**
- **D Established sufficient management reserves**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Residual risk is the risk that remains after risk responses have been implemented, whereas a
secondary risk is a risk that arises as a direct result of implementing a risk response.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

- **A secondary risk is a risk that arises as a direct result of implementing a risk response. In this**
case, the risk response of replacing a team member introduced the secondary risk of the team
member disrupting the cohesiveness of the high performing team represented by the team

---

reverting to the storming stage of team development. Thus, the team falling behind schedule is
the result of the secondary risk posed by the introduction a new member to the team. One cannot
assume that a newly hired team member will be able to replace a member of a high performing
team without some disruption. The project manager should have anticipated this secondary risk
and developed an appropriate risk response. For example, the project manager could have
included schedule reserves during project planning to address this secondary risk, which may
have prevented the project from falling behind schedule. Therefore, of the choices provided,
identifying the secondary risk and developing a response plan to address it could have helped
avoid the situation described in the scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Developed a response plan for the residual risk**
Incorrect. Residual risk is the risk that remains after risk responses have been implemented.
Although residual risk may or may not have been a factor in this case, the risks associated
with the implementation of the risk response by introducing a new member to a high
performing team is best described as a secondary risk. In this scenario, the secondary risk
is more likely to be the cause of the project running behind schedule rather than any
residual risk.
- **B Established sufficient contingency reserves**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are established to address known risks. According to the
scenario, the planned risk response has been implemented implying contingency reserves
have been established and were sufficient.
- **C Developed a response plan for the secondary risk**
Correct. The risk that the new team member might not perform as well as the original team
member, or disrupt the cohesiveness of a high performing team, should have been
anticipated by the project manager. The project manager should have anticipated these
secondary risks and developed a risk response during project planning to address them.
- **D Established sufficient management reserves**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the loss of a project team member had been identified
as a risk during project planning with the development of a planned risk response. Thus,
this risk was a known rather than unknown risk. Management reserves are set aside to
address unknown risks. Even if management reserves were insufficient, according to the
scenario, the risk has been addressed as planned implying contingency reserves were used
without the need to tap into management reserves.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 439, 448, 455, 457

Question 133 of 200
Question ID: 612798
Your project team functions as a well-organized unit. The team members are interdependent and
work through issues smoothly and effectively.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Provide clear direction on the project objectives and the behavior expected from the team**
members
- **B Help the team to get through their struggle by ensuring they listen to each other and understand**
their differences
- **C Ensure the team resolves conflicts quickly and continues to work collaboratively and step in only**
when needed
- **D Serve as a gateway between the project team and the stakeholders and delegate decision making**
to the team members
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What do high-performing teams need from the project manager the most?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question is in reference to the Tuckman ladder, which is one of the models used to describe
team development. This model includes five stages of development that teams may go through

---

including forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning. The question suggests that
the project team had reached the performing stage of team development. Teams that reach the
performing stage function as a well-organized unit, and the team members are interdependent
and work through issues smoothly and effectively. This makes the life of project managers
relatively easy and requires from them to mostly serve as a gateway between the project team
and the stakeholders and delegate decision making to the team members.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Provide clear direction on the project objectives and the behavior expected from the team**
members
Incorrect. This answer choice describes the role of the project manager when the team is in
the forming stage of their development. During the forming stage, the project team
members meet and learn about the project and their formal roles and responsibilities. The
project manager should provide clear direction on the project objectives and the behavior
expected from the team members.
- **B Help the team to get through their struggle by ensuring they listen to each other and**
understand their differences
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the role of the project manager when the team is
in the storming stage of team development. During this phase, the team begins to address
the project work, technical decision, and the project management approach. If the team
members are not collaborative or open to differing ideas and perspectives, the environment
can become counterproductive. The team needs help from the project manager to get
through their struggle, listen to each other, and understand their differences.
- **C Ensure the team resolves conflicts quickly and continues to work collaboratively and step**
in only when needed
Incorrect. This answer choice describes the role of the project manager when the team is in
the norming stage of their development. During the norming stage, the team members begin
to work together and adjust their work habits and behaviors to support the team. The team
members begin to trust each other. In this phase, the best course of action for the project
manager is to ensure the team resolves conflicts quickly and continues to work
collaboratively. The project manager will step in only when needed.
- **D Serve as a gateway between the project team and the stakeholders and delegate decision**
making to the team members
Correct. This answer choice describes the role of the project manager when the team
reaches its performing stage when they function as a well-organized unit, and the team

---

members are interdependent and work through issues smoothly and effectively. This is the
ideal stage of team development that requires from the project manager to be a gateway
between the project team and the stakeholders and delegate decision making to the team
members.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 338; see
also https://www.projectmanagement.com/blog-post/15192/The-Five-Stages-of-Team-Developm
ent-and-the-Role-of-the-Project-Manager

Question 134 of 200
Question ID: 613789
As a project manager for a small university, you are currently in the process of selecting a vendor
to develop a textbook and other training materials for a new course. Several vendors are
interested in bidding on the contract. During a bidder conference, one of the prospective
suppliers asks about ownership of the intellectual property that will be created from the project.
Which project document should have this information at this stage of the project?
Top of Form
- **A Seller proposals**
- **B Requirements documentation**
- **C Source selection criteria**
- **D Procurement contract**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where can information on nontechnical requirements be found?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The requirements documentation may include technical and nontechnical requirements that the
seller is required to satisfy. Nontechnical requirements include requirements with contractual and
legal implications including intellectual property rights among others. The question implies that
the project manager is carrying out the Conduct Procurements process. Information on

---

ownership of the intellectual property can be included in the requirements documentation which
is an input to the Conduct Procurements process or the procurement contracts which are an
output from the process. Based on the scenario described, a bidder conference takes place;
therefore, it is reasonable to assume that no contracts have been awarded yet. This means that at
this stage of the project, of the available options, the requirements documentation is the best
place to find information on intellectual property rights.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Seller proposals**
Incorrect. The question indicates that a bidder conference is underway. A bidder
conference is conducted before proposal submittal. Therefore, this answer choice can be
eliminated.
- **B Requirements documentation**
Correct. Intellectual property rights are included among other nontechnical requirements
in the requirements documentation.
- **C Source selection criteria**
Incorrect. Source selection criteria describe how bidder proposals will be evaluated. The
source selection criteria do not provide information on intellectual property rights.
- **D Procurement contract**
Incorrect. The terms and conditions of the contract may contain information on the
ownership of intellectual property. However, the question states that the selection process is
currently being performed. Therefore, a contract has yet to be created to be used as a
source for this information.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 485

Question 135 of 200
Question ID: 651349
To fulfill project requirements, the performing organization must partner with an outside firm.
The project manager revises the stakeholder register to reflect the new arrangement and marks
the partner as downward in the classification under the directions of influence.
What does that indicate?
Top of Form
- **A The project manager and partner can share resources and information.**
- **B The partner can influence the project with their specialized knowledge in a temporary capacity.**
- **C The project manager can hold the partner in low esteem.**
- **D The partner can influence the project manager to make decisions and acquire additional**
resources.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

View the direction of influence from the perspective of the project.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

When identifying stakeholders on a project, a project manager can evaluate the stakeholders and
their needs, expectations, involvement, impact, and many other aspects, including influence.
'Directions of influence' is an example of a data representation technique that can be used as part
of the Identify Stakeholders, which is the process described in the scenario. Classifying the

---

direction of a stakeholder's influence in relation to the project provides the project manager a
conceptual understanding of how that stakeholder could shape or sway the project and the project
team. Downward direction can refer to the team or to specialists that contribute knowledge or
skills in a temporary capacity such as the partner described in the question. By classifying the
partner as downward, the project manager indicates that the inclusion of the partner within the
bounds of the performing organization enables the partner to influence from their downward
point of reference the larger project and project organization. Apart from downward, other
directions of influence, includes upward, sideward, and outward.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project manager and partner can share resources and information.**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents sideward influence, which applies to peers of the
project manager.
- **B The partner can influence the project with their specialized knowledge in a temporary**
capacity.
Correct. The classification of various directions of influence is from the perspective of the
project. Since the partners are considered part of the composition of the project, they are
below or under the project umbrella; hence a downward influencer.
- **C The project manager can hold the partner in low esteem.**
Incorrect. The direction of influence is about the stakeholder's influence on the project
work, not about a stakeholder's respectability or decency, so it is not the case that the
project manager would have little respect for partner classified as a downward influencer.
- **D The partner can influence the project manager to make decisions and acquire additional**
resources.
Incorrect. Partners may have an influence on the project manager, but downward influence
classification does not pertain to the partner's ability to sway the project manager's
decisions and acquisitions.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 513

Question 136 of 200
Question ID: 613654
You are beginning to develop a project schedule for the construction of a new pizza vending
machine. When you reach the activity labeled as 6.5.3, you are unsure if a refrigeration specialist
is needed for the installation of the cooling mechanism for the pizza dough.
What project document would you reference in order to get information on the resources
required for installing the cooling mechanism?
Top of Form
- **A Resource calendar**
- **B Resource management plan**
- **C Activity attributes**
- **D Procurement management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document includes details of project activities?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Activity attributes is a project document containing the resource requirements for a particular
activity. The activity attributes for activity 6.5.3 would indicate what credentials, if any, are
required to install the cooling mechanism. The resource requirements project document would

---

also be a good answer, but since resource requirements are not provided as a choice, "activity
attributes" is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource calendar**
Incorrect. The resource calendar is a project document that provides information on
resource availability, but not resource assignments.
- **B Resource management plan**
Incorrect. The resource management plan is not a project document. It is a component of
the project management plan that outlines the approach to acquiring, allocating,
monitoring, and controlling resources. While the plan may have some information about
the project roles and responsibilities, it does not specify resources down to the activity level.
- **C Activity attributes**
Correct. Activity attributes is a project document that expands the description of the activity
by identifying many aspects of the activity, including resource requirements, predecessor
and successor activities, logical relationships, lead and lags, etc.
- **D Procurement management plan**
Incorrect. Although a refrigeration specialist may be an outside resource acquired as part
of procurement management, the procurement management plan would not indicate
resource assignments.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 186

Question 137 of 200
Question ID: 613538
You are executing an IT infrastructure project which requires a team with a variety of complex
skillsets. Since many of the team members do not possess all of the skills required, you have
spent a lot of time and money to get the team trained. However, as the training unfolds, your
team reports that the training they are receiving is not a good match for the real needs of the
project.
How can you prevent this for future projects?
Top of Form
- **A Request additional training funds**
- **B Perform updates to employee development plan records**
- **C Rewrite the project's training and evaluation documentation**
- **D Update training requirements in the company's learning and development system**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer retains the information in the organization's database to be referred to for future
projects?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario, you are carrying out the Develop Team process. The source of the
problem is that the training requirements were not correctly specified, resulting in wasted time

---

and money. The immediate fix may require additional training with the associated loss of time
and funds. But, in order to prevent the same issue from happening in the future, you need to
revise the training requirements which are considered organizational process assets and are
updated as an output of the Develop Team process.
Note: It is likely that you will also want to add an entry in the lessons learned register; however,
this option is not provided among the answer choices.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Request additional training funds**
Incorrect. Although additional training funds may be needed to meet the needs of the
current project, this will not help correct the issue for future projects.
- **B Perform updates to employee development plan records**
Incorrect. Performing updates to employee development plan records is strongly
recommended in order to capture team members' development progress. However, doing so
will not necessarily help future projects avoid the same issue.
- **C Rewrite the project's training and evaluation documentation**
Incorrect. Any changes to the training and evaluation documentation of the current project
will not necessarily help to prevent the training requirements mismatch from reoccurring in
future projects.
- **D Update training requirements in the company's learning and development system**
Correct. Training requirements can be documented by position, role, project type, or a
variety of useful parameters. By updating requirements in the corporate system, you make
the correct set available to future projects.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 344

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 138 of 200
Question ID: 651406
According to the communications management plan, the project should use a dashboard to
communicate information to stakeholders. Some team members are struggling to keep their
project data current.
What is the best action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Encourage team members to enter any information whenever they can**
- **B Offer help to those team members who are struggling to report on time**
- **C Have the team focus on their work and report the status on their behalf**
- **D Reduce or adjust the format of those not able to keep their data current**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How does a project manager ensure proper communications?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Manage Communications is the process of ensuring timely and appropriate collection, creation,
storage, distribution, retrieval, monitoring, and disposal of project information. The question
states that according to the project communications plan the project status and other information
should be communicated on a project dashboard for all stakeholders to view. The data on the
dashboard needs to be current enough to be relevant and valuable to stakeholders. Some team

---

members are trying to do this but are having trouble. The project manager can lead assistance to
help the team with their communications. This may be in many forms. If the assistance or
removal of barriers helps, then changes might be needed. But it also starts with understanding the
issues, the root causes, and seeking solutions.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Encourage team members to enter any information whenever they can**
Incorrect. Incomplete and inconsistent data risks incorrect interpretations of project status
and health. Misleading data may cause inappropriate responses and actions.
- **B Offer help to those team members who are struggling to report on time**
Correct. A project manager needs to manage the project communications effectively. That
may mean removing obstacles or assisting by some other method. Offering help to those in
need is the best course of action among the choices given.
- **C Have the team focus on their work and report the status on their behalf**
Incorrect. Completing project work is very important, but so is following thru with the
project communications plans. Without proper communications, the project risks failures
and unpleasant surprises - possibly at the point beyond repair. Helping someone is not the
same as doing the work for them.
- **D Reduce or adjust the format of those not able to keep their data current**
Incorrect. Allowing some of the project team members to input less or in a different format
that others on the team may result in inaccurate data, breakdowns of communications, and
potentially create damaging team dynamics.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 379-381

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 139 of 200
Question ID: 651399
The project manager and the team decide that the project will be divided into five-week
iterations with two weeks in between for retrospectives and iteration planning.
Where should this approach be documented?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule management plan**
- **B Agile Practice Guide**
- **C Schedule network diagrams**
- **D Project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the plan?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

How the project is to manage and lay out its schedule is part of what is included in the schedule
management plan. The Plan Schedule Management process pulls together and determines how
the project is to manage the time and scheduling of a project. That schedule management plan
can contain many components dependent on the project, the needs of the project, and the extent
of documentation and thoroughness of the project and the project organization. In this scenario,
the inclusion of the timeboxing format of the iterations would definitely be involved. Projects

---

managed in an agile methodology aim to retain a consistent and repeatable iteration pattern.
Those decisions and other relevant information are documented in the schedule management
plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule management plan**
Correct. The schedule management plan documents the arrangement and desired designs of
the schedules to be used in a project. This includes the timeboxed segments agreed on by
the agile team.
- **B Agile Practice Guide**
Incorrect. The Agile Practice Guide is a publication of the Project Management Institute
(PMI)®. The Agile Practice Guide can be a source of reference to learn more about agile
scheduling best practices; however, it is not the location of the agile schedule plans of a
project.
- **C Schedule network diagrams**
Incorrect. Schedule network diagrams are visual representations of schedule activities and
their relationships. These diagrams are not the documented source of how the schedule is to
be managed.
- **D Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter provides high-level information about the project, its
objectives, and other relevant information. The charter does not detail the scheduling
structure and design of a project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 181-182

Question 140 of 200
Question ID: 610021
You are currently in the process of determining, documenting, and managing stakeholder needs
and requirements to meet project objectives. A project stakeholder has suggested that it would be
helpful to have a visual depiction showing how people and other systems will interact with the
new payroll system. You like the idea and want to address it.
What is the best way to implement the stakeholder’s suggestion?
Top of Form
- **A Develop a context diagram**
- **B Design an affinity diagram**
- **C Create a fishbone diagram**
- **D Build a matrix diagram**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which diagram might be used during the Collect Requirements process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is performing the Collect Requirements process,
which is the process of determining, documenting, and managing stakeholder needs and
requirements to meet project objectives. A context diagram is one of the tools and techniques
that might be used during the Collect Requirements process. A context diagram is a visual

---

depiction of the product scope showing a business system (process, equipment, computer system,
etc.), and how people and other systems (actors) interact with it. Of the available choices,
developing the context diagram is the best way to implement the stakeholder’s suggestion.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Develop a context diagram**
Correct. A context diagram is a visual depiction of the product scope showing a business
system (process, equipment, computer system, etc.), and how people and other systems
(actors) interact with it. Of the choices provided, developing the context diagram is the best
way to address the stakeholder’s request.
- **B Design an affinity diagram**
Incorrect. An affinity diagram is a technique that allows large numbers of ideas to be
classified into groups for review and analysis. The question describes a diagram which
depicts how people and systems will interact with the product scope rather than a
classification technique.
- **C Create a fishbone diagram**
Incorrect. A fishbone diagram is a cause and effect diagram that helps trace an undesirable
effect back to its root cause. The scenario does not describe an undesirable effect that
should be analyzed, making this answer choice incorrect.
- **D Build a matrix diagram**
Incorrect. A matrix diagram is a quality management and control tool used to perform data
analysis within the organizational structure created in the matrix. The question implies that
the Collect Requirements process is being performed rather than a quality management
process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 146

Question 141 of 200
Question ID: 651353
The updated version of the product is to be at the customer's location by the end of the week, but
the deliverable, despite the team's best efforts will not be complete by then. The deployment
team who is supposed to install the product at the customer site is under a lot of stress to meet the
deadline and will be furious that the update will not be there on time.
What is the project manager's best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Wait until the deadline hoping the team eventually makes it**
- **B Send the status report to the customer**
- **C Make the phone call to the customer to inform them of the delay**
- **D Cancel the installation at the customer site**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is in the best interest of the customer?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Managing and monitoring the communications between project stakeholders, including the
employees at the customer site, must benefit the project and its stakeholders. Withholding
information that can be useful to stakeholders is a disservice. Project reporting is part of the tools
and techniques of the Manage Communications process implied by the scenario. To

---

communicate effectively, project managers have to employ their interpersonal and team skills,
which are also among the tools and techniques of this process. In the scenario described, the
project team has determined that they cannot meet the deadline, despite their best efforts. This
inevitable outcome must be communicated to the customer, even if the conversation is
uncomfortable. No communication or late communication would cause more damage.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Wait until the deadline hoping the team eventually makes it**
Incorrect. Knowingly holding back information from the customer in hopes that the
situation changes is not productive or helpful. The project team has no solutions and
expects to miss the deadline. The customer needs to be informed.
- **B Send the status report to the customer**
Incorrect. Sending reports or other communications to customers without context and
additional information risks the message not being heard or understood.
- **C Make the phone call to the customer to inform them of the delay**
Correct. Communicating the status and the details to all affected stakeholders is more
important than worrying about disappointing them. The customer needs to know this
information to make accommodations and plan accordingly.
- **D Cancel the installation at the customer site**
Incorrect. While canceling (or at least postponing) the installation at the customer site
seems unavoidable, merely taking this action without informing the customer is unlikely to
be the best course of action in this situation.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 385-386

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 142 of 200
Question ID: 651390
- **A key stakeholder has been resistant to the project's objectives, and the support of this**
stakeholder is vital to the success of the project. The project manager has employed various
engagement strategies which have been ineffective and needs to determine the underlying reason
that stakeholder engagement is not having the planned effect.
What should the project manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Develop a stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
- **B Conduct data analysis**
- **C Submit a change request to update the stakeholder engagement plan**
- **D Perform an alternative analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Root cause analysis can be used to determine the basic underlying reason that stakeholder
engagement is not having the planned effect.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests that the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process has identified a
variance in the current and desired engagement level of a key stakeholder. The question asks
about root cause analysis which is a data analysis technique that may be useful in performing the

---

Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process. As it applies to this process, root cause analysis can
be used to determine the basic underlying reason that stakeholder engagement is not having the
planned effect. Thus, the project manager should perform a root cause analysis in this scenario.
What makes this question challenging is that root cause analysis is not listed as an answer
choice. There will likely be instances on the actual PMP exam where the obvious answer is not
available, and the best option of the available responses must be selected. In this case, root cause
analysis is a form of data analysis. Therefore, among the available choices, conducting a data
analysis is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Develop a stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
Incorrect. A stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is a data representation technique
that compares current and desired stakeholder engagement levels. However, the question
indicates that the key stakeholder's current engagement level is resistant and the desired
engagement level is supportive. Therefore, a determination of the current and desired
engagement levels for this stakeholder has already been determined.
- **B Conduct data analysis**
Correct. As it applies to the Monitor Stakeholder Engagement process, root cause analysis
can be used to determine the basic underlying reason that stakeholder engagement is not
having the planned effect. Root cause analysis is an example of a data analysis technique.
- **C Submit a change request to update the stakeholder engagement plan**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement plan may or may not need to be updated in this
scenario. The project manager should first seek to understand why the existing stakeholder
engagement plan is not having the desired effect in order to determine what changes need
to be made.
- **D Perform an alternative analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis can be used to evaluate options to respond to variances in
the desired results of stakeholder engagement. However, the question states that the project
manager needs to determine the underlying reason that stakeholder engagement is not
having the planned effect, which describes root cause analysis rather than alternative
analysis. Additionally, the root cause of the variance should be understood before
identifying options to address the gap.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 533
Bottom of Form

Question 143 of 200
Question ID: 612617
You are a project manager for an engineering services company, in the process of bidding to
work on a solar energy project for a utility company.
What is the first thing you should do to position your company as the best fit for the project?
Top of Form
- **A Attend the bid conference to learn all you need to know about the utility company's**
requirements.
- **B Request an independent cost estimate to include in your seller response.**
- **C Look for the selection method in the procurement documents of the utility company's bid**
package.
- **D Re-use a proposal that won selection by a telecommunications company.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In this scenario, you are the seller. Think about how you may have heard that the buyer needs
your services.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

When being faced with procurement-related questions on the PMP exam, a prospective PMP
aspirant has first to determine what side of the procurement the scenario is talking about. While
the majority of procurement-related questions on the exam describe the situation from a buyer's

---

point of view, some questions are worded from the seller's perspective. This question is an
example of the latter: you are the seller (or a bidder, a vendor). Therefore, some of the answer
choices can be eliminated as they refer to processes, inputs, outputs, tools or techniques that are
buyer-related.
As it pertains to the scenario described, it is a good practice for buyers to include their selected
evaluation method in the procurement documents, so bidders know how they will be evaluated.
Commonly used selection methods include least cost, qualifications only, quality-based/highest
technical proposal score, quality and cost-based, sole source, or fixed budget. To position your
company as the best fit for the project, it is essential for you to understand the requirements and
selection criteria that you need to meet as a seller. Therefore, of the choices provided, looking for
the selection method in the procurement documents of the utility company's bid package is the
best answer to the question asked.
Note, the complete source selection criteria is not always provided by the buyer to the seller.
These criteria are often internal for the buying organization. However, some subset of the criteria
can be exposed to the prospective sellers to provide them with a better understanding of what the
buyer is looking for besides the technical details of the solution.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Attend the bid conference to learn all you need to know about the utility company's**
requirements.
Incorrect. Without first thoroughly reading the bid package, you would not be prepared to
ask useful questions or even assessing whether your company meets the minimum
requirements.
- **B Request an independent cost estimate to include in your seller response.**
Incorrect. Independent cost estimates are typically developed by the buying organization,
while in the scenario described you are the seller.
- **C Look for the selection method in the procurement documents of the utility company's bid**
package.
Correct. The bid package from the buyer should provide you as a seller all the requirements
and selection criteria that you need to meet.
- **D Re-use a proposal that won selection by a telecommunications company.**
Incorrect. If your project management office does not provide a bid or proposal template,
an existing proposal may be used as a basis, but you must be careful not to break any
non-disclosure or intellectual property agreements with the previous company. Then again,

---

a proposal for a telecommunications project may not be relevant to the solar energy
project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 473-474, 478, 485
Bottom of Form

Question 144 of 200
Question ID: 651347
To utilize a few employees who are not assigned to any projects this month, the functional
manager can authorize a project specifically for them. There are two project ideas that have been
vetted. One is an IT project to implement a new software tool. Another is a charity project for the
community. Alas, there is only enough budget for one of the projects.
How should the functional manager approach the project chartering?
Top of Form
- **A Evaluate the business value of each of the projects to determine which one brings more value to**
the company
- **B Charter the IT project of the new software tool implementation since it is likely to provide a**
long-term tangible benefit
- **C Charter the charity project for the community since it is likely to have a positive, long-lasting,**
intangible, public benefit
- **D Charter both projects with a reduced scope that can be covered by the available budget to gain a**
little value from each
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What can be gained by the projects under consideration?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**


---

The question states that the functional manager can only sponsor and charter one project at this
point. The functional manager then must select a project that makes the most sense for the
functional area and the company. What is best is a factor of many things. In this scenario, since
the project selection method is not provided, business value is the deciding factor. Business value
is the net quantifiable benefit derived from a business endeavor. The benefit may be tangible,
intangible, or both. Business value is considered the return, in the form of elements such as time,
money, goods, or intangibles in return for something exchanged. As such, factoring in the value
to be gained or lost by chartering a project is the most viable variable for the functional manager
to consider.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Evaluate the business value of each of the projects to determine which one brings more**
value to the company
Correct. Evaluating the business value and the return on investment (ROI) are metrics to
assist a sponsor in selecting a project. The two proposed projects in this scenario are
focused more on business value than ROI. Therefore, the business value should be used in
the project selection approach.
- **B Charter the IT project of the new software tool implementation since it is likely to provide**
a long-term tangible benefit
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if the IT project
would provide a long-term tangible benefit. The scenario does not provide project selection
criteria. Therefore, selecting one project over another, in this case, cannot be made solely
based on one aspect such as tangible benefit.
- **C Charter the charity project for the community since it is likely to have a positive,**
long-lasting, intangible, public benefit
Incorrect. The scenario does not provide enough information to determine if the charity
project would provide a positive, long-lasting, intangible, public benefit. The scenario does
not provide project selection criteria either. Therefore, selecting one project over another,
in this case, cannot be made solely based on one aspect such as intangible benefit.
- **D Charter both projects with a reduced scope that can be covered by the available budget to**
gain a little value from each
Incorrect. Reducing the scope of the projects may negate the positive outcomes of the
projects. According to the scenario, the projects have been already vetted with their

---

original scope (likely high-level scope). Therefore, additional vetting should be conducted
before the decision of chartering both projects with a reduced scope can be made.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 7
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 145 of 200
Question ID: 613188
- **A project manager for a software development project has collected the work performance data**
and used the requirements documentation and requirements traceability matrix to generate the
work performance information regarding variances in the project work compared to the baseline.
What process is the project manager performing?
Top of Form
- **A Validate Scope**
- **B Control Scope**
- **C Manage Quality**
- **D Direct and Manage Project Work**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which process requires work performance data as inputs and produces work performance
information as outputs after performing variance analysis?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

To answer this question correctly, it is important to understand how work performance data is
transformed into work performance information. Work performance data is produced as a result
of project execution. The work performance data can then be analyzed during various controlling
processes to produce work performance information (see the image below). Work performance

---

information is only produced as an output during the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group.
In this scenario, the question suggests that a variance analysis has been performed using work
performance data in order to produce work performance information. Thus, it can be concluded
that the process underway is part of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group, and the two
answer choices representing executing processes can be eliminated.
Both the Validate Scope and Control Scope processes produce work performance information as
an output. However, only the Control Scope process uses variance analysis to produce work
performance information regarding variances in the project work compared to the scope baseline.
Therefore, of the available choices, the project manager must be executing the Control Scope
process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Validate Scope**
Incorrect. The Validate Scope process does produce work performance information as an
output. The work performance information that is created during this process includes
information such as which deliverables have been accepted and which have not been
accepted and the reasons why. The work performance information derived from the
Validate Scope process would not include information on variances from the scope
baseline.
- **B Control Scope**
Correct. The Control Scope process uses variance analysis to produce work performance
information regarding variances in the project work compared to the scope baseline.
- **C Manage Quality**
Incorrect. The Manage Quality process is part of the Executing Process Group. Work
performance information is only generated as an output of the monitoring and controlling
processes.
- **D Direct and Manage Project Work**
Incorrect. The Direct and Manage Project Work process is part of the Executing Process
Group. Work performance information is not generated by the processes of that group.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 26-27, 169-170
Bottom of Form

Question 146 of 200
Question ID: 613784
- **A company stores all of its documentation on the corporate computer network. Each project is**
assigned a directory with folders. A team member has been tasked to send the request for
proposal (RFP), source selection criteria, and procurement statement of work (SOW) to potential
sellers.
Which folder from the project directory should the team member access to find these documents?
Top of Form
- **A Bid documents**
- **B Requirements documentation**
- **C Procurement documentation**
- **D Test and evaluation documents**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where can the bid documents, procurement statement of work, source selection criteria, and
independent cost estimates be found?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Conduct Procurements process is underway. Procurement
documentation provides a written record used in reaching the legal agreement and can include
bid documents, procurement statement of work, independent cost estimates, and the source

---

selection criteria. Of the available options, only the procurement documentation contains all of
the elements specified by the question.
Note, source selection criteria may or may not be sent to prospective sellers. This would
typically depend on the performing organization's policies. Sometimes, only part of the source
selection criteria is sent to the prospective sellers while some criteria are kept confidential for
internal use of the performing organization.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Bid documents**
Incorrect. Bid documents such as the request for proposal (RFP), request for information
(RFI), and request for quotation (RFQ) are typically sent by the procuring organization to
prospective sellers so they can develop a bid response. Bid documents, however, do not
include source selection criteria, making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **B Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the
business need for the project. The procurement statement of work and bid documents are
not found in the requirements documentation.
- **C Procurement documentation**
Correct. Procurement documentation includes the bid documents, procurement statement of
work, independent cost estimates, and source selection criteria.
- **D Test and evaluation documents**
Incorrect. Test and evaluation documents are project documents that describe the activities
used to determine if the product meets the quality objectives stated in the quality
management plan. The RFP, source selection criteria, and the procurement SOW are not
among the test and evaluation documents.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 485

Question 147 of 200
Question ID: 613674
You are planning a project to design and manufacture a new style of personal watercraft. The
product will be developed and produced in-house as the company has the warehouse space and
production facilities available to support the project. As you prepare the project budget, you need
to know whether or not to include prorated rent, utilities, and other such costs.
Where is the best place to find this information?
Top of Form
- **A Basis of estimates**
- **B Agreements**
- **C Project funding requirements**
- **D Cost baseline**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which input of the Determine Budget process includes a determination on whether or not
indirect costs will be included in the project budget?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Determine Budget process is being carried out. Inputs into the
Determine Budget process include project documents such as the basis of estimates. Rent and
utilities as described in the question are examples of indirect costs. Supporting detail for cost

---

estimates in the basis of estimates should specify any basic assumptions dealing with the
inclusion or exclusion of indirect or other costs in the project budget. Therefore, the basis of
estimates is the best source to obtain a determination on the inclusion of rent and utilities.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Basis of estimates**
Correct. Rent and utilities are examples of indirect costs. Supporting detail for cost
estimates in the bases of estimates should specify any basic assumptions dealing with the
inclusion or exclusion of indirect or other costs in the project budget.
- **B Agreements**
Incorrect. Agreements contain information relevant to the Determine Budget process
including costs associated with products and services that will be purchased. Rent and
utilities represent indirect costs which are not covered by agreements for the project.
- **C Project funding requirements**
Incorrect. Project funding requirements are a forecast of project costs to be paid that are
derived from the cost baseline. However, the project funding requirements do not have
information on whether indirect costs such as rent and utilities are to be included in the
project budget.
- **D Cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline is the approved version of the time-phased project budget. The
determination of whether or not rent and utilities are to be included in the project budget is
not available from the cost baseline.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 250

Question 148 of 200
Question ID: 612166
You are about to start the development of the assumption log for the project you are leading.
What should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Examine the project management plan**
- **B Start the Identify Stakeholders process**
- **C Review the project scope statement**
- **D Read the project business case**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The assumption log is created as an output of the Develop Project Charter process during project
initiation.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The assumption log is a project document used to record all assumptions and constraints
throughout the project life cycle. The assumption log is created as an output of the Develop
Project Charter process, as such limited information is available to create this project document.
High-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints are normally identified in the
business case before the project is initiated and will flow into the project charter. Lower-level
activity and task assumptions are generated throughout the project. The assumption log is used to

---

record all assumptions and constraints throughout the project life cycle. Therefore, of the
available options, the project business case is the best source of information to use in the
development of the assumption log.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Examine the project management plan**
Incorrect. The assumption log is created as an output of the Develop Project Charter
process during project initiation. The project management plan is not created until later in
the project as part of project planning. Therefore, the project management plan is not yet
available to provide information for inclusion in the assumption log.
- **B Start the Identify Stakeholders process**
Incorrect. The assumption log is an output of the Develop Project Charter process and not
the Identify Stakeholders process. The assumption log might be updated as the result of the
Identify Stakeholders process, but it is not created during this process.
- **C Review the project scope statement**
Incorrect. The project scope statement is developed as part of the Define Scope process,
which occurs in the Planning Process Group. The assumption log is created as an output of
the Develop Project Charter process during project initiation. Therefore, the project scope
statement is not yet available to be used as a source of information for the assumption log.
- **D Read the project business case**
Correct. High-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints are normally
identified in the business case before the project is initiated and can serve as a source of
relevant information for inclusion in the assumption log.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81
