PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 149 of 200
Question ID: 613577
During project execution, after investing in the training of your project team members, you
notice that one of them consistently exceeds expectations while performing her tasks. To have
the project benefit from the team member's skills and reduce the risk of missing defects in the
project deliverables, you have tasked the team member to handle the most advanced quality
inspections.
Where would you record the new duties of this team member?
Top of Form
- **A Resource calendar**
- **B Project team assignments**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Quality inspection report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is the best place to record individual duties?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Develop Team is the process of improving competencies, team member interaction, and the
overall team environment to enhance project performance. In the scenario, after you invest in
team training, you notice a high performer and task her with advanced responsibilities to

---

improve project performance, implying you are involved in the Develop Team process. When
team development results in changes to assignments, the changes are recorded in the project
team assignments documentation. Updates to project team assignments is among the outputs of
the Develop Team process. While there are many other places to record individual capabilities,
this question is focused on changes to assignments, making project team assignments the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource calendar**
Incorrect. Resource calendars identify the working days, shifts, weekends, hours and
holidays when resources are available. However, this document does not necessarily
include the full capabilities, roles, and responsibilities of each team member.
- **B Project team assignments**
Correct. Project team assignments record the team members and their roles and
responsibilities for the project. When team development results in new duties, the project
team assignments documentation should be updated.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is the project document that captures the result of the risk
management activities. While this document specifies risk owners and may list the name of
the team member as one of the risk owners, the risk register does not provide information
on duties assigned to the project team members.
- **D Quality inspection report**
Incorrect. 'Quality inspection report' is a made-up term. Quality reports are an output from
the Manage Quality process; they provide information on quality management issues
detected by the team. Inspections are among the tools and techniques of the Control Quality
process; they are used to examine project deliverables to determine if they conform to the
documented standards. While both documents may specify the name of the individual that
conducted the inspection or prepared the report, none of these documents specify the duties
of the team members.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 344
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 150 of 200
Question ID: 612733
- **A team member reports that the risk she is assigned as an owner has occurred and will have a**
significant negative impact on the project.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Use management reserves to cover the costs associated with the risk response plan**
- **B Reprimand the team member for being unable to keep the risk from occurring**
- **C Advise the team member to check project documents for the risk response plan**
- **D Conduct the root-cause analysis to determine why the risk has happened**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risk response plans are documented in the risk register.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario indicates that the project manager is going to conduct the Implement Risk
Responses process. Project documents are an input to this process. The risk register is a project
document that records the agreed-upon risk responses for each individual risk and the nominated
owners for each response plan. Ideally, if the risk planning has been done properly on the project,
all or most of the risks are supposed to have their corresponding responses. While there is not
enough information in the question to determine if a response has been planned for this risk, of

---

the choices provided, advising the team member to check project documents for the risk response
plan is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use management reserves to cover the costs associated with the risk response plan**
Incorrect. The action described by this answer choice is premature. First, reserve analysis
should be conducted to assess if contingency reserves allocated for the response (if one
exists) planned for this risk are sufficient to cover the cost of the response. Only if the
contingency reserves are insufficient, the issue should be discussed, and a decision made
which may or may not involve tapping into the management reserves.
- **B Reprimand the team member for being unable to keep the risk from occurring**
Incorrect. While a risk owner should work towards reducing the impact or probability of
their assigned risks, preventing risks from happening is not always possible. The project
manager should first analyze the situation and make a decision that would benefit the
project. Reprimanding the team member would not resolve the situation neither it is the
first thing to do.
- **C Advise the team member to check project documents for the risk response plan**
Correct. The risk register is a project document that provides information on the
agreed-upon risk responses for each individual risks and the nominated owner for each
response plan. If the response were planned for this risk, the risk register would have this
information.
- **D Conduct the root-cause analysis to determine why the risk has happened**
Incorrect. Conducting the root-cause analysis to determine why the risk has happened can
be among the items on the agenda of the lessons learned meeting. However, this action is
unlikely to be the first step for the project manager to take in the situation described by the
scenario where the risk may have a significant negative impact on the project. It is better to
focus on options of how to address the risk rather than what caused it.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 450
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 151 of 200
Question ID: 613043
- **A vendor on a time and materials (T&M) contract to deliver corn for testing a new ethanol**
production facility is able to acquire the contracted materials at a dramatically lower price than
expected due to a crash in the commodities market. The corn represents the single biggest
expense for the project.
What is the best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Allow the project to proceed significantly under budget**
- **B Submit a change request to update the cost baseline**
- **C Split the cost savings with the vendor**
- **D Update the work breakdown structure (WBS)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might the performing organization best use the cost savings?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where project costs will be significantly less than originally
planned. Updates to the cost baseline are typically the result of costs exceeding the established
contingency reserves. However, although not common, the cost baseline can be impacted
(positively) by significant cost savings. If the cost savings were relatively minor, then the project

---

would likely be allowed to just proceed under budget, but the question describes a situation
where the biggest single project cost has been cut dramatically. The main reason to update the
cost baseline is to free up the extra capital. By updating the cost baseline, the cost savings can be
transferred from the project to the performing organization where the funds can be used for other
projects or priorities. Having resources tied up where they are not required is a form of waste,
which can and should be eliminated. An approved change request is required to update the cost
baseline. Therefore, of the available options, submitting a change request to update the cost
baseline is the best course of action.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Allow the project to proceed significantly under budget**
Incorrect. Minor cost savings would likely be addressed by simply allowing the project to
proceed under budget. However, the question describes a situation where the single
greatest expense has been reduced dramatically. These funds should be released to the
performing organization where they can be put to better use.
- **B Submit a change request to update the cost baseline**
Correct. The project has experienced a windfall with the dramatically reduced cost of the
single greatest expense. These funds should be released to the performing organization
where they can be put to better use.
- **C Split the cost savings with the vendor**
Incorrect. This answer choice describes a cost plus incentive fee (CPIF) contract rather
than a T&M contract described in the scenario. In CPIF contracts, if the final costs are less
or greater than the original estimated costs, then both the buyer and seller share costs from
the departures based upon a prenegotiated cost-sharing formula. A T&M contract is not
likely to have a cost-sharing clause.
- **D Update the work breakdown structure (WBS)**
Incorrect. The WBS is a hierarchical decomposition of the total scope of work to be carried
out by the project team to accomplish the project objectives and create the required
deliverables. The WBS is typically updated when there is a change in work to be carried
out. In the scenario, the cost of the materials change but not the work associated with them.
Therefore, an update to the WBS is not required.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 489-490
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 152 of 200
Question ID: 651401
As part of a larger initiative involving many projects, all the activities from this and all of the
other projects have to be aligned and be carried out perfectly.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Coordinate with the program manager to ensure accurate direction**
- **B Execute the work according to the directions of the project management office (PMO)**
- **C Follow the project team around to remove anyone not performing**
- **D Submit a change request to merge the project management plans of all involved projects**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What are projects that need to be managed together?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the projects are part of a program. Programs consist of projects that are
better managed and coordinated with unified oversight than as only individuals projects.
Program management in this scenario comes about due to the various projects underway all
working on similar objectives, outcomes, and objectives. The question suggests that efforts and
deliverables from multiple projects are planned to deliver one conceive entity. Coordination and
communication between projects and between the project and the program manager are crucial

---

for the success of this major initiative. Therefore, of the choices provided, coordinating with the
program manager to ensure accurate direction is the best course of action for the project
manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Coordinate with the program manager to ensure accurate direction**
Correct. The project and other projects are part of a program based on an aligned strategic
objective. Coordinating with the program manager better ensures proper direction and
execution.
- **B Execute the work according to the directions of the project management office (PMO)**
Incorrect. It is unclear what type of the PMO (supportive, controlling, or directive) is
described in the scenario. Unless stated otherwise, the PMO is not typically intimately
involved with the project. Executing the work according to the PMO's (and not the project
manager's) directions would unlikely be the best course of action.
- **C Follow the project team around to remove anyone not performing**
Incorrect. The project manager should provide direction and support. Micromanaging and
removing team members may not be the best use of the project manager's time, could cause
unneeded stress on the team, and negatively impact the project.
- **D Submit a change request to merge the project management plans of all involved projects**
Incorrect. Each project which is a part of a larger initiative should have its own project
management plan. It is the program manager who is supposed to have the program
management plan. However, the latter is not a result of merging between the project
management plans of all project involved in the initiative.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 14

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 153 of 200
Question ID: 651418
Your organization has a dedicated procurement department. Per your request, the department
prepares the procurement documentation and, during the next week, will request bids from the
prospective vendors. You really want XYZ Incorporated to be selected.
What can you say to XYZ Incorporated?
Top of Form
- **A They should expect an invitation to bid by next week.**
- **B You need product-specific information.**
- **C You can say nothing related to the bid while the bid is being prepared.**
- **D Price is the deciding factor in vendor selection.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What action is reasonable and does not violate the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional
Conduct?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

When conducting the procurement activities on a project, it is important that you remain fair,
honest, and ethical. The PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct expects this standard of
behavior of every project manager. Procurement professionals should also conduct themselves in
a fair, honest, and ethical manner. In buyer-seller transactions, it is extremely important to ensure

---

that all parties are given equal treatment and equal footing. Providing any inside information,
regardless of how small, could be interpreted as extending an unfair advantage to one potential
vendor over the others. The bid documents are going to announce the terms and evaluation
criteria of the procurement, including the price, timing, and other details. The procurement
department will send all relevant bid documents all prospective vendors at the same time. No one
should be receiving information that others are not. The communications should follow the rules
and terms of the bidding procedures, which implies that you can say nothing related to the bid
while the bid is being prepared.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A They should expect an invitation to bid by next week.**
Incorrect. Providing inside information about the timing of the bid only to one vendor and
not informing their competitors is unethical. It gives an unfair advantage to one vendor
over the others.
- **B You need product-specific information.**
Incorrect. Requesting specific information on the vendor's products may tip them off. It
gives them an unfair advantage since they can start to prepare a potential response sooner
than their competitors.
- **C You can say nothing related to the bid while the bid is being prepared.**
Correct. Prior to a formal bid, the communication between the buyers and potential
vendors should not involve any bid-related subjects. The communications should follow the
rules and terms of the bidding procedures.
- **D Price is the deciding factor in vendor selection.**
Incorrect. Telling one vendor that price is the deciding factor without providing the same
information to other competitors gives an unfair advantage to this vendor, violates the PMI
Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct, and goes against the best project management
and procurement practices.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 482-491
Bottom of Form

Question 154 of 200
Question ID: 610045
You are managing a hotel construction project, and you have asked your project team to calculate
the current earned value metrics to determine the project performance. Your team reports back
that the project's to-complete performance index (TCPI) is 0.9 based on the budget at completion
(BAC).
Which of the following is true regarding your project's current situation as reflected by this TCPI
value?
Top of Form
- **A The project is within budget**
- **B The project is over budget**
- **C The project is behind schedule**
- **D The project is ahead of schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

TCPI is not a schedule performance measurement.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The to-complete performance index (TCPI) is a measure of the cost performance that is required
to be achieved with the remaining resources in order to meet a specified management goal,
expressed as the ratio of the cost to finish the outstanding work to the remaining budget. A TCPI

---

value equal to 1.0 means you are right on budget, and as long as you maintain the present cost
performance index (CPI), you should not exceed the project budget. A TCPI value greater than
1.0 means you need to take a stricter cost management approach or you will exceed your budget
at completion (BAC). A TCPI value less than 1.0 indicates you are within your budget and have
done an excellent job of managing project costs.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project is within budget**
Correct. A TCPI is a measure of the cost performance that is required to be achieved with
the remaining resources to meet a specified management goal, such as the BAC. It is
expressed as the ratio of the cost to finish the outstanding work to the budget available. A
TCPI of less than one indicates you are operating within your remaining budget.
- **B The project is over budget**
Incorrect. A TCPI of less than one indicates you are operating within your remaining
budget. A TCPI of more than one would indicate that you are overspending and need to
improve cost performance to finish the project within budget.
- **C The project is behind schedule**
Incorrect. A TCPI is a measure of cost performance rather than schedule performance.
- **D The project is ahead of schedule**
Incorrect. A TCPI is not a direct measure of the project's schedule performance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 266-268
Bottom of Form

Question 155 of 200
Question ID: 613749
- **A project manager is starting the Plan Risk Management process. The project sponsor is risk**
averse, and this will affect the risk management plan. In preparing this plan, the project manager
is seeking a high-level understanding of the project description and boundaries, high-level
requirements, and risks.
Where is the best place for the project manager to find this information?
Top of Form
- **A Probability and impact matrix**
- **B Risk breakdown structure (RBS)**
- **C Project charter**
- **D Statement of work (SOW)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What document is issued by the project sponsor and contains high-level information about the
project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project charter is issued by the sponsor and documents the high-level project description and
boundaries, high-level requirements, and risks. The project charter is an input to the Plan Risk

---

Management process and is the best place for the project manager to gain a high-level
understanding of the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Probability and impact matrix**
Incorrect. The probability and impact matrix is a grid for mapping the probability of
occurrence of each risk and its impact on project objectives if that risk occurs. The
probability and impact matrix does not contain a high-level project description and
boundaries, high-level requirements, and risks.
- **B Risk breakdown structure (RBS)**
Incorrect. The risk breakdown structure (RBS) is a hierarchical representation of potential
sources of risk. The RBS does not contain a high-level project description and boundaries,
high-level requirements, and risks.
- **C Project charter**
Correct. The project charter documents the high-level project description and boundaries,
high-level requirements, and risks. Additionally, the project charter is an input to the Plan
Risk Management process.
- **D Statement of work (SOW)**
Incorrect. The statement of work (SOW) is a narrative description of products, services, or
results to be delivered by the project. The SOW does not contain a high-level project
description and boundaries, high-level requirements, and risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 402

Question 156 of 200
Question ID: 613169
Due to favorable weather conditions, the heating equipment you have rented for your
construction project is no longer required. Following the resource management plan, you are
returning the equipment earlier than originally planned to realize cost savings.
What should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Use the saved funds to hold a team building activity**
- **B Update the resource management plan**
- **C Let the project sponsor know about cost savings**
- **D Update the physical resource assignments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where should physical resources that are used during the project be documented?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to
the project are available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of
resources and performing any corrective action as necessary. In this case, the actual utilization of
the heating equipment was lessened by favorable weather conditions. The physical resource
assignments represent one of the project documents that may be updated as part of the Control

---

Resources process. Documentation of the physical resource assignments records the material,
equipment, supplies, locations, and other physical resources that are used during the project. The
incorrect answer choices represent actions which should not be necessary in this case. Therefore,
of the available options, updating the physical resource assignments is what you, as the project
manager, should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use the saved funds to hold a team building activity**
Incorrect. While it is important to hold team building activities to enhance the team's social
relations and build a collaborative and cooperative working environment, the saved funds
cannot be used at will without using the procedures established for the project. Typically,
dedicated funds are allocated for such activities.
- **B Update the resource management plan**
Incorrect. The question indicates that the resource management plan is being followed by
returning the heating equipment early when it is no longer needed. Thus, it is reasonable to
assume the possibility of realizing cost savings based on favorable weather conditions was
previously captured in the resource management plan. Therefore, the resource management
plan needs to be followed, rather than updated, in this scenario.
- **C Let the project sponsor know about cost savings**
Incorrect. There is nothing wrong with sharing the good news of cost savings with the
project sponsor. However, it is unlikely that the savings in the scenario described are so
significant that they warrant to be shared with the sponsor. Additionally, of the choices
provided, there is a more important action for you to take before updating the project
sponsor.
- **D Update the physical resource assignments**
Correct. The physical resource assignments represent one of the project documents that
may be updated as part of the Control Resources process. Documentation of the physical
resource assignments records the material, equipment, supplies, locations, and other
physical resources that are used during the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 358

Question 157 of 200
Question ID: 612903
An organization has a policy that directs to use only prequalified vendors. A project manager
finds a logistics company that offers much better prices than its competitors. The project
manager wants to add the vendor to the list, but the procedure can take several months due to the
rigorous qualification process.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Add the new logistics company to the prequalified vendors list and use their services for the**
project
- **B Work with the purchasing department to add the new logistics company to the prequalified**
vendors list
- **C Select the new logistics company since their price is the best among all other prequalified vendors**
- **D Ignore the new logistics company since they are not on the prequalified vendors list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In addition to prequalified seller lists, how might the organizational process assets affect this
process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**


---

The scenario implies the Conduct Procurements process is underway. Organizational Process
Assets (OPAs) are an input to this process. The OPAs that apply to this scenario include
prequalified seller lists and established policies regarding the exclusive use of prequalified
sellers. The question states that the performing organization's policy requires the use of
prequalified vendors. The reason for prequalifying sellers is typically to check credit, delivery
history, longevity, references, and the like to reduce the purchasing organization's risk exposure.
Even though it takes a long time to get qualified, working with the purchasing department to get
the new logistics company added to the preferred seller list is the only reasonable and fair
solution that is consistent with company policy and is, therefore, of the choices given, the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Add the new logistics company to the prequalified vendors list and use their services for**
the project
Incorrect. Automatically adding the new local logistics company to the prequalified seller
list bypasses the qualification process.
- **B Work with the purchasing department to add the new logistics company to the prequalified**
vendors list
Correct. Even though it takes a long time to get qualified, going through the steps to be
added to the prequalified vendors list is the only fair solution consistent with company
policy.
- **C Select the new logistics company since their price is the best among all other prequalified**
vendors
Incorrect. The new vendor is not yet on the list. Price is only one aspect. There are many
other factors to be considered before a vendor can be added to the list of prequalified
vendors. Regardless of the price, the project manager should abide by the organizational
policy and use a vendor from the list even if their price is worse than the one offered by the
new company.
- **D Ignore the new logistics company since they are not on the prequalified vendors list**
Incorrect. The project manager has a responsibility to improve the organization. Even
though the new logistics company may not get qualified on time for the current project, they
may be added later and used in future projects. The new company should not be ignored,
but rather advised to work with the performing organization's procurement department.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 486

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 158 of 200
Question ID: 651419
The work is getting done, and the project is on track. However, the project manager does not
understand why so many team members keep requesting to be moved off the project. As far as
the project manager is concerned, all she is trying to do is to ensure that the work is being
completed as specified in the project management plan.
What might be the most likely cause?
Top of Form
- **A The project manager gives the team too much work.**
- **B The team lacks the training needed to complete project activities.**
- **C The project manager lacks emotional intelligence.**
- **D The project manager does not clearly communicate the project's objectives.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Does the project manager understand the project team?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

There can be many reasons team members wish to leave a project. But in this scenario, the trend
of people asking to leave the project over the course of the project life cycle seems to be more
than just the work or the understanding of the project objectives. The root cause may be the
project manager herself. Emotional intelligence (EI) is a range of competencies around the

---

ability to identify, assess, and manage the personal emotions of oneself and other people, as well
as the collective emotions of groups of people. As such, the project manager may not be
observing or recognizing the emotions of others and/or herself. The breakdown of relationships
and the collapse of a healthy environment may lead to higher staff turnover. Investing more in EI
may translate to less project team turnover.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project manager gives the team too much work.**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if there is too much
(or too little) work assigned to the team members.
- **B The team lacks the training needed to complete project activities.**
Incorrect. The question states that the work is getting done and the project is on track,
implying the project team is sufficiently trained to be able to complete the project activities.
- **C The project manager lacks emotional intelligence.**
Correct. Emotional intelligence would help the project manager understand relationships,
self-awareness, and other emotional components beyond just getting the project team to get
work done.
- **D The project manager does not clearly communicate the project's objectives.**
Incorrect. While communicating the project objectives well may gain greater buy-in from
the project team, the lack of that on its own is less likely to be the primary reason people
are requesting to leave the project over the project life cycle.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 310

Question 159 of 200
Question ID: 651410
The project manager is concerned that the new system planned to be delivered by the project
may not be adopted by the end users in the department due to their anti-change culture and
resistance to new initiatives as seen in the past.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Build an FAQ website and respond to every end user inquiry quickly**
- **B Have the sponsor announce the value of the new system and how everybody is to benefit from it**
- **C Meet with the end users and listen to what they have to say**
- **D Get the new system in the hands of end users as early as possible and let them see its benefits**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Does the project manager understand the stakeholders and aware of the culture?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Achieving and managing stakeholder engagement in the project can be easy in some cases,
incredibly difficult in others, and every point in between. According to the scenario, there is a
culture of hesitation and resistance to new programs and projects in the department. Based on the
past projects, the end users in the department felt disenfranchised and uninvolved. The project
manager must overcome these stakeholder engagement hurdles by encouraging more stakeholder

---

involvement and buy-in. The first step towards achieving that starts with open dialogue and
active listening. The other methods of communicating and engaging with these stakeholders can
potentially be useful, if determined appropriate, at a later time. Communication skills as well as
interpersonal and team skills are among the tools and techniques that can be used by project
managers as part of the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process implied by the scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Build an FAQ website and respond to every end user inquiry quickly**
Incorrect. Providing information is good, but the culture is resistant to change. Passive
communication is incomplete and ineffective to overcome the engagement needs of these
stakeholders.
- **B Have the sponsor announce the value of the new system and how everybody is to benefit**
from it
Incorrect. Upper-level support is good, but not enough on its own to have management
decree the virtues of the new system and expect all to use it. The project manager needs to
overcome the resistance to change.
- **C Meet with the end users and listen to what they have to say**
Correct. Engaging with stakeholders includes listening to their issues and concerns about
the project, especially when the culture is resistant to change and new programs. Better
managing their engagement this time by active listening and other techniques improves the
chances of a successful rollout.
- **D Get the new system in the hands of end users as early as possible and let them see its**
benefits
Incorrect. The end users may appreciate seeing the new system, but are not going to very
supportive of it simply because they see it. They are resistant to change which is the main
issue in the scenario described.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 527

Question 160 of 200
Question ID: 651415
The project manager and project team have worked together for many years. There is a deep
sense of community and collaboration. Everyone knows their stuff and gets better with every
project.
Which leadership style of the project manager is most effective in deepening those connections?
Top of Form
- **A Communications leadership**
- **B Servant leadership**
- **C Transformational leadership**
- **D Charismatic leadership**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How can the project manager best assist a team that already works well?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Project managers must lead and manage the project team. Dealing with people, like those on the
project team, and getting things done requires a project manager to apply various leadership
styles within a project and sometimes across projects. There is no one 'correct' way to lead a
project. Circumstances in this scenario suggest that the project manager's style to best be
associated with servant leadership. Servant leadership puts the team first and seeks to enhance

---

the connections and collaboration of the team. The project manager can serve as an encourager.
Pushing the team forward by clearing the way, removing distractions, and supporting the team
would help the team and the project to achieve the project objectives. Applying this style of
leadership then enhances the connections and community aspects of the team.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communications leadership**
Incorrect. 'Communications leadership' is a made-up term.
- **B Servant leadership**
Correct. Servant leadership is a leadership approach where the project manager serves and
supports the needs of the project team over everything else to maintain the
high-performance level of the team and achieve the project objectives.
- **C Transformational leadership**
Incorrect. Transformational leadership is a style that seeks to empower and inspire others
to follow or develop oneself via idealized attributes and behaviors. Inspirational motivation
is used as part of this leadership approach. According to the scenario, the team is already
working as a well-organized high-performing unit and does not need any further motivation
to complete the project work or deepen the relationships amongst the team members.
- **D Charismatic leadership**
Incorrect. Charismatic leadership is based on the personality of the leader and is aimed to
inspire the team and strengthen the relationships among the team members. The project
manager's charisma is not required to deepen the relationships of the team that has known
each other for a length of time.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 65, 341
Bottom of Form

Question 161 of 200
Question ID: 651397
The project sponsor is concerned about possible ethics violations between the project and
vendors.
What independent review can the sponsor order?
Top of Form
- **A Team assessment**
- **B Performance review**
- **C Monte-Carlo analysis**
- **D Procurement audit**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Remember the concern is around contracts and procurement activities of the project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the Control Procurements process should be carried out to determine if any
ethics violations between the project and vendors took place. To improve the procurement
process and proceedings, organizations seek reviews independent of the project via procurement
audits. Conducting these audits independent of the team intimately involved in the project
enables the review of the procurement activities and process without influence. The
organization's code of ethics, its legal counsel, and external legal advisory arrangements

---

including any ongoing anti-corruption initiatives can contribute to proper procurement controls.
- **A procurement audit reviews the contracts and the contracting process for completeness,**
accuracy, and effectiveness. If there are any ethical violations as the project sponsor speculates, it
is possible those will come to life during a procurement audit. The violations would unlikely
emerge from performance reviews, assessments of the project team, or a Monte-Carlo
simulation.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Team assessment**
Incorrect. Project individual and team assessments are a set of tools used by a project
manager to assess the strengths and weaknesses of the individuals on the project team and
the team as a whole or its sections. It is unlikely that such assessments would reveal
violations between the project and vendors.
- **B Performance review**
Incorrect. A performance review is an example of a data analysis technique that can be
used by many processes of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group to compare and
analyze actual work results to plans. The technique reviews the results, not the procurement
process.
- **C Monte-Carlo analysis**
Incorrect. The Monte-Carlo simulation analyzes the data to present statistical
representation of what could occur in a project or as a result of a project activity rather
than an insight into the procurement process or any possible ethics violations.
- **D Procurement audit**
Correct. A procurement audit is an independent, structured review of the procurement
process, contracts, and other documents. The audit looks at the effectiveness and
ineffectiveness of procurement proceedings, including identifying any questionable ethics.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 494

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 162 of 200
Question ID: 613559
- **A vendor supplies highly specialized subject matter experts for the project you are leading. The**
vendor has just informed you that a key resource essential to the development of one of the
project’s deliverables will not be available for one month due to unforeseeable circumstances
beyond the vendor's control. The contract with the vendor contains a force majeure clause.
What should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Contact corporate counsel to note the vendor is in breach of contract**
- **B Tell the vendor they need to pay damages for lost time while the resource is out**
- **C Revise the resource calendar to reflect resource availability**
- **D Inform stakeholders that the project would not be able to deliver on schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document should be updated?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The circumstances that led to the absence of the subject matter expert are likely to be considered
a force majeure. A force majeure can be described as an unforeseeable circumstance or event that
prevents a party from fulfilling a contract. Contracts typically contain a force majeure clause
which alleviates a party to the contract of their contractual obligations. Thus, it is unlikely that

---

the performing organization will have any legal recourse with the vendor for a breach of
contract. Regardless, this situation will require the project manager to update the resource
calendar to account for the unavailability of the subject matter expert. A resource calendar is a
calendar that identifies the working days and shifts upon which each specific resource is
available. The situation described by the question will likely trigger several actions to mitigate
the impact of the issue on the project. However, of the available answer choices, the only viable
response is to revise the resource calendar to reflect resource availability.
Note, while the topic of force majeure is not covered by the PMBOK® Guide, the
PMP® Examination Content Outline assumes that the prospective PMP® aspirants are familiar
with knowledge and skills associated with contract types, procurement planning, vendor
management, conflict resolution, etc. that are required to perform to the industry-wide standard
in the role of a project manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Contact corporate counsel to note the vendor is in breach of contract**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the contract with the vendor contains the force
majeure clause. The situation described in the scenario meets the definition of force
majeure, which is unforeseeable circumstances that are beyond the vendor's control.
Therefore, claiming that the vendor is in breach of contract is unlikely to be the case.
- **B Tell the vendor they need to pay damages for lost time while the resource is out**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, an unforeseeable situation which is beyond the
vendor's control is covered under a force majeure clause in the contract. Such a clause may
alleviate the vendor's liability to pay damages for lost time while the resource is out. There
is not enough information in the question to determine additional details of the contract.
Therefore, one cannot conclude that the vendor should pay damages.
- **C Revise the resource calendar to reflect resource availability**
Correct. A resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts upon
which each specific resource is available. The situation described in the scenario will
require the project manager to update the resource calendar to account for the
unavailability of the subject matter expert.
- **D Inform stakeholders that the project would not be able to deliver on schedule**
Incorrect. While it is likely that the project will be impacted by the lack of a key resource,
without analyzing the situation in detail and evaluating options, informing stakeholders
that the project would not be able to deliver on schedule is a premature action.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 491; see
also https://www.projectmanagement.com/blog-post/8555/How-Project-Managers-Can-Execute-
Force-Majeure-Clauses

Question 163 of 200
Question ID: 651358
The plan to have 80% of the 10,000 employees enrolled in the new system by the end of the
month is nowhere near target. The project team has sent multiple emails to the entire company
with the reminders to enroll.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Instruct the team to send another email stressing the importance of the deadline**
- **B Evaluate project communications and the communication strategy**
- **C Offer an incentive to managers who get 80% or greater of their employees enrolled**
- **D Submit a change request to update the communications management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is there a communication breakdown?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Monitor Communications is the process of ensuring the information needs of the project, and its
stakeholders are met. The poor results of the employees receiving and following through on the
communications indicate the needs of the project and its stakeholders are not being met. Instead
of increasing the currently ineffective communication methodologies and attempting another
communications strategy without much thought or analysis, the project manager and the project

---

team must evaluate the current communications and analyze why they are ineffective. Knowing
what is not working and why the project team can develop better communications to fulfill the
needs of the project and its stakeholders.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Instruct the team to send another email stressing the importance of the deadline**
Incorrect. The multiple emails already sent by the project team is not working. Sending
more ineffective communications does not instantly make them effective. More analysis of
why the communications are not working is more important at this juncture.
- **B Evaluate project communications and the communication strategy**
Correct. The lack of employee enrollments may be due to many reasons. The issues
presented in the scenario are likely communications related. Examining the current project
communications and strategy may help the project team get to the root cause of the issue.
- **C Offer an incentive to managers who get 80% or greater of their employees enrolled**
Incorrect. Offering an incentive to managers may be a good strategy to encourage
employee enrollment, but there is a larger issue to be a communication lapse or lack of
buy-in from employees. Resolving those issues first may be better than incentivizing
managers.
- **D Submit a change request to update the communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan describes how project communications
will be planned, structured, implemented, and monitored for effectiveness. An update to the
plan may or may not be required. However, before taking this action, the effectiveness of
the project communications should be evaluated. This will help the project team understand
if and how the plan should be updated.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 388-393

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 164 of 200
Question ID: 612902
You are planning a project to construct a luxury condominium complex that will include jacuzzi
tubs among its numerous features. Due to technical constraints, it has been decided to eliminate
the jacuzzi tubs from the final project requirements. You document the jacuzzi tubs as an explicit
scope exclusion in the project scope statement as well as update the requirements documentation
to reflect this change.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Reflect the scope exclusion in the requirements traceability matrix**
- **B Document the status of the change in the change log**
- **C Record the elimination of the jacuzzi tubs as an issue in the issue log**
- **D Capture the exclusion of the jacuzzi tubs in the exclusion register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What document helps ensure that each element of a product adds business value by linking it to
the business and project objectives?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests you are in the Define Scope process developing the scope statement for
your project. As part of this process, final project requirements are selected, and a detailed

---

description of the project and product is developed. Requirements that have been eliminated are
explicitly documented as exclusions in the project scope statement. Updates of project
documents, such as the requirements traceability matrix are among the outputs of the Define
Scope process. Since you have added the jacuzzi tubs as an exclusion in the scope statement, of
the choices available, only updates to project documents are required next. Therefore, reflecting
the scope exclusion in the requirements traceability matrix is the best answer to the question
asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reflect the scope exclusion in the requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. The requirements traceability matrix is a project document that links product
requirements from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. This document helps
ensure that each requirement adds business value by linking it to the business and project
objectives. Since the jacuzzi tubs were eliminated as a requirement, the requirements
traceability matrix would need to be updated to reflect the change in requirements
documentation.
- **B Document the status of the change in the change log**
Incorrect. The change log is a comprehensive list of changes submitted during a project
and their current status. Changes only need to be documented in the change log after the
project management plan has been approved. The scenario suggests you are in project
planning implying the project management plan is still in development.
- **C Record the elimination of the jacuzzi tubs as an issue in the issue log**
Incorrect. An issue is a problem, gap, inconsistency, or conflict that occurs unexpectedly
and requires action, so project performance is not impacted. While eliminating the jacuzzi
tubs from the project requirements may sound like an issue for a luxury condominium
complex, the issue log is created for the first time as an output of the Direct and Manage
Project Work process. According to the scenario, the project is in planning implying project
execution has not yet begun which means the issue log does not yet exist. Even if the project
was in execution, the question states that elimination of the jacuzzi tubs has been decided,
suggesting it did not occur unexpectedly.
- **D Capture the exclusion of the jacuzzi tubs in the exclusion register**
Incorrect. 'Exclusion register' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 155

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 165 of 200
Question ID: 612908
You are planning the must-have features of a new product in detail so that work can begin and
the product can be released to the market as early as possible. The future features are unknown at
the moment and will depend on what the competitors release. You will plan these features in
greater detail later on.
As you and your team create the work breakdown structure (WBS), what will you use to indicate
the future features?
Top of Form
- **A Control accounts**
- **B WBS dictionary**
- **C Work packages**
- **D Planning packages**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which WBS component is below the control account and above the work package?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The WBS is a hierarchical decomposition of the total scope of work to be carried out by the
project team to accomplish the project objectives and create the required deliverables. The
planned work is contained in work packages, the lowest level of WBS components, where work

---

can be scheduled, estimated, monitored, and controlled. In projects using rolling wave planning,
as described in the scenario, decomposition may not be possible for deliverables that will be
completed later in the project. The future features are an example of this type of deliverable. You
know there will be features added later in the project, but you are not able to decompose them
down to the level that the work can be scheduled, estimated, monitored, and controlled. In this
case, the future features will be added to the WBS as planning packages. When more information
about the future features is available, the planning packages will be decomposed into work
packages.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control accounts**
Incorrect. A control account is a management control point where scope, budget, and
schedule are integrated and compared to the earned value for performance measurement.
Each work package on the WBS is assigned to a control account. Control accounts are used
for performance measurement, not future planning and cannot be assigned to an undefined
work package, which relies on an unknown yet feature.
- **B WBS dictionary**
Incorrect. The WBS dictionary is a document that provides detailed deliverable, activity,
and scheduling information about each component in the work breakdown structure. The
WBS dictionary contains details to support the WBS, but it is not the best choice among
those provided since the details of many of the future features are still unknown.
- **C Work packages**
Incorrect. A work package is a work defined at the lowest level of the WBS for which cost
and duration are estimated and managed. Since there is not enough detail known about the
future features, they can only be planned at a high level, which does not include cost and
duration estimates.
- **D Planning packages**
Correct. A planning package is a WBS component with known work content but without
enough detail to estimate cost and duration. The future features have been planned at a
high level, but there is not enough information to determine their cost or duration.
Therefore, the future features are indicated on the WBS as planning packages, which will be
broken down into work packages when more information becomes available.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 161
Bottom of Form

Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 166 of 200
Question ID: 612866
An unexpectedly high turnover of contracted developers threatens the objectives of the project
that you are managing. To address this issue, you want to increase the rate of pay for the
developers and add a bonus for completing the project on scope and schedule. You estimate that
the management reserves will be required to cover the cost.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Use contingency reserves as necessary to cover the extra costs**
- **B Request the additional funds from the project sponsor**
- **C Issue a change request to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline**
- **D Submit a change request to increase the project budget**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Management reserves are part of the project budget but are not included in the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources assigned and allocated to
the project are available as planned, as well as monitoring the planned versus actual utilization of
resources and performing any necessary corrective action. Thus, the question implies that the
Control Resources process is being performed in this scenario. Project management plan updates,

---

including the cost baseline, are one of the outputs of the Control Resources process. Changes to
the project cost baseline may be required to reflect the way project resources are being managed.
In this case, you need to access the management reserves in order to meet the project's
objectives. The management reserves are included in the project budget but are not part of the
cost baseline. A project manager only has direct control over the funds in the cost baseline. An
approved change request is required to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline.
Therefore, of the available options, your best course of action is to issue a change request to
transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline.
Note, the scenario does not provide enough information on how it was determined that the
management reserves will be required to cover the cost. Therefore, this determination should be
accepted as a fact and considered while selecting the correct answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use contingency reserves as necessary to cover the extra costs**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are allocated for identified risks. According to the
scenario, the high turnover of contracted developers was unexpected implying this risk has
not been identified during project planning, and therefore, no contingency reserves were
allocated for that issue. Using contingency reserves allocated for other risks would be
inappropriate.
- **B Request the additional funds from the project sponsor**
Incorrect. There is nothing wrong with approaching the project sponsor. However, the
project manager is first expected to use practices acceptable in such situations, for
example, submitting a change request to access the management reserves. Only if all
options have been exploited to no avail, would approaching the project sponsor make
sense.
- **C Issue a change request to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline**
Correct. In this case, access to the management reserves is necessary to meet project
objectives. The management reserves are included in the project budget but are not part of
the cost baseline. An approved change request is required to transfer the management
reserves into the cost baseline.
- **D Submit a change request to increase the project budget**
Incorrect. The management reserves are included in the project budget. Accessing the
management reserves, as described by the question, does not necessitate an increase in the
project budget.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 254-255, 358

Question 167 of 200
Question ID: 613499
You are managing an IT infrastructure development project. The project is being monitored for
several performance indicators such as the percentage of tasks completed on time, the number of
defects identified per day, and the number of change requests that have been submitted.
How will you know if your project is compliant with these indicators?
Top of Form
- **A By comparing the results to the quality management plan**
- **B By reviewing the audit report**
- **C By comparing the results to the quality metrics**
- **D By using quality analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document provides information on an acceptable range of variation?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests the project is in the Control Quality process as performance indicators are
being monitored and compared against an acceptable range of variation. The quality metrics are
developed as an output of the Plan Quality Management process and used as an input to the
Control Quality process. Quality metrics define which areas of the project will be measured and
what the acceptable range of variation will be. Therefore, to determine if the project is compliant

---

in the areas that are monitored in the scenario, the results should be compared to the quality
metrics.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A By comparing the results to the quality management plan**
Incorrect. In this scenario, the project is being monitored to determine whether the project
is meeting several performance indicators. The quality management plan describes how the
quality objectives will be achieved but does not provide acceptability data.
- **B By reviewing the audit report**
Incorrect. The goal of an audit is to evaluate whether the project is following the
organization's quality policies and procedures documented in the quality management plan.
In the scenario described, the project team is monitoring performance indicators, not
quality policies.
- **C By comparing the results to the quality metrics**
Correct. Quality metrics define which areas of a project are essential to measure as well as
what range of variation is acceptable. By comparing the indicators mentioned in the
scenario to the quality metrics, you will be able to determine if the project complies with
the metrics.
- **D By using quality analysis**
Incorrect. 'Quality analysis' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 287

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 168 of 200
Question ID: 613008
As a project manager, you are leading a century-old building renovation project, where theft of
equipment, materials, and supplies has been a problem. You have found that moving anything of
value that is portable into a single secured room of the building has significantly reduced the
losses with minimal cost.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Include the information in the lessons learned repository**
- **B Add the daily security task to the milestone schedule**
- **C Include the information in the lessons learned register**
- **D Discuss the situation with the team during the next retrospective**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document is used to record knowledge gained during a project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question describes the adoption of a best practice which has been found to be effective in
controlling project resources. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record
knowledge gained during a project so that it can be used in the current project and then entered
into the lessons learned repository at the end of the project. Although two of the incorrect answer

---

choices represent actions that should be performed, the question is asking what should be done
'next' in this scenario. When knowledge is gained during a project, the information should be
recorded in the lessons learned register to be available for the remainder of the project.
Therefore, of the available choices, including the information in the lessons learned register is
what you should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Include the information in the lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. Typically, any knowledge gained during a project is first captured in the lessons
learned register. Only at the end of the project, the information contained in the lessons
learned register is transferred to the lessons learned repository for the benefit of future
projects.
- **B Add the daily security task to the milestone schedule**
Incorrect. A milestone schedule is a type of schedule that presents significant points and
events in a project with planned dates. A daily task such as securing the equipment,
supplies, and materials is not a significant event for a project warranting inclusion in the
milestone schedule.
- **C Include the information in the lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is the project document that captures knowledge
gained during a project to be used to improve the performance of the project. Moving
valuable stuff into a secured room has significantly reduced the losses and is, therefore,
worth to be included as a technique that was effective in managing project resources.
- **D Discuss the situation with the team during the next retrospective**
Incorrect. A retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons learned. While discussing
the best practice during the next retrospective is a good idea, there is no reason to wait
until the next retrospective to document the knowledge gained. It is best to capture any
techniques in the lessons learned register as soon as they have been proven to be effective.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 358

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 169 of 200
Question ID: 651428
- **A new member joins the project team. The project manager wants to get the new member up to**
speed on how project communications are conducted.
What is the best action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Have a project team member show her the communication methods and tools being used**
- **B Provide her with a report of completed work packages and the current project status**
- **C Forward her all project communications and share with her links to the online resources**
- **D Add her name to the stakeholder register and introduce her to the project sponsor**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Does she know the communication means used by the project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

New people are added to projects at various points in the project lifecycle, especially very large
projects spanning years. Whether small or large or anywhere in between, new project team
members and other stakeholders need to be able to access and acquire the communications fitting
for their needs and their roles. To be effective and to onboard a project quickly and understand
what is going on, a new project team member needs more than past and present communications
dumped on them. They need to understand the communication methods used and expected by the

---

project. They need to comprehend the communication technologies leveraged by the project and
how to use them. These are all aspects of managing the project communications and is an
example of the Manage Communications process described in the scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Have a project team member show her the communication methods and tools being used**
Correct. To properly manage the proper access, use, and flow of project communications,
all project team members need to be aware of the project's communication methods and the
tools and technologies leveraged to assist in the communications.
- **B Provide her with a report of completed work packages and the current project status**
Incorrect. A report or presentation of the project does not fulfill the need of bringing the
new employee up to speed on the project communications. She needs to understand the
communication means, not to be communicated on the project.
- **C Forward her all project communications and share with her links to the online resources**
Incorrect. Dumping all the project communications and resources on the new employee is
not the most productive means of getting her up to speed on project communications. Some
filtering of what is sent to her and/or a demonstration of the various communication tools
used would be more productive.
- **D Add her name to the stakeholder register and introduce her to the project sponsor**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document about the stakeholders. True, she
is a project stakeholder. However, her inclusion on the list does not get her up to speed on
the project communications; nor introducing her to the sponsor helps accomplish the task.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 383

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 170 of 200
Question ID: 651352
During the project's iterations, the daily standup meetings have been held at 9 AM every day.
Three of the project team members have missed or been late to the last seven meetings because
the team members are running tests in another building at that time. These tests will most likely
continue for the rest of the iteration.
What is the project manager's best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Start the meeting once everyone is present**
- **B Cancel the meetings**
- **C Keep on holding the meetings as scheduled**
- **D Move the meeting to a set time later in the day**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who is the daily standup meeting for?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Meetings are a tool of the Monitor Communications process. As projects move through the
iterations when managed in an agile manner, daily standup meetings are the cornerstone of good
team communications. The structure of a standup meeting may vary greatly from one team or
one project to the next. What is most important is that these meetings are held at the same time

---

and place for a pre-determined cadence beneficial to the team. Whether every day or once a
week or some other timing, the meeting is designed to include as many of the project team
members to briefly meet, share updates, ask for assistance, and align efforts. If the timing of the
meeting does not work for part of the team, the project manager should seek to accommodate the
team by seeking more beneficial times. Canceling or continuously moving the meeting times
does not help the team's communication in this scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Start the meeting once everyone is present**
Incorrect. Daily standup meetings are designed to be succinct and efficient. Having others
on the team standing around waiting for others to be present is wasteful and not efficient.
- **B Cancel the meetings**
Incorrect. The daily standup meetings are of value to the project team. Based on the
information provided in the scenario, the meetings should still continue. The timing may
need adjustment to accommodate the team's needs.
- **C Keep on holding the meetings as scheduled**
Incorrect. On agile projects, daily standup meetings are the cornerstone of good team
communications. To be reliable and efficient, all team members should attend the meetings.
Holding the meetings with only some of the team members would negate the benefit and
purpose of the meeting.
- **D Move the meeting to a set time later in the day**
Correct. Daily standup meetings are for the team to collaborate and share updates. If the
standing meeting time does not meet the needs of the team, then finding a more suitable
time is the best action.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 364, 392, 95
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 171 of 200
Question ID: 651346
An organization is considering rolling out a new technology that could enhance employee
productivity and excitement. Some have warned that the new technology could be out-of-date
soon after roll out and there would be substantial costs in material and end-user training.
Management is unsure whether to green light this project.
What is the best course of action for the organization to take before making a decision?
Top of Form
- **A Validate the scope of the technology roll out to confirm that the technology increases employee**
productivity and excitement
- **B Determine if the benefits of the project implementation will be greater than the costs in material**
and end-user training
- **C Conduct a benefit analysis to validate the project's alignment with organizational strategy and**
expected business value
- **D Survey developers of the technologies under consideration to better understand all the technical**
specifications and uses
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is most important for a business to undertake a project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**


---

There are many reasons to initiate a project. New technology is one such option. Nonetheless,
what is most important is how a project aligns with business needs and strategies. Analyzing
business needs and strategies helps determine whether or not a project brings value to the
business. Other information and criteria may assist in making a more educated and
comprehensive decision, but the most important aspect to consider is the business value to be
gained or lost by initiating and completing a project, not the technology on its own.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Validate the scope of the technology roll out to confirm that the technology increases**
employee productivity and excitement
Incorrect. Validate Scope is the process that measures and validates how the project has
delivered on the scope defined in the project. There is no project yet or scope defined to be
validated. At this point, management must decide first whether or not to charter the project.
- **B Determine if the benefits of the project implementation will be greater than the costs in**
material and end-user training
Incorrect. Assessing if the benefits of the project implementation will be greater than the
costs in material and training is only one aspect of project selection. Other considerations
should be made before a project can be selected, such as the alignment of the project with
organizational strategy.
- **C Conduct a benefit analysis to validate the project's alignment with organizational strategy**
and expected business value
Correct. Initiating a project within an organization, management should determine and
validate how the project outcomes bring value to the organization and the business
strategy.
- **D Survey developers of the technologies under consideration to better understand all the**
technical specifications and uses
Incorrect. Understanding the technical specifications and uses may be valuable to learn
about the industry and technologies, but it is not the most needful of the options presented.
The decision to initiate a project should focus on the business need and less on the
technology itself.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 77-78

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 172 of 200
Question ID: 612472
- **A project manager had originally planned to use two industrial 3D printers simultaneously for a**
project but has just learned that one of them will be unavailable. The project manager adjusts the
schedule so that the components are created sequentially using one printer. Unfortunately, this
action affects the critical path and delays the planned finish date of the project.
What tool or technique has the project manager used in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Fast tracking**
- **B Resource smoothing**
- **C Crashing**
- **D Resource leveling**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A resource optimization technique in which start and finish dates are adjusted based on resource**
constraints.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Resource leveling is a resource optimization technique in which start and finish dates are
adjusted based on resource constraints with the goal of balancing the demand for the resources
with the available supply. Resource leveling can often cause the original critical path to change

---

which is what happened in the scenario described. Adjusting the schedule to accommodate the
loss of one of the 3D printers is an example of resource leveling. Therefore, of the choices
provided, it can be reasonably assumed that the project manager performed resource leveling.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Fast tracking**
Incorrect. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique in which activities normally
done in a sequence are performed in parallel for at least a portion of their duration. The
question indicates that the original plan was to use both 3D printers at the same time (in
parallel), and with the loss of one of the 3D printers, the project manager scheduled the
activities to be performed in sequence. Therefore, fast tracking is not what the project
manager used in this situation.
- **B Resource smoothing**
Incorrect. Resource smoothing is a resource optimization technique in which activities may
only be delayed within their free and total float, thus not affecting the critical path. The
question states that the critical path is affected, so resource smoothing is an incorrect
answer choice.
- **C Crashing**
Incorrect. Crashing is a technique used to shorten the schedule duration for the least
incremental cost by adding resources. Acquiring an additional 3D printer is an example of
crashing. However, the question does not indicate that any resources are being added in
this scenario.
- **D Resource leveling**
Correct. Resource leveling is a resource optimization technique in which start and finish
dates are adjusted based on resource constraints. Resource leveling can often cause the
original critical path to change. Adjusting the schedule to accommodate the loss of one of
the 3D printers is an example of resource leveling and, therefore, is the best answer to the
question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 211
