Question 173 of 200
Question ID: 651345
- **A number of projects are under consideration for the upcoming quarter. The Director of Global**
Systems strongly believes that one of the projects, a system upgrade, is needed and aligned with
the long-term business strategy.
At the executive steering committee meeting scheduled to select projects for the upcoming
quarter, what action should the Director take?
Top of Form
- **A Advocate for the project with the highest NPV**
- **B Select a project sponsor**
- **C Present the merits of the system upgrade project**
- **D Select a project manager**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How can a project get chartered?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Projects are selected for many reasons. Not all desired projects can be undertaken by an
organization. Decisions as to which projects an organization is to take on are often part of an
executive steering committee's responsibility. To get a certain project sponsored and chartered,
the Director in this scenario must present the merits and value to the business to the steering

---

committee. Upon selection and approval, the project charter for the project can be commissioned
and the project made official.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Advocate for the project with the highest NPV**
Incorrect. The scenario does not provide project selection methods used by the steering
committee. Additionally, according to the scenario, the Director strongly believes that a
system upgrade is a project to be selected. Therefore, advocating a project with the highest
NPV (unless it's the system upgrade which is not clear from the question) makes no sense.
- **B Select a project sponsor**
Incorrect. Based on the scenario, it seems that the Director or the executive steering
committee would likely be the project sponsor. Even if not, it is unclear if the Director has
the authority to select the project sponsor.
- **C Present the merits of the system upgrade project**
Correct. The Director is attempting to gain support for the system upgrade project. Making
a case for the project to the steering committee is the best action to take to achieve this
goal.
- **D Select a project manager**
Incorrect. The project has not yet even been selected. Therefore, selecting a project
manager is a premature action. Additionally, there is not enough information in the
question to determine if the Director has the authority to select project managers.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 174 of 200
Question ID: 651365
Labor costs during the winter months were far higher than expected.
What is the best action for the project manager and project team?
Top of Form
- **A Allocate additional funds to the project**
- **B Record this information in the lessons learned register**
- **C Adjust the project cost baseline**
- **D Schedule more work during the summer months**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What has the team learned?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

There is plenty that can be learned during a project. Capturing and managing those lessons that
have been learned is an important part of a project manager's, project team's, the project
organization's growth and improvement. The lessons learned register could be updated for many
reasons, such as the techniques that were or were not effective, measurement tools used,
forecasting methods, and in the case of the scenario, learning from conditions and events that
impacted the control of project costs. What is learned from the capturing and analyzing of the

---

lessons turn into actions, such as trying to schedule more activities during non-winter months,
allocating more funds, or preparing forecasts to be closer to actuals.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Allocate additional funds to the project**
Incorrect. It is the project sponsor, not the project manager or the team, who has the
authority to allocate additional funds to the project if needed. But that need is not known
fully at this point. There may not be additional work in the winter months requiring more
funds.
- **B Record this information in the lessons learned register**
Correct. Capturing, analyzing, and managing lessons learned enable continuous
improvement. Those lessons learned can be applied and/or referenced in this project, future
projects, or in other concurrent projects.
- **C Adjust the project cost baseline**
Incorrect. The cost baseline is the approved version of the project budget which can be
adjusted only through an approved change request. The cost baseline is not changed as a
result of the fact that the actual costs were higher than expected. Rather, it serves as a basis
for comparison between the planned and actual costs which is what happened in the
scenario described where cost variance has been found. The situation should be analyzed
and a decision made. Adjusting the cost baseline may or may not be needed.
- **D Schedule more work during the summer months**
Incorrect. The lesson learned may be to adjust the schedule or to plan future work to fall
more in the summer months rather than the winter months, although there is not enough
information presented to determine if this is needed, wanted, or even possible.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 259

Question 175 of 200
Question ID: 612701
An opportunity has triggered some previously approved risk responses. After the primary
responses failed to produce the desired results, you discuss fallback plans with your team. The
sponsor is concerned and is asking for the current overall risk exposure.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Consult the risk management plan**
- **B Look in the lessons learned register**
- **C Refer the sponsor to the risk register**
- **D Provide the sponsor with the risk report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risk exposure is an aggregate measure of the potential impact of all risks. Such measurement
and analysis would be an output of the Monitor Risks process.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In the scenario described, you are discussing with your team the results of implementing risk
responses, implying you are in the Monitor Risks process. The risk report can be updated as an
output of this process to provide an aggregated view of the collective impact of all identified
risks on your project schedule, budget, quality, and other project constraints, which constitutes

---

the current overall project risk exposure. The risk report may also specify the results of Monte
Carlo S-curves, tornado diagram, criticality analysis to determine the contingency reserve
required to account for risk exposure. To assist with the implementation of risk responses, this
report also describes the agreed-upon risk response strategy and the major individual project
risks with their planned responses.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Consult the risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan specifies the risk thresholds that define the acceptable
target ranges (in the project schedule and costs) that the risk responses are required to
achieve. However, this component of the project management plan is not designed to show
current aggregated risk exposure.
- **B Look in the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. Lessons learned from implementing risk responses are recorded in this project
document. However, this project document does not include information about current
project risk exposure.
- **C Refer the sponsor to the risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register records the agreed-upon risk responses for each 'individual' risk
and the nominated owners for each response plan. This project document does not show
'overall' risk exposure.
- **D Provide the sponsor with the risk report**
Correct. The risk report provides an aggregated view of the collective impact of all
identified risks on your project schedule and budget, which constitutes the current overall
project risk exposure.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 458

Question 176 of 200
Question ID: 612988
- **A project manager is leading a project to manufacture a new type of wheel for the automobile**
industry. The first lot of wheels has been created, and the project manager wants to know if the
quality objectives have been met.
What should the project manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Review the work breakdown structure**
- **B Perform a quality audit**
- **C Use the test and evaluation documents**
- **D Develop a quality report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the following can be used as checklists and detailed requirements traceability matrices?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Test and evaluation documents are created in the Manage Quality process and provide a format
with which the project team can evaluate whether quality objectives have been met. Examples of
test and evaluation documents are checklists and detailed requirements traceability matrices.
These documents are an output of the Manage Quality process and an input to the Control
Quality process where they are used to evaluate the achievement of quality objectives. According

---

to the scenario, the first lot of the wheels has been manufactured. Therefore, of the choices
provided, to evaluate if the lot is compliant with the quality specifications, the next step for the
project manager would be to use the test and evaluation documents created in the Manage
Quality process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review the work breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The work breakdown structure (WBS) is a hierarchical decomposition of the total
scope of work to be carried out by the project team to accomplish the project objectives and
create the required deliverables. The WBS does not specify quality objectives.
- **B Perform a quality audit**
Incorrect. An audit is a structured review to determine if current project activities comply
with organizational and project policies, processes, and procedures. An audit is focused on
processes rather than actual adherence of the project deliverables to quality standards.
- **C Use the test and evaluation documents**
Correct. The test and evaluation documents provide a format with which the deliverables
can be evaluated for their compliance with the quality objectives. The documents are
outputs from the Manage Quality process and are used in the Control Quality process.
- **D Develop a quality report**
Incorrect. A quality report is an output of the Manage Quality process that provides
information about quality management issues escalated by the team. The act of developing
the quality report does not necessarily mean that quality objectives have been met. Data
should be collected and compared to the predefined specifications outlined in the test and
evaluation documents.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 296, 300

Question 177 of 200
Question ID: 651350
- **A project has just been approved and formally chartered.**
What is one of the first things the assigned project manager should do?
Top of Form
- **A Start the development of the project management plan**
- **B Acquire the resources necessary to perform the project work**
- **C Inform stakeholders of the approved project charter**
- **D Perform a project assessment based on available information**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who is aware of the approved project and its purpose?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario, it can be implied that the Develop Project Charter process has just been
completed. The project charter formally authorizes the project and documents the high-level
goals and business value, as well as other key information. Communicating the final, approved
information captured in the charter to all affected stakeholders ensures a common understanding
of the objectives, expected deliverables, milestones, and the stakeholder's expected involvement.
Of the choices provided, informing stakeholders of the approved project charter is one of the first

---

things the assigned project manager should do and is, therefore, the best answer to the question
asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Start the development of the project management plan**
Incorrect. While the development of the project management plan starts soon after the
project charter gets approved, another answer choice represents an action that should be
taken before the development of the plan begins.
- **B Acquire the resources necessary to perform the project work**
Incorrect. Although some of the resources can be pre-assigned early in the project life
cycle, most of the resources are typically acquired during project execution. According to
the scenario, the project is in late initiation / early planning, therefore, acquiring the
resources at this point is unlikely to be one of the first things for the project manager to do.
- **C Inform stakeholders of the approved project charter**
Correct. As a formal, approved project charter has been issued, project stakeholders must
be informed of the objectives and other key information about the project.
- **D Perform a project assessment based on available information**
Incorrect. In the selection and chartering of the project, the assessments and evaluations
were already conducted. Additional project assessments performed by the project manager
is unnecessary at this point in the project.

Question 178 of 200
Question ID: 613675
- **A project manager is determining a cost baseline for a project to develop a new sales training**
course. As part of this process, the project manager sums up the lower-level cost estimates from
the work packages in the work breakdown structure (WBS).
What tool or technique is the project manager using in this process?
Top of Form
- **A Expert judgment**
- **B Cost aggregation**
- **C Reserve analysis**
- **D Funding limit reconciliation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique used during the Determine Budget process involves the summation of
work package cost estimates?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Determine Budget process is underway. One of the tools and
techniques used during the Determine Budget process is that of cost aggregation. Cost
aggregation is conducted by summing the lower-level cost estimates associated with the various

---

work packages for a given level within the project’s work breakdown structure (WBS). Based on
the description provided by the scenario, the project manager is performing cost aggregation.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is judgment provided based upon expertise in a relevant area.
The question describes the process of aggregating costs. Expert judgment is typically not
required to perform this procedure.
- **B Cost aggregation**
Correct. Cost aggregation is conducted by summing the lower-level cost estimates
associated with the various work packages for a given level within the project’s work
breakdown structure (WBS).
- **C Reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis is an analytical technique used to establish a reserve for the
project budget. Based on the scenario described, the project manager is not establishing a
reserve.
- **D Funding limit reconciliation**
Incorrect. Funding limit reconciliation is the process of comparing the planned expenditure
of project funds against any limits on the commitment of funds for the project. The
procedure described in the question relates to a summation of costs rather than
reconciliation.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 252

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 179 of 200
Question ID: 651348
Management has called you in as they are evaluating and laying out the expectations of an
upcoming project. They ask you if you want to be involved in the meetings since you are most
likely to be the project manager assigned to the project. You are leading another project, and your
schedule is very busy.
What is your best response?
Top of Form
- **A Accept the offer since a project manager must be involved in a project starting with the Develop**
Project Charter process
- **B Decline the offer since the involvement of a project manager in a new project does not begin until**
after the project charter is approved
- **C Accept the offer since it is beneficial for a project manager to understand the project objectives**
and other related information
- **D Decline the offer since you are leading another project, and project managers are not allowed to**
work on multiple projects concurrently
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What will help the project manager make the project a success?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**


---

The role of the project manager does not formally start until the project has been approved and
chartered. Nevertheless, it is highly advantageous for a potential project manager to be involved
as much as possible and as early as possible in the crafting and direction of the project charter.
Having the project manager collaborate with the project initiators allows the project manager to
better understand the project objectives, vision, purpose, expected outcomes, and benefits. The
best decision is for the project manager to be involved in the discussions and assist in chartering
the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Accept the offer since a project manager must be involved in a project starting with the**
Develop Project Charter process
Incorrect. While it is highly beneficial for the project manager to be involved in the project
as soon as possible, preferably when project chartering has begun, the involvement is not a
'must'. The project manager is authorized by the project charter and can, therefore, decline
the offer if the project charter is not yet approved.
- **B Decline the offer since the involvement of a project manager in a new project does not**
begin until after the project charter is approved
Incorrect. True, a project manager is formally assigned to the project after the project
charter is approved. Nevertheless, a project manager can have involvement and participate
in the direction and goals of the project while the project is still under consideration and
chartering.
- **C Accept the offer since it is beneficial for a project manager to understand the project**
objectives and other related information
Correct. Being involved early in the analyzing and collecting of project goals and
expectations enables the soon-to-be project manager insight on how decisions came about
and influence the project's direction.
- **D Decline the offer since you are leading another project, and project managers are not**
allowed to work on multiple projects concurrently
Incorrect. Project managers should be capable of handling their schedules in a way that
will allow them to allocate their time for unanticipated events. Unless specified otherwise
in the scenario, saying that project managers are not allowed to work on multiple projects
concurrently would not be accurate. While multitasking is not ideal, declining the offer
since you are leading another project and having a busy schedule does not look like a
professional response.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 77
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 180 of 200
Question ID: 613590
The various teams working on your project have gone through an extensive array of training and
development activities specified in the resource management plan to ensure optimum
performance. However, one of the teams has seen substantial turnover since the training was
completed. You realize that for this particular team, you will have to identify specific training
and coaching to align the competencies of these new team members with the rest of the teams.
What is the best approach for you to take in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Conduct team performance assessments**
- **B Repeat the training regime for the team**
- **C Create work performance reports**
- **D Review the resource management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Look for the best way to measure team shortcomings.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Team performance assessments are the output of the Develop Team process. The best way to
measure team performance is by assessment. In this case, the assessment should be given to the
high-turnover team to ensure that you can most effectively target any shortcomings. It will not be

---

useful to base your adjustments on past performance, because a substantial part of the team
consists of new members.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Conduct team performance assessments**
Correct. By conducting team evaluations, the project manager can determine the specific
training, coaching, and mentoring needs of the team members. Without this assessment, the
project manager can only guess at the needs of the team.
- **B Repeat the training regime for the team**
Incorrect. It is wasteful to repeat the entire training regime when more targeted and focused
efforts may be all that is required. Additionally, repeating training can be demotivating for
many high-performing individuals.
- **C Create work performance reports**
Incorrect. Although work performance reports can give insight into team performance for
work already conducted, they cannot identify specific needs for upcoming work where no
work performance information yet exists.
- **D Review the resource management plan**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the resource management plan has already been
reviewed. While the plan may provide guidance, it cannot identify the specific needs of the
team members, especially when these team members are new to the organization and were
not even identified at the time the resource management plan was in development.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 343, 342

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 181 of 200
Question ID: 613243
- **A project to design and develop a new prototype medical device will require several vendors to**
develop the subcomponents. As you review the responses to the RFP, you realize that all the
vendors plan to re-use your competitors' designs. This "re-use" is unacceptable for your
company.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Select a vendor based on the source selection criteria as specified by the approved project**
management plan
- **B Add the intellectual property clause to the requirements documentation and ask the vendors to**
resubmit their proposals
- **C Select a vendor based on the source selection criteria and then add the intellectual property**
clause to the contract
- **D Notify the legal department about the breach of contract and initiate alternative dispute**
resolution to settle the conflict
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The proposals were based on the assumption that the vendors would be able to re-use the design.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**


---

According to the scenario, you are reviewing the responses to the RFP, implying the project is in
the Conduct Procurements process. During this process, the requirements documentation may be
updated to incorporate requirements with contractual and legal implications including intellectual
property rights. The relevant criteria from the requirements documentation are then included in
the bid documents including the request for proposal (RFP). In this scenario, the question
suggests that the retention of intellectual property rights was not included as a requirement in the
request for proposal (RFP), and the vendors based their proposals on the assumption that they
would be able to re-use the design with competing companies. Since the proposals were based
upon an invalid assumption, it will be necessary to update the requirements documentation and
ask the vendors to revise their bids accordingly.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Select a vendor based on the source selection criteria as specified by the approved project**
management plan
Incorrect. The vendors will need to be selected based on the established source selection
criteria. However, in this scenario, it is clear that the retention of intellectual property
rights was not communicated effectively, and the vendors based their proposals on the
belief that they will be able to re-use the designs of competing companies. Proposals that
miss addressing intellectual property rights cannot be considered valid and serve as a basis
for vendor selection.
- **B Add the intellectual property clause to the requirements documentation and ask the**
vendors to resubmit their proposals
Correct. The question suggests that the retention of intellectual property rights was not
included as a requirement in the request for proposal (RFP), and the vendors based their
proposals on the assumption that they would be able to re-use the designs of competing
companies. Since the proposals are not valid, the requirements documentation should be
updated, and vendors' bids revised accordingly.
- **C Select a vendor based on the source selection criteria and then add the intellectual property**
clause to the contract
Incorrect. Although it will be necessary to include the retention of intellectual property
rights in the awarded contract, the question suggests that the vendors have based their
proposals on the assumption that they will able to re-use the designs of other companies.
Since all of the vendors have the same misunderstanding, it is clear that the retention of
intellectual property rights was not included as a requirement. Therefore, the submitted
proposals are not valid and will need to be resubmitted based on revised requirements.

---

- **D Notify the legal department about the breach of contract and initiate alternative dispute**
resolution to settle the conflict
Incorrect. The question indicates that the vendor selection process is still underway, which
means that the contracts have yet to be awarded. The contracts have yet to exist. Therefore,
there are no conflicts due to a breach of contract that need to be resolved.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 491

Question 182 of 200
Question ID: 613257
Midway into project execution, the director of marketing leaves the company and is replaced by
an external candidate. After meeting with the new stakeholder, the project manager learns that
the new director of marketing has a much greater interest in the project, and would like to be
updated on progress and project specifics with greater frequency.
With the stakeholder register updated to reflect the relevant information, what should the project
manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Review and revise the stakeholder engagement plan as necessary**
- **B Perform stakeholder analysis for the newly identified stakeholder**
- **C Update the project documents with the information for the new stakeholder**
- **D Submit a change request to update the communications management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Any modification to a component of the project management plan requires an approved change.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The communications management plan is a component of the project management plan that
describes how, when, and by whom information about the project will be administered and
disseminated. The communications management plan includes information on who will receive

---

project information, including information about their needs, requirements, and expectations.
The new director of marketing would like to be updated on progress and project specifics with
greater frequency than her predecessor. This information should be reflected in the
communication management plan. However, since the project is underway, implying the project
management plan has been approved, a change request is required for any subsidiary plan to be
modified. The incorrect answer choices either have already been completed or cannot be done
without first seeking an approved change request. Therefore, of the available options, submitting
a change request to update the communications management plan is what the project manager
should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review and revise the stakeholder engagement plan as necessary**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement plan is a component of the project management
plan that identifies the strategies and actions required to promote the productive
involvement of stakeholders in project decision making and execution. While the
stakeholder management plan should be revised in this scenario, an approved change
request is first required to modify any component of the project management plan.
- **B Perform stakeholder analysis for the newly identified stakeholder**
Incorrect. Stakeholder analysis is performed during the Identify Stakeholders process in
order to create or update the stakeholder register. However, according to the scenario, the
stakeholder register has already been updated with the relevant information about the
newly identified stakeholder.
- **C Update the project documents with the information for the new stakeholder**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document that includes the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. The stakeholder register should be
updated in this scenario, and the question indicates that this action has already been
completed.
- **D Submit a change request to update the communications management plan**
Correct. The communications management plan includes information on who will receive
project information, including information about their needs, requirements, and
expectations. The plan should be updated with the communication needs of the new
marketing director. However, first, an approved change request is required to update the
communications management plan since it is a subsidiary of the project management plan.

**Reference:**

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 183 of 200
Question ID: 620001
- **A project manager is currently managing a manufacturing process improvement project which**
will be completed in five phases. The project manager has prepared the following chart to review
the status of the project.
Based on the information provided, what is the earned value of the project?
Top of Form
- **A $7,750**
- **B $9,000**
- **C $20,000**
- **D $8,000**
Question answered incorrectly

---


**Hint:**

Earned value (EV) is the sum of the planned value of completed work.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question is asking for the current earned value (EV) of the project thus far. Earned value
(EV) is the sum of the planned value of completed work. The define and measure phases are
complete with planned values of $1,000 and $3,000 respectively. The analyze phase is 75%
complete with a planned value of $5,000, which means the EV for the analyze phase is $3,750.
Therefore, the sum of the planned values of the completed work is $1,000 + $3,000 + $3,750
which is a total EV of $7,750.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A $7,750**
Correct. The earned value (EV) is the sum of the planned value of completed work. In this
case EV = (1 x $1,000) + (1 x $3,000) + (.75 x $5,000) = $7,750
- **B $9,000**
Incorrect. $9,000 represents the total planned value for the first three phases of the project.
However, only 75% of the third phase has been completed, and not all of the planned value
of the third phase has been realized at this point in the project.
- **C $20,000**
Incorrect. The budget at completion (BAC) is the sum of the planned values for the
individual phases which equals $20,000. The question is asking for the earned value and
not the BAC.
- **D $8,000**
Incorrect. $8,000 represents the total costs that have been incurred by the project to date.
The question is asking for the earned value and not the actual cost.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 261, 267

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 184 of 200
Question ID: 612159
- **A project manager is leading a project to streamline the manufacturing process of modular**
homes. The project manager researches and discovers a set of technical guidelines that will make
the homes easier and cheaper to manufacture without compromising quality. The team
incorporates these guidelines by designing a new modular home that reduces the total number of
parts and uses more standard and multi-functional components.
This is an example of:
Top of Form
- **A Problem solving**
- **B Design for X**
- **C Change request**
- **D Data gathering**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is a set of technical guidelines that may be applied during the design of a product for the
optimization to a specific aspect of the design?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Design for X (DfX) is a set of technical guidelines that may be applied during the design of a
product for the optimization of a specific aspect of the design. In this scenario, technical

---

guidelines are being applied to design a new modular home that optimizes its manufacturability.
DfX provides the most accurate and precise definition of the technique being used in this
scenario and is, therefore, of the available choices, is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Problem solving**
Incorrect. Problem solving entails finding solutions for issues or challenges, which is
certainly an aspect of what the project manager is doing in this scenario by looking for
ways to improve the manufacturability of the product. However, another answer choice
more accurately describes the technique used in this situation.
- **B Design for X**
Correct. Design for X is a technique of the Manage Quality process whereby a person
follows certain technical guidelines that may be applied during the design of a product for
the optimization of a specific aspect of the design (in this case, manufacturability). In this
scenario, the goal is to design a home that is easily and economically manufactured. Using
the DfX, the project manager implements certain design decisions (e.g., reducing the total
number of parts) in order to accomplish this goal.
- **C Change request**
Incorrect. A change request is a formal proposal to modify a document, deliverable, or
baseline. In this scenario, however, the project manager is not requesting a change to an
existing product but rather incorporating new technical guidelines to improve
manufacturability into the design of a new product.
- **D Data gathering**
Incorrect. Data gathering, within the context of quality management as implied by the
question, generally refers to a set of tools or techniques (e.g., checklists, process analysis,
root cause analysis, alternatives analysis, etc.) used to identify underlying problems,
variances, risks, or defects and ensure that project requirements have been met. In this
scenario, however, the focus is on improving the manufacturability of the product using a
set of technical guidelines to enhance that aspect of product development - an illustration
of the Design for X technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 295

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 185 of 200
Question ID: 651411
The project manager is ready to transition the final project's deliverable and close the project.
Which of the following would ensure the smoothest transition?
Top of Form
- **A Coordination with the operations manager**
- **B Strong matrix organizational structure**
- **C Submission of a final project report**
- **D Constant communications with the project sponsor**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is the product, service, or result of the project going?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Close Project or Phase is the process of finalizing all activities for the project, phase, or contract.
One of the outputs from this process is the transitioning of the final product, service, or result to
the customer, end user, and/or operations. The question states that the project is ready to
transition its final deliverable. There is not enough information in the question to determine who
is the receiving end of this transition. However, one of the answer choices mentions an
operations manager while other answer choices do not describe a party that would have been
considered an entity receiving the final project deliverable. Therefore, it is reasonable to assume

---

that the deliverable is being transitioned into the organization's operations. Hence, of the choices
provided, working closely with the operations manager would likely increase the odds of a better
transition and project closure and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Coordination with the operations manager**
Correct. Since operations are frequently a party to which a final product, service or result
is transitioned, coordination and communication between the project team and the
operations' team(s) increases the likelihood of a smooth, successful transition.
- **B Strong matrix organizational structure**
Incorrect. Matrix, whether weak, strong, or balanced, does not ensure a smooth transition.
It is the processes, procedures, and, most importantly, human interactions, collaboration,
cooperation, and communication between the relevant parties that help ensure the
transition of the final project deliverable is being done in the best possible way.
- **C Submission of a final project report**
Incorrect. Submitting a final report occurs after the deliverables, and the project comes to a
close. The final report aims to summarize the project, its operations, and other relative
information rather than to ensure the smoothest transition.
- **D Constant communications with the project sponsor**
Incorrect. While communicating with the project sponsor is important, communications
alone (whether it's constant or irregular) would not ensure the smoothest transition of the
final project deliverable. The project manager should work closely with the entity who is
supposed to operate, maintain, and support the product after the transition.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 121-123, 127

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 186 of 200
Question ID: 612577
- **A project manager is estimating the number of work periods needed to complete individual**
project activities with estimated staff.
To complete this process, the project manager should consider all of the following factors except
for:
Top of Form
- **A Staff motivation**
- **B Number of resources**
- **C Law of diminishing returns**
- **D Political awareness**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is carrying out the Estimate Activity Durations process. Which factors
should be considered as part of this process? Note, the question is looking for an exception.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Estimating the number of work periods needed to complete individual project activities with
estimated staff is the definition of the Estimate Activity Durations process. There are many
factors to consider while carrying out this process. Some of them include staff motivation,
number of resources, the law of diminishing returns, and advances in technology. Political

---

awareness is not among these factors. Political awareness refers to the recognition of power
relationships, and the willingness to operate within these structures. Political awareness may help
the project manager to plan and manage communications, manage and monitor stakeholder
engagement, and manage project knowledge. However, among the choices provided, political
awareness is the least likely factor to be considered as part of the Estimate Activity Resources
process and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Staff motivation**
Incorrect. When estimating activity durations, the project manager should be aware of staff
motivation and consider how quickly and well a team member would perform the project
activity. A poorly motivated team member might procrastinate, take too long at a task, or
make mistakes that would affect the activity duration.
- **B Number of resources**
Incorrect. A project manager needs to understand the number of resources involved in a
project activity since this number would affect the activity duration. At times, adding more
resources helps to shorten time to complete a task. However, at some point, adding too
many resources to the activity may increase the activity duration due to additional time
spent on knowledge transfer, learning, coordination, etc.
- **C Law of diminishing returns**
Incorrect. The law of diminishing returns is a principle in economics that states that in a
production process, adding more of one factor in production (such as labor, capital,
resource, technology, or overtime), while holding all other factors constant, at some point,
will yield a lower incremental return. Thus, the law of diminishing returns should be
considered when activity durations are estimated.
- **D Political awareness**
Correct. Political awareness is an example of interpersonal and team skill that can be used
as a tool or technique in several project management processes. According to the scenario,
the project manager is performing the Estimate Activity Durations process. Political
awareness is not associated with this process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 376, 197

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 187 of 200
Question ID: 651394
Stakeholders are not sure what to do about the multiple failures the project has been experiencing
recently. Changes need to be made quickly. Otherwise, the project may be terminated, as it is
consistently missing its objectives.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Recommend terminating the project as its objectives cannot be met**
- **B Consult with the project sponsor due to the urgency and the severity of the situation**
- **C Implement the most promising change immediately and transparently**
- **D Facilitate a discussion amongst the stakeholders on what should be changed**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Has any change been proposed?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Any changes that may potentially modify a deliverable, baseline, or control document must be
reviewed, evaluated, and passed via the Perform Integrated Change Control process. That
process is triggered by a change request. No action regarding implementation or reaction to a
change can take place until the change need is understood and crafted into a change request. That
change request(s) - in whichever format determined or suitable for the project - is then evaluated

---

and decided on according to the organization's change control process established for the project.
Hence, the first action is to facilitate the discussion of the change request and suggestion
responses.
One may argue that since the project is in critical condition, engaging several stakeholders with
varying degree of influence and interest in the project doesn’t look as the measure to bring the
needed results. Consulting with the sponsor, on the other hand, means engaging the person who
has authority and resources to make the required changes. While this is true, one should
remember that the sponsor is a project stakeholder. Therefore, facilitating a discussion amongst
the stakeholders implies involving the sponsor as well.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Recommend terminating the project as its objectives cannot be met**
Incorrect. Although the scenario suggests the project might be terminated, the scenario is
also talking about changes that can be made to avoid project termination. Therefore,
terminating the project at this point seems premature.
- **B Consult with the project sponsor due to the urgency and the severity of the situation**
Incorrect. The situation looks severe enough to warrant the involvement of the project
sponsor. However, based on the scenario, the project manager has not yet attempted to
resolve the situation using tools and resources under her control. There are other steps that
the project manager can take before turning to the sponsor.
- **C Implement the most promising change immediately and transparently**
Incorrect. The scenario does not provide any information about any specific change
request. The scenario is talking about the need for a change. Regardless, even if such a
promising change has been proposed, it should have gone through the Perform Integrated
Change Control process. The change can be sped up if needed, but it should have been
requested first and approved.
- **D Facilitate a discussion amongst the stakeholders on what should be changed**
Correct. The change control board must evaluate and approve a change request via the
Perform Integrated Change Control process. The group must decide on what the suggested
change(s) is(are) to be.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 113-115
Bottom of Form

Question 188 of 200
Question ID: 612131
- **A microprocessor manufacturer has released its new chip to the market. The company tried to**
balance chip performance versus manufacturing expense. The project manager wants to
determine whether the performance and features that sophisticated consumers demand from
modern processors were met by the new chip.
What is the best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Send questionnaires and surveys**
- **B Make telemarketing calls**
- **C Send standard mail**
- **D Issue email subscriptions**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager should consider what would be an efficient way to collect specific data
from the target consumer.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The project manager should gather data that indicates whether or not the project deliverables
meet the expectations of the client or end user. The best way to accomplish this task is to ask the
client or end-user directly. Questionnaires and surveys are an example of the data gathering

---

technique that can be used in this situation to solicit information about customer satisfaction after
the deployment of the product or service. Typically, with the expectations identified in the
quality management plan, the project manager needs more data to address any changes or
updates to the deliverables that may be needed to meet the quality expectations.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Send questionnaires and surveys**
Correct. Questionnaires and surveys are useful tools to identify the desires and
expectations of the client or end-user of a product. These tools are a simple and effective
way to have a written record of the client or end-user expectations. In electronic form, these
tools provide a way to collect and process highly-detailed information from a target
audience efficiently.
- **B Make telemarketing calls**
Incorrect. Making telemarketing calls is not an effective way to capture the needs of the
clients or end-users. Telemarketing calls are commonly screened and have a very low
success rate in gathering information.
- **C Send standard mail**
Incorrect. Standard postal mail is a time- and resource-intensive means of communication
with a high probability of the delivered mail being discarded as "junk mail." The hard-copy
nature of this medium also requires significant processing time to produce useful
information for the project team.
- **D Issue email subscriptions**
Incorrect. Email subscriptions demand a high level of participation from the client or
end-user to engage with the message content proactively. In addition, many email service
providers screen emails for "junk." In this case, the message contents may never reach the
intended audience.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 303

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 189 of 200
Question ID: 651351
- **A project team member ran an earned value analysis (EVA) report that showed an unexpected**
spike in actual costs over the last three weeks. The team member showed the report to the project
manager and based on her analysis presents four possible reasons for the spike.
Which reason is most probable?
Top of Form
- **A Soaring steel prices have impacted the fixed price with economic price adjustments procurement**
contracts
- **B There was a strike at the loading dock which delayed many needed steel shipments until today**
- **C Fewer employees are showing up for work the past two weeks causing a backlog of unfinished**
work
- **D Much higher than expected quarterly bonuses were given to executives during that three week**
period
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which cost is most prone to unexpected fluctuations?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Earned value analysis (EVA) is an example of the data analysis techniques that can be used as
part of the processes in the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group. In the context of this

---

question, the team member has applied the technique to the Control Costs process. By analyzing
the earned values and associated costs of the project, the project team can react or make
adjustments or request changes. To know the appropriate action to take, the project manager
must know how to interpret the data. In the scenario, the variability of the steel prices would be a
probable cause of the actual costs spiking beyond the planned values. The other three options do
not directly impact the actual costs of the project within the scenario's circumstances.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Soaring steel prices have impacted the fixed price with economic price adjustments**
procurement contracts
Correct. A fixed price with economic price adjustments (FPEPA) procurement contract with
suppliers adjusts over time as there are fluctuations to agreed upon commodities, such as
steel in this scenario.
- **B There was a strike at the loading dock which delayed many needed steel shipments until**
today
Incorrect. The decrease of inventory or inability of shipments to reach their destination
does not increase the actual costs. While there may be costs associated with the strike,
these costs are unlikely to result in the spike at the same extent as if they were the result of
the reason provided in another answer choice.
- **C Fewer employees are showing up for work the past two weeks causing a backlog of**
unfinished work
Incorrect. The reduction of human resources would typically decrease, not increase, the
actual costs.
- **D Much higher than expected quarterly bonuses were given to executives during that three**
week period
Incorrect. Company bonuses and other expenses outside the project organization are not
reflected in the earned value analysis as an actual cost of the project. These costs are
typically external to the budget and controls of the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 261, 471

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 190 of 200
Question ID: 651420
The project manager and members of the project team start an Ishikawa diagram for a quality
issue. Someone writes down 'source material' as a potential cause.
What is the next best action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Instruct the production department to stop using the source material**
- **B Request the team to brainstorm other possible causes of the quality issue**
- **C Suggest switching from the Ishikawa diagram to the cause-and-effect diagram**
- **D Direct the team to focus on issues from the customer perspective of quality**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Could there be other reasons?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

An Ishikawa diagram is a quality management tool that can be used as part of the Manage
Quality process or Control Quality process to assist in the brainstorming, discussion, and
examination of potential causes to a problem, issue, or other quality concern. Ishikawa diagrams
are also referred to as cause-and-effect diagrams, why-why diagrams, and fishbone diagrams -
due to the resemblance of a fish skeleton with the problem at the head and possible causes
branching out. Similar to a mind map, Ishikawa diagrams can extend out and are shaped by the

---

input of the team. There is no correct path. It is an exercise to brainstorm and ask how and why.
After the tool stimulates enough thinking, the targeted causes from the diagram can be examined
further with follow up actions suggested. Until then, the project manager should encourage and
facilitate more brainstorming and good discussion.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Instruct the production department to stop using the source material**
Incorrect. Ishikawa diagrams and other cause-and-effect diagrams are used to assist the
team to brainstorm, discuss, and examine potential reasons or causes for a quality problem.
Writing down a possible cause is the start, not the end point requiring immediate action.
- **B Request the team to brainstorm other possible causes of the quality issue**
Correct. The purpose of a cause-and-effect diagram such as the Ishikawa is to brainstorm
various possibilities and connections to potential causes to a problem, issue, or other
quality concern. The project manager should encourage the process to continue.
- **C Suggest switching from the Ishikawa diagram to the cause-and-effect diagram**
Incorrect. The Ishikawa diagram and the cause-and-effect diagram are essentially the
same. Other names include fishbone diagrams and why-why diagrams.
- **D Direct the team to focus on issues from the customer perspective of quality**
Incorrect. Ishikawa diagrams can examine the process and the product. It can focus both
internally on the project organization and operations as well as the customer or other
external sources.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 304, 293
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 191 of 200
Question ID: 613308
- **A project manager is leading an infrastructure development project and is just starting the**
process of prioritizing individual project risks for further analysis. A stakeholder has expressed
concern that the existing information about individual project risks may not be accurate and
reliable.
What is the best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Perform the Identify Risks process again**
- **B Capture the concern in the stakeholder register**
- **C Perform a risk data quality assessment**
- **D Conduct a risk probability and impact assessment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which data analysis technique might be useful in evaluating the degree to which the data about
individual risks is accurate and reliable as a basis for qualitative risk analysis?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process is underway. A risk data
quality assessment is an example of the data analysis technique that can be used in this process.
- **A risk data quality assessment evaluates the degree to which the data about individual project**

---

risks is accurate and reliable as a basis for qualitative risk analysis. The use of low-quality risk
data may lead to a qualitative risk analysis that is of little use to the project. If data quality is
unacceptable, it may be necessary to gather better data. Risk data quality may be assessed via a
questionnaire measuring the project's stakeholder perceptions of various characteristics, which
may include completeness, objectivity, relevance, and timeliness. A weighted average of selected
data quality characteristics can then be generated to provide an overall quality score. Therefore,
of the available choices, to address the stakeholder's concern, performing a risk data quality
assessment is the best course of action.
Note, ideally, the project manager would have to meet with the stakeholder to better understand
the concerns expressed by the stakeholder before spending project resources to perform the risk
data quality assessment. However, this answer choice is not provided.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Perform the Identify Risks process again**
Incorrect. Identify Risks is the process of identifying individual project risks as well as
sources of overall project risk. While this process can be performed more than once
throughout the project, the scenario does not indicate that risks have been missed. Rather,
the concern is that information about already identified risks may not be accurate.
- **B Capture the concern in the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document that includes the identification,
assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. Information about project risks is
not part of this document.
- **C Perform a risk data quality assessment**
Correct. Risk data quality assessment evaluates the degree to which the data about
individual project risks is accurate and reliable as a basis for qualitative risk analysis.
- **D Conduct a risk probability and impact assessment**
Incorrect. A risk probability assessment considers the likelihood that a specific risk will
occur. A risk impact assessment considers the potential effect on one or more project
objectives. A risk probability and impact assessment cannot provide an evaluation of the
degree to which the data about individual project risks is accurate and reliable.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 423
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 192 of 200
Question ID: 625021
The project charter for a cross-functional project has already been approved. The project
manager wants to identify stakeholders as soon as possible so that the project planning can start.
The project manager quickly creates a document listing the project manager, project sponsor, and
the project customer as the only project stakeholders.
What has the project manager done wrong?
Top of Form
- **A The project manager did not identify all of the project stakeholders.**
- **B The project manager has done nothing wrong, as the people that are documented are all project**
stakeholders.
- **C The project manager should have identified all project stakeholders before the approval of the**
project charter.
- **D The project manager should have done this exercise after developing the project management**
plan.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Stakeholders are identified during project initiation.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**


---

- **A stakeholder is an individual, group, or organization that may affect, be affected by, or perceive**
itself to be affected by a decision, activity, or outcome of a project, program, or portfolio.
Identifying project stakeholders is an iterative activity that involves identifying both the positive,
as well as negative stakeholders and documenting their relevant interests, involvement and
impact in the project. Although the people the project manager listed are indeed project
stakeholders, it is clear from the scenario that the project manager did not identify all of the
project stakeholders. For example, potential stakeholders include team members as well as
groups, departments and other people and organizations who may be impacted by the project.
The project charter is one of the inputs to the Identify Stakeholders process. Therefore, the
project manager could not identify the project stakeholders before the approval of the project
charter. The stakeholder register is used for planning that will help shape the project management
plan.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project manager did not identify all of the project stakeholders.**
Correct. This choice describes what the project manager did that was wrong Since the
project charter only has the high-level project stakeholders, the project manager should
identify others who affect, are affected by, or perceive themselves to be affected by the
project.
- **B The project manager has done nothing wrong, as the people that are documented are all**
project stakeholders.
Incorrect. The project manager has done something wrong. There are usually more
stakeholders than those identified in the project charter.
- **C The project manager should have identified all project stakeholders before the approval of**
the project charter.
Incorrect. This choice does not describe what the project manager did that was wrong. The
project charter is usually developed before or sometimes coincident with, the stakeholder
register. The stakeholder register then needs to be maintained throughout the project.
- **D The project manager should have done this exercise after developing the project**
management plan.
Incorrect. This choice does not describe what the project manager did that was wrong.
Although identifying stakeholders is an iterative process and as the project management
plan is developed, new stakeholders are identified, the stakeholder register should be
maintained from the start of the project.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 509

PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 193 of 200
Question ID: 612729
You are leading a project to construct a new runway at an existing commercial airport. After
completion of the project, the residents under the flight path of the new runway are making noise
complaints and want the airport to compensate them for the diminished values of their homes.
What might you have missed earlier in the project?
Top of Form
- **A Including in the stakeholder register those with a contribution stake in the project**
- **B Stakeholder analysis including consideration for those with an interest stake in the project**
- **C A thorough review of the agreements prior to the development of the stakeholder register**
- **D The inclusion of the affected homeowners in the project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What stake did the homeowners have in the project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the homeowners under the flight path of the new runway have been
negatively impacted by the resulting noise as well as a potential reduction in property values.
This situation implies that the impact of the project on the affected homeowners was not
considered or was just disregarded. Stakeholder analysis is used during the development of the
stakeholder register to identify relevant information about the stakeholders including their stakes

---

in the project. In this case, the affected homeowners, whether they realized it at the time or not,
had an interest stake in the project. Any person or group that is affected by a decision related to
the project or its outcomes has an interest stake in a project. Had the impact of the project on the
affected homeowners been fully considered, steps may have been taken to mitigate the impact of
the project on the homeowners. Mitigation steps may have included noise abatement procedures
for aircraft or perhaps a different runway orientation. Therefore, of the available options,
stakeholder analysis including consideration for those with an interest stake in the project is what
you likely missed during project initiation.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Including in the stakeholder register those with a contribution stake in the project**
Incorrect. A contribution stake involves the provision of funds or other resources, including
human resources, or providing support for the project in more intangible ways. There is no
information from the question that the affected homeowners contributed funds or support
for the project; thus, it is unlikely that they would have a contribution stake in the project.
- **B Stakeholder analysis including consideration for those with an interest stake in the project**
Correct. Stakeholder analysis is used during the development of the stakeholder register to
identify relevant information about the stakeholders including their stakes in the project. In
this case, the affected homeowners had an interest stake in the project.
- **C A thorough review of the agreements prior to the development of the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. Agreements are one of the inputs into the Identify Stakeholders process.
However, there is no indication provided by the question to suggest that the affected
homeowners were parties to any of the agreements to build the new runway.
- **D The inclusion of the affected homeowners in the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter does contain high-level information about the project
including key stakeholders. Although the affected homeowners do have an interest stake as
they are impacted by the project, they may or may not be considered key stakeholders.
Another answer choice better addresses the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 512

PMP Exam 7

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 194 of 200
Question ID: 651392
The project requires frequent input from the senior management team. Some of the past projects
succeeded to engage the team, however, most failed as senior management is notorious
throughout the organization of responding slowly and not attending meetings.
What is the best strategy for the stakeholder engagement plan of the current project?
Top of Form
- **A Patiently wait until management indicates that they are available to provide their input**
- **B Schedule regular, short update meetings at a constant time and convenient location**
- **C Review lessons learned from other projects involving the management stakeholders**
- **D Require one senior management representative to attend meetings or the project will be halted**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What has worked for other projects?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process. Lessons learned repository is
an organizational process asset which can be used as an input to this process. When planning
stakeholder engagement for the project, the project manager should take in the lessons learned
from other projects that had to engage with similar stakeholders. In the scenario, the project
stakeholders of the senior management team are known not to respond or attend meetings. Other

---

projects have learned ways to gather feedback or other forms of engagement. Learning from their
successes and failures will reduce the chances of the current project repeating failures and
increase successes. Planning approaches without consulting past or current attempts and methods
risks the project wasting time, money, resources, and more.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Patiently wait until management indicates that they are available to provide their input**
Incorrect. Passively waiting for stakeholders to determine their own engagement with the
project is not a wise solution unless that approach is explicitly stated as a successful tactic
from the lessons learned of other projects and conversations with the stakeholders.
- **B Schedule regular, short update meetings at a constant time and convenient location**
Incorrect. Senior management has a history of not attending meetings. Scheduling more of
them and hoping for a different result is an unwise strategy. The type, timing, and structure
must be understood first.
- **C Review lessons learned from other projects involving the management stakeholders**
Correct. Lessons learned from other projects can be an extremely valuable input to the
Plan Stakeholder Engagement process. Learning from the successes and failures of other
projects can guide the plans for the current project.
- **D Require one senior management representative to attend meetings or the project will be**
halted
Incorrect. Forcing rules that a project manager may not be able to enforce is doomed to
fail. A project manager's primary goal is to deliver project objectives within time and
budget. Halting a project as a result of unattended meetings risks the goal being met.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 520

Question 195 of 200
Question ID: 613328
At a steering committee meeting, the committee chair reprimands the project manager for not
following the company’s guidelines for exchange, storage, and retrieval of project information.
The project manager explains that she followed the team's recommendation as to how to manage
project information.
What most likely caused this situation?
Top of Form
- **A The project manager did not research the enterprise environmental factors**
- **B The project manager did not review the organizational process assets**
- **C The project team did not investigate communication tools to be used for information sharing**
- **D The project manager did nothing wrong**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

It sounds like the project manager did not follow company policy.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Many companies have policies for the storage, retention, distribution, safeguarding, and access to
company information, which includes project data. These standardized guidelines are considered
organizational process assets (OPAs), which are defined as plans, processes, policies, procedures,
and knowledge bases that are specific to and used by the performing organization. OPAs are

---

among the inputs to all processes of the Project Communications Management Knowledge Area.
The question indicates that the project manager did not follow the company’s guidelines for
exchange, storage, and retrieval of project information. Had a review of the OPAs been
conducted, the project manager would have realized that the company's guidelines required the
use of the company's file sharing system and, likely, would have rejected the project team's
recommendation to manage project information differently. Therefore, of the choices provided,
the most likely cause for the situation presented in the scenario was the project manager's failure
to review the organizational process assets.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project manager did not research the enterprise environmental factors**
Incorrect. Enterprise environmental factors are conditions, not under the immediate control
of the team, that influence, constrain, or direct the project. The standardized guidelines for
the development, exchange, storage, and retrieval of information are considered
organizational process assets and not enterprise environmental factors.
- **B The project manager did not review the organizational process assets**
Correct. Organizational process assets are defined as plans, processes, policies,
procedures, and knowledge bases that are specific to and used by the performing
organization. In this case, the question suggests that the project manager did not follow the
organization’s policy on file sharing. Instead, the team recommended to deviate from the
policy, and the project manager did nothing to prevent his deviation.
- **C The project team did not investigate communication tools to be used for information**
sharing
Incorrect. The scenario surrounds the way the project information is developed, exchanged,
stored, and retrieved rather than what communication tools are used to share the
information.
- **D The project manager did nothing wrong**
Incorrect. The question states that the project manager did not use the company’s file
sharing system as required. This situation suggests that the project manager did not follow
the relevant company policies and procedures regarding the company's file sharing system.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 369, 383, 391

Question 196 of 200
Question ID: 651341
An organization is using multiple systems and tools from three different vendors. The
organization wants to undertake a project that would integrate those systems and tools.
Which is the best course of action by the organization?
Top of Form
- **A Charter a project with all vendors involved**
- **B Wait until procurement documents are written before involving vendors**
- **C Make the vendors the customer of the project**
- **D Separate the three vendors into three projects to be managed concurrently**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When is the most optimal time to involve the vendors?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests that the project has not yet been chartered. The project is still undergoing
feasibility studies and other initiating activities. Partnering with the owners of the various
systems already in use that are targeted for integration is ensuring more success than not
involving them. Crafting the project charter with the input from all key stakeholders - which
includes the system vendors - can align the project objective with the abilities and interests of the

---

suppliers. The inclusion of the vendors provides valuable information about goals, timing,
assumptions, constraints, and other considerations included in a project charter.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Charter a project with all vendors involved**
Correct. The multiple systems supplied by multiple vendors should partner with the
performing organization to set the project up for success. Involving the vendors in the
crafting of the project charter is the best course of action.
- **B Wait until procurement documents are written before involving vendors**
Incorrect. At this point the procurement needs are not fully understood. If the organization
is already using system and tools from the vendor, waiting for procurement documents is an
unnecessary delay.
- **C Make the vendors the customer of the project**
Incorrect. The vendors are partners in this project objective, not the customer. Based on the
scenario, the customer is internal to the performing organization.
- **D Separate the three vendors into three projects to be managed concurrently**
Incorrect. The objective is to integrate the systems, not to separate them. Therefore,
separating the vendors is unlikely to help in achieving the goal. It is typically more
expensive to manage three similar projects concurrently, as opposed to managing one
project that has the same objectives and would benefit from the optimal approach for
managing organizational resources.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 75-77
