PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 197 of 200
Question ID: 651413
- **A project has been chartered with so many unknowns and little clarity as to how the products are**
to be built and designed even though it is extremely clear to all that something has to be done
and fast.
What is the best approach for the project manager to take?
Top of Form
- **A Ensure all stakeholders are in agreement on the product and project scope at the start, then**
progress towards one solution
- **B Establish an evolving product roadmap, then define and refine the scope as the project progresses**
- **C Stabilize the primary project requirements before any project team members are acquired**
- **D Create a program of different projects to see which one works best**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is enough known about the project and product scope to finalize all requirements?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Defining project and product scope can be accomplished in many different ways depending on
the needs of the project and other circumstances. The circumstances in this scenario are that there
is a time sensitivity but lots of unknowns. Without clear knowledge of what needs to be done and
how, deciding as a team all that needs to be done before started is difficult. Attempting to fully

---

define the project work before starting work may be more time consuming compared to starting
with a roadmap and some less clear requirements. Building off lesser requirements and gathering
feedback and input provides fodder for the stakeholders to work from and define the scope
further. This agile approach to project management enables stakeholders to progressively
elaborate the project's outcomes and plans to achieve those outcomes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ensure all stakeholders are in agreement on the product and project scope at the start, then**
progress towards one solution
Incorrect. Time is of the essence, and too much is unknown. The stakeholders do not fully
understand the scope that is needed or desired. Spending too much time debating the
unknowns might corner the project in an unviable solution. Ensuring all stakeholders are in
agreement on the product and project scope that is unknown is unlikely to be the best
approach for the project manager to take in this situation.
- **B Establish an evolving product roadmap, then define and refine the scope as the project**
progresses
Correct. Based on the scenario described, the project scope is not fully understood and still
evolving. Adopting an agile project management approach to this project better suits the
stakeholders' need to flesh out the product and outcomes.
- **C Stabilize the primary project requirements before any project team members are acquired**
Incorrect. In traditional project management, the team is typically acquired during project
execution. However, a project consisting of many unknown requirements would benefit from
the early input, feedback, and perspectives of subject matter experts and team members
who are going to plan and execute the project. Therefore, stabilizing the primary project
requirements before any project team members are acquired will likely delay the project
which, as implied by the scenario, is already under the time constraint.
- **D Create a program of different projects to see which one works best**
Incorrect. Running multiple projects and multiple programs is cost intensive. Additionally,
expecting that many will fail makes the cost of resources, time, and finances even greater.
An agile approach can accomplish much of this on a shorter timescale.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 133

Question 198 of 200
Question ID: 612486
You are leading a project with some of the deliverables outsourced to a vendor. You have been
working closely with your procurement administrator to ensure that all claims, invoices, and
final payments have been finalized with the vendor. Terms and conditions of the contract have
been met, and all deliverables have been accepted.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Notify the vendor that the contract has been completed**
- **B Finalize all activities for the project and release the project team**
- **C Conduct the final inspection of the vendor's deliverables**
- **D Carry out a structured review of the procurement process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Closed procurements are an output of the Control Procurements process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the Control Procurements process is underway. Closed procurements are an
output of this process. When all claims, invoices, and final payments have been finalized with
the vendor, when terms and conditions of the contract have been met, and all deliverables have
been received, the buyer, usually through its authorized procurement administrator, provides the

---

seller with formal written notice that the contract has been completed. The incorrect answer
choices describe actions that either should have been already taken prior to this point in time or
are premature. Of the choices provided, noticing the vendor that the contract has been completed
is what you should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Notify the vendor that the contract has been completed**
Correct. Closed procurements are an output of the Control Procurements process implied
by the scenario. The buyer should provide the seller (vendor) with a formal written notice
that the contract has been completed.
- **B Finalize all activities for the project and release the project team**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents actions that typically take place as part of the
project (or phase) closure. According to the scenario, the vendor has been responsible for
delivering 'some' of the deliverables, implying there are other deliverables. There is not
enough information in the question to determine if those deliverables have already been
completed. Therefore, carrying out activities related to project closure may be premature.
- **C Conduct the final inspection of the vendor's deliverables**
Incorrect. An inspection, as it pertains to procurement management, is a structured review
of the work performed by the vendor. Based on the scenario, the deliverables have been
accepted suggesting the necessary inspections have already been conducted. Once the
deliverables are accepted, no further inspections are required.
- **D Carry out a structured review of the procurement process**
Incorrect. A structured review of the procurement process is a procurement audit. The
procurement audit is one of the tools and techniques of the Control Procurements process
described in the scenario. According to the scenario, the deliverables have been accepted
suggesting the audit has already been carried out (assuming it was planned). Once the
deliverables are accepted, no further audits are required. While audits can be performed
after the deliverables are accepted, typically an audit should be performed while the work
is still in progress to allow the parties to make adjustments to the process, when necessary.
Therefore, if the deliverables have already been accepted, carrying out the procurement
audit is of little value.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 499

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 199 of 200
Question ID: 613317
- **A project manager is leading a project to build a new model of all-terrain vehicle (ATV). The**
resource requirements documentation calls for the suspension parts to be painted. However, in
response to an issue captured in the issue log, it has been recommended to use powder coating
instead of paint for better corrosion resistance.
What should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Deny the recommendation as it represents gold plating**
- **B Follow the original resource requirements**
- **C Purchase the powder coating equipment and supplies**
- **D Submit a change request**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is required to modify a subsidiary of the project management plan?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

If the recommendation to use powder coating instead of paint is accepted as corrective action, it
will change the requirements that address corrosion resistance of suspension parts. To implement
the recommended corrective action, the project manager will need to acquire the powder coating
material and supplies, which may incur additional cost to the project. As it pertains to the

---

acquisition of resources, an approved change request will be required to update the relevant
components of the project management plan, such as the cost baseline, to permit the acquisition
of the powder coating equipment and supplies. While the correct answer choice does not
specifically mention what project artifact is supposed to be addressed by the change request, it
can be reasonably assumed that the cost baseline is one of those artifacts. Although the cost
baseline may eventually remain unchanged, a change request should be submitted to evaluate the
impact. Otherwise, on what basis would a project manager ask the project team to spend time
evaluating a request that is not even documented? Therefore, of the available answer choices,
submitting a change request is what the project manager should do first.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Deny the recommendation as it represents gold plating**
Incorrect. Gold plating can be described as the addition of features or functionality that is
not included in the project scope without following the established change control process.
If a project team member took it upon themselves to powder coat the parts when the
resource requirements documentation calls for paint, then this would be an example of gold
plating. However, in this scenario, the powder coating of parts is just being recommended
to address an issue. If a change request is submitted and approved to change the
requirements to include the powder coating of the suspension parts, then it is not gold
plating.
- **B Follow the original resource requirements**
Incorrect. The question implies that corrosion of the painted suspension parts is an issue
that should be resolved. Blindly following the resource requirements without modification
does not address the issue and goes against the responsibility of the project manager to act
in the best interests of the project.
- **C Purchase the powder coating equipment and supplies**
Incorrect. Implementing the recommendation may be a good idea. However, this action, as
it pertains to the acquisition of resources, may require a modification to the cost baseline or
other components of the project management plan. Any modification to a component of the
project management first requires an approved change request.
- **D Submit a change request**
Correct. Powder coating may cost more than paint. Therefore, the impact of this change
should first be evaluated. However, before the team spends time evaluating the impact, a
change request should be submitted.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 334
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 7
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 200 of 200
Question ID: 651361
Which is an example of a positive schedule variance?
Top of Form
- **A The ratio of work completed to work planned is greater than 1.0**
- **B The ratio of work planned to work completed is greater than 1.0**
- **C The actual costs of the project are lower than the work performed**
- **D The actual costs of the project are lower than the work planned**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How is the schedule performance index (SPI) connected with the schedule variance (SV)?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The schedule variance (SV) is a measure of schedule performance expressed as the difference
between the earned value (EV) to planned value (PV): SV = EV - PV. The schedule performance
index (SPI) is a measure of schedule efficiency expressed as the ratio of earned value to planned
value: SPI = EV/PV, in other words, the amount of value that has been gained or earned to this
point divided by what was planned to be earned up to this point. When the numerator (EV) is
greater than the denominator (PV), the SPI ratio is greater than 1. When the minuend (EV) is
greater than the subtrahend (PV), the difference is positive. If the ratio is greater than 1.0 (or the
difference is positivie), the project is considered ahead of schedule. If the SPI is less than 1.0 (the

---

SV is negative), the project is considered behind schedule. Ideally, a project aims to be equal to
1.0 which indicates that the project is performing as planned.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The ratio of work completed to work planned is greater than 1.0**
Correct. The schedule performance index (SPI) is a ratio. A number greater than 1.0
indicates that there is more work being completed than planned at this point in the project.
The schedule variance (SV) is a difference: SV = EV - PV. When (EV) is greater than (PV),
the difference (SV) is positive.
- **B The ratio of work planned to work completed is greater than 1.0**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents an inverse ratio of the schedule performance
index (SPI) which is an incorrect usage of the SPI formula.
- **C The actual costs of the project are lower than the work performed**
Incorrect. Actual costs are used in the formulas to calculate the cost performance index
(CPI) and the cost variance (CV), not the SPI or the SV. The SPI and SV are based on the
planned work against the work performed.
- **D The actual costs of the project are lower than the work planned**
Incorrect. This answer choice mixes actual costs (AC) with planned value (PV). This
combination is not used in the SPI or SV calculations.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263
